Nicky let out a dramatic sigh and settled back in his seat, the mystery of the surprise hanging in the air like a tangible thing. As they drove, he kept throwing out guesses—nothing quite right, but each one more excited than the last. Agatha’s heart lightened with every passing moment, her earlier exhaustion from the workday slowly slipping away as she watched him get lost in the anticipation.

When they finally pulled up in front of the Disney on Ice venue, Nicky froze. His jaw dropped, eyes wide, his little hands clutching the armrest like he was bracing for takeoff.

“Where are we, Mom?” he asked, his voice full of awe.

“Disney on Ice,” Agatha said slowly, glancing at him with a smile.

“Disney on Ice?” he whispered, turning to her with a look of pure disbelief.

Agatha unbuckled her seatbelt, still smiling. “Yup. I thought you might like it.”

Nicky didn’t say another word. Instead, he launched himself at her, wrapping his arms around her neck in a tight hug. “Best. Surprise. Ever!”

Agatha chuckled, her heart swelling. “I’m glad you like it, buddy.”

As they stepped out of the car and made their way toward the venue, Nicky’s eyes grew even wider, darting from the colorful signs to the buzzing families around them. The earlier disbelief on his face had morphed into pure, unfiltered excitement.

But then he tugged on her hand and asked, “Mom… What's Disney on Ice?”

Agatha blinked, a little stunned. Right. She’d forgotten that Nicky probably had no clue what this was. Crouching down to his level as they neared the entrance, she tried her best to explain. 

"Disney on Ice is like... well, it's like a giant ice skating show, but with all of your favorite Disney characters." She paused, watching his face for signs of recognition.

"Skating? Like Elsa?" Nicky asked, his voice full of hope.

"Exactly!" Agatha laughed, nodding enthusiastically. "Elsa, Anna, and all their friends will be skating around on the ice, doing special tricks and dances. They even have cool scenes from the movies where they bring the magic to life right before your eyes"

Nicky’s eyes lit up as the thought sank in. "So, there’s going to be ice, and magic... and Elsa?!"

"Yep. And more than that," Agatha added, grinning at his excitement. "There will be other characters too, like Mickey Mouse, and maybe even Moana. It's going to be a whole big adventure."

Nicky's small hand shot up into the air, his voice full of wonder. "And there will be singing? And dancing? And ice?" His energy was practically vibrating through him.

"Yes, all of that and more." Agatha laughed, taking his hand and guiding him through the crowd. "I think you're going to love it."

While they walked  through the parking lot Nicky kept glancing back at her, as if he still couldn’t quite believe it was real. His wide grin and excited chatter were contagious, filling Agatha with a warm sense of pride. She’d been a little uncertain about the whole idea, but seeing him so happy, so swept up in the magic, made every bit of effort worth it. This was the kind of moment she’d been searching for—a day where the world outside faded away, leaving just the joy they shared together.

As Agatha and Nicky approached the entrance, a cheerful voice called out, cutting through the background noise of laughter and chatter.

“Agatha! Over here!”

She turned to see Wanda waving enthusiastically, a vibrant grin on her face. Beside her were two boys, identical in appearance but already exuding distinct personalities. One of them had a mischievous twinkle in his eye, while the other stood a little more reserved, clutching a stuffed animal in one hand. 

“Hi, Wanda,” Agatha said,

The boys stared up at Nicky with curiosity, and before Agatha could say anything, Wanda gestured toward them. “Agatha, meet my twins—Billy and Tommy.”

One of them, the more outgoing of the two, grinned. “Hi!” he said, his voice filled with confidence.

“Hello,” the other one added softly, giving a small wave but staying close to Wanda’s side.

Agatha nudged Nicky forward gently. “This is my son, Nicky” she introduced, her voice carrying a hint of pride.

“Nice to finally meet you Nicky” Wanda said, ushering her kids forward with a bright smile, her energy effortlessly infectious.

One of the boys practically bounced on his heels, his excitement bubbling over. “Hi! I’m Billy!” he exclaimed, waving enthusiastically. He had his mother’s red hair and a mischievous grin that made him instantly endearing.

Tommy, on the other hand, was a bit more reserved, his bright brown eyes studying Nicky with curiosity. "Hey," he said softly, his expression friendly but cautious. He held out his hand shyly, and Nicky took it eagerly, shaking it with a grin.

Nicky, thrilled to meet new friends, took Tommy’s hand eagerly and shook it. “Hi, I’m Nicky!” he replied, his grin widening as he looked between the twins. “This is gonna be awesome!”

Wanda watched the exchange with a proud smile and leaned over to Agatha. “They’re good kids,” she said warmly. “Billy’s the adventurous one, always looking for the next big thing. Tommy’s a little quieter, but he’s just as sweet. I think they’re going to get along great.”

Just as Agatha was about to say more, a tall man approached, his posture relaxed but his steps purposeful. He looked like he was about to greet Wanda, but his eyes flicked to Agatha with polite curiosity.

“Hey, babe,” he said casually, placing a hand on Wanda’s shoulder.

“Oh! Vision,” Wanda said brightly. “This is Agatha”

Agatha gave a small nod, taking him in—calm demeanor, neatly dressed, and with a quiet charm that made sense next to Wanda’s vibrant energy.

“And this is Vision,” Wanda added, glancing at Agatha. “My partner”

Vision acknowledges Agatha with a smile extending a hand. “Nice to finally meet you Agatha. Wanda has spoken very highly of you”

“Likewise,” Agatha replied, shaking his hand briefly before stepping back, feeling slightly out of place in the easy familial dynamic unfolding before her.

Wanda clapped her hands lightly. “Well, looks like the kids are hitting it off already.”

Agatha glanced at Nicky, who was now animatedly leading Billy and Tommy toward a nearby display. She sighed, a small but genuine smile forming. “Yeah, looks like it.”

As she spoke, Vision stepped forward, crouching down to Nicky’s level with a kind smile. “Hey, Nicky. I’m Vision. Are you ready to see some magic?”

Nicky nodded enthusiastically. “Yeah! I’ve never seen anything like this before! Are you here for the show too?”

Vision chuckled, straightening up. “That’s the plan. But I’m mostly here to make sure everyone has a good time—and to keep an eye on these two,” he added with a teasing glance at Billy and Tommy. “Sometimes their excitement gets a little… energetic .”

Billy, overhearing, shot Vision a playful look. “We’re not wild, Dad. We’re just excited!”

“Of course you are,” Vision replied with mock seriousness, his eyes sparkling. “But let’s all agree to stay in our seats this time, alright?”

Wanda winked at Agatha. “Vision’s the peacekeeper in the family. He keeps us all grounded.”

Meanwhile, Nicky was already deep in conversation with the twins. “Let’s sit together!” he suggested excitedly. 

Billy’s eyes lit up. “Yes! Best idea ever”

As the group made their way to their inside of the venue  Wanda leaned toward Agatha, her expression warm. “It’s so nice to see everyone getting along so well. I have a feeling this is going to be a great night.”

Agatha smiled, taking a moment to soak it all in—the bright lights, the sound of happy chatter, and Nicky’s pure, unfiltered joy. “Yeah,” she agreed softly. “It really is.”

As the group made their way through the venue, Wanda took the lead, expertly navigating the crowd with a casual confidence that suggested she’d done this plenty of times before. Agatha followed, keeping an eye on Nicky, who was practically vibrating with excitement as he chatted nonstop with Billy and Tommy about dinosaurs, superheroes, and all the wonders they expected to see.

It wasn’t until they arrived at their destination—an arena with rows of seats encircling a large, open ice rink—that Agatha noticed where Wanda was leading them.

“Wait,” Agatha said, glancing around as Wanda confidently marched toward the front. “These are... front row seats?”

Wanda turned and gave Agatha a sly smile. “Of course. Why wouldn’t they be?”

Agatha blinked, taken aback. “You mean you planned it like this? Like, actually went out of your way to make sure you’d get us first row seats?”

Wanda shrugged, her grin widening as she herded Billy and Tommy into their spots. “What can I say? I know people. And besides, it’s worth it to see the kids light up.” She gestured toward the boys, who were already clamoring to get the best view of the stage, their eyes wide with anticipation.

Agatha glanced at Nicky, who was now standing on his tiptoes, craning his neck to see over the barrier separating the rink from the audience. His face was a mix of awe and glee, and she could practically see the gears turning in his head as he imagined what was about to happen.

“Don’t tell me you were planning to sit in the back,” Wanda teased, her voice dripping with mock incredulity.

“I don’t know, maybe,” Agatha said with a smirk. “Some of us aren’t out here pulling strings to impress six and four year-olds.”

Wanda laughed, a warm, genuine sound that made even Agatha smile despite herself. “Oh, come on, Harkness. Live a little.”

Agatha rolled her eyes but couldn’t help glancing back at Nicky, whose excitement was almost tangible. His little hands gripped the edge of the barrier, his eyes darting around as he took in every detail.

Wanda leaned closer, her tone teasing. “See? Totally worth it.”

Agatha huffed, crossing her arms. “Fine. You win this one.”

But as she settled into her seat, watching the kids buzz with excitement and chatter, she had to admit. Front row wasn’t such a bad place to be.

Agatha nodded, feeling a sense of unexpected calm settle over her. As the show began and the lights dimmed further, the laughter and chatter of the group filled the air, making everything feel just a little less chaotic. Maybe, just maybe, these spontaneous moments were the kind that made life feel a bit more... magical.

The lights flickered, and the music began to swell, filling the arena with a sense of anticipation. The crowd’s excitement grew, and Nicky’s face lit up with wide-eyed wonder as the first characters took the stage. The ice glowed beneath the dazzling lights, the crystal-clear surface reflecting the performers' movements with a kind of magic only found in such a place.

The first segment of the show was an extravagant display of Disney's most beloved princesses. Agatha watched as Cinderella, Snow White, and Belle twirled across the ice, their costumes sparkling like diamonds. The elegance of their movements, the fluidity of the choreography, and the grandiose set pieces made it feel as if the fairy tales themselves were coming to life right before their eyes. Nicky was practically bouncing in his seat, his eyes glued to the performers, a wide smile stretched across his face.

As the show progressed, characters from The Lion King appeared, with Simba and Nala gliding gracefully across the ice. The transition from the fairy tale princesses to the wild savannah was seamless, with vibrant colors filling the arena. The giant lion costumes—especially one designed to look like Mufasa—were breathtaking, and the children let out gasps of awe at the sheer scale of the production. The dancers mimicked the powerful, yet graceful movements of the animals, while dramatic projections of the African landscape played on the backdrop.

Agatha found herself drawn into the spectacle, the magic of the show pulling her in, even as she tried to maintain her usual level of cool detachment. She glanced at Wanda, who was clearly enjoying the show as much as the kids. Wanda’s eyes were filled with joy as she watched her twins’ reactions, laughing along with them. It was hard not to be swept up in the energy of the moment.

The final act was the most thrilling—a high-energy performance featuring Elsa and Anna from Frozen . The ice rink was transformed into a wintry kingdom, complete with swirling snowflakes and shimmering blue lights. Elsa’s ice powers were brought to life in stunning special effects as she "created" ice sculptures that seemed to materialize in midair. The arena was filled with snowflakes falling from above, and the sound of Let It Go reverberated through the crowd, everyone singing along.

Nicky was completely captivated by the sight. “Mom, look! It’s Elsa! She’s making snow!” he exclaimed, his voice full of awe. Agatha couldn’t help but smile at his enthusiasm, the little moments of wonder reminding her that there was so much magic to be found, even in the simplest things.

Throughout the performance, there were moments where the performers would skate close to the edge of the rink, and the kids in the front row would reach out their hands, almost as if they could touch the characters. The energy in the arena was electric, with everyone cheering, clapping, and laughing together. Even the adults couldn’t help but get caught up in the infectious joy of the night.

When the show finally came to an end, the lights slowly came back up, and the performers took their final bows, waving to the crowd. Nicky, Billy, and Tommy stood up, clapping furiously and shouting their approval. 

“That was amazing!” Nicky yelled, his voice filled with genuine excitement.

Wanda, laughing, gave Agatha a playful look. “See? I told you it would be a good time. You’ve got a future ice-skater here,” she teased, nudging Agatha with her elbow.

Agatha shook her head with a grin. “I don’t know about that,” she replied, watching as Nicky bounced on his heels. "But he’s definitely got some enthusiasm.”

The entire group lingered for a moment, taking in the last bits of the performance as the arena slowly emptied out. The laughter, the chatter, the lingering joy—it was a perfect moment of shared happiness. 

As they made their way out of the arena, Nicky clutched her hand tightly, his face flushed with excitement. “Mom, that was the best day ever!” he declared, his voice filled with a sense of wonder.

Agatha glanced at Wanda, feeling a sense of gratitude for the unexpected joy of the night. Maybe it hadn’t been such a bad idea, after all.

As they stepped out of the arena, Billy and Tommy were already buzzing with excitement. “Mom, can we go to the mall?” Tommy asked, practically bouncing on his toes.

“Yeah, please, Mom? There’s an arcade there! And they have this cool new racing game!” Billy chimed in, his enthusiasm infectious.

Wanda raised an eyebrow, glancing at Vision, who nodded indulgently. “Well, I suppose we could. It’s not too late,” Wanda said thoughtfully, then turned to Agatha. “What do you think? Would Nicky like to join them?”

Agatha hesitated, her lips pressing into a thin line. Nicky was practically vibrating with excitement at the mention of the arcade, his big eyes fixed on her pleadingly. 

“Mom, can I? Please? I’ll be super good!” he promised, tugging on her hand.

Agatha sighed, torn. “I don’t know…” She trailed off, glancing between Wanda and Vision. “It’s been a long day, and I don’t want him running wild when he’s already this wired.”

“Oh, come on,” Wanda said, waving a hand dismissively. “The kids will be fine. Vision can take them to the arcade while we hit a few stores. It’ll give us a chance to catch up, and they’ll burn off some of that energy.”

Vision smiled warmly, his tone reassuring. “I’d be happy to watch them, Agatha. I’ll keep a close eye on all three, and I promise they won’t get into any trouble.”

Agatha glanced down at Nicky, whose face was a mix of hope and excitement. It was hard to say no when he looked so eager. 

“Fine,” she relented with a sigh, “but only if you promise to behave and stick with Vision the whole time.”

“I promise!” Nicky practically shouted, bouncing up and down.

“Great,” Wanda said with a grin, linking her arm through Agatha’s. “Let’s go, then. Shopping and some adult conversation are exactly what you need.”

Agatha couldn’t help but smile at Wanda’s enthusiasm, even as she mentally braced herself for what the next hour might hold. Together, they all headed for the mall, the kids already chattering excitedly about what games they would play at the arcade.

When they arrived, Vision took charge of the boys, guiding them toward the neon-lit entrance of the arcade, while Agatha and Wanda veered off toward the nearby shops. “Relax,” Wanda said, giving her a nudge. “They’ll be fine. Trust me, Vision’s practically a saint.”

“I’m sure he is,” Agatha muttered, watching as Nicky waved at her before disappearing into the arcade with Billy and Tommy. She couldn’t help but feel a little anxious, though she knew Nicky was in good hands.

“Now, come on,” Wanda said, tugging her toward a chic boutique. “Let’s see if we can find you something that isn’t black or purple. You know, a little color wouldn’t kill you.”

Agatha rolled her eyes but followed along, resigned to the fact that Wanda wasn’t going to let her leave without at least one new outfit. "You’re relentless, Maximoff," she muttered, but there was a hint of amusement in her tone.

The mall buzzed with weekend energy—teenagers wandering in packs, families bustling from store to store, and holiday sales signs screaming for attention. Agatha followed Wanda through the crowd, occasionally glancing back toward the arcade, even though it was out of sight. She tried not to think about how the boys were faring under Vision’s supervision, but Wanda’s chatter kept her mostly distracted.

They hit a few stores, starting with a boutique full of bohemian-style dresses that Wanda insisted were "so in right now"  

Agatha tried on exactly nothing, instead standing guard with their shopping bags while Wanda modeled a rust-colored wrap dress.

“I’m telling you, you’d look amazing in something like this,” Wanda said as she adjusted the neckline in the mirror. “It’s flowy but flattering. You’re all sharp angles; this would soften you up.”

“Thanks,” Agatha said dryly, but there was no real sting to her words. She was too used to Wanda’s relentless commentary.

Their next stop was a home goods store where Wanda ogled quirky throw pillows while Agatha discreetly checked her phone for messages from Vision. Nothing yet, which she decided to take as a good sign.

As they moved through the mall, Wanda suddenly came to an abrupt halt, her eyes lighting up like she’d struck gold.

Agatha followed her gaze and she spotted a lingerie store. 

“Ooooh perfect timing” Wanda said enthusiastically, grabbing Agatha’s arm. “We’re going in.”

Agatha balked. “Oh hell no”

“Come on!” Wanda said, practically dragging her toward the entrance. “I need to pick up a couple of things anyway. Vision’s been very...appreciative of these little trips lately, and I could use a refresh. And you…” she added, her grin turning mischievous, “should grab something too. Maybe spice things up a little”

“Do I have to?” Agatha groaned, attempting to keep walking.

“Yes,” Wanda said firmly, steering her toward the entrance. “I’m just saying, a little effort never hurts. Plus, you never know when you’ll need it.”

Agatha groaned but allowed herself to be pulled inside, instantly feeling out of place amid the racks of lacy bras, silk robes, and barely-there underwear. The store smelled like vanilla and roses, and the lighting was uncomfortably flattering. There were racks of delicate items in every shade imaginable. 

Wanda dove right in, flipping through racks with ease, confidence palpable, while Agatha lingered awkwardly near the entrance.

“Are you really going to just stand there?” Wanda asked, holding up a fiery red lace bodysuit. “You should pick something out too. You never know when it’ll come in handy.”

“I’m not seeing anyone,” Agatha said flatly.

“So?” Wanda replied, barely looking up from the rack she was browsing. “It’s not always about someone else. Sometimes it’s about feeling good for you .”

Agatha stood stiffly, her arms crossed.

“Seriously, Agatha, stop hovering like a suspicious mom at prom. Come pick something out,” Wanda called over her shoulder. 

“I’m fine, thanks,” Agatha said tightly, while rolling her eyes but begrudgingly followed Wanda through the store. She wasn’t about to let the closest thing she had to a friend  in this new city go. 

Wanda, of course, was in her element, piling bras, panties, and slips into her arms. “This would be amazing on you,” she said, her tone matter-of-fact,  holding up a sheer black slip.

Agatha’s face flushed. “Absolutely not,” she said, trying to wave her off.

“Why not?” Wanda pressed, her grin widening. “Live a little. It’s not like anyone has to see it.”

“That’s exactly why I don’t need it,” Agatha retorted.

But Wanda wasn’t letting up. She piled a few items into Agatha’s arms, ignoring her protests. “Here,” she said, thrusting a few things into Agatha’s hands. “Try these. Trust me, you’ll thank me later.”

Agatha stared at the pile of delicate garments, most of them far skimpier than anything she’d ever even considered wearing. 

“These are barely clothes.” she said, exasperated, holding up a bralette that looked more like a suggestion of clothing than an actual piece. 

“That’s the point,” Wanda replied, her grin widening “Go on.”

Agatha shuffled toward the dressing room, grumbling under her breath feeling both self-conscious and annoyed. She pushed the door closed behind her and eyed the pile of lingerie like it was a puzzle she didn’t particularly want to solve. Once inside, she stared at the pile of delicate fabrics with growing dread. Most of the pieces Wanda had chosen for her were daring: sheer bodysuits, bralettes with intricate lace patterns, and matching sets in bold, vibrant colors. 

She hesitated, her fingers brushing against the fabric. What was the point of lingerie anyway? She’d always considered herself pragmatic, bordering on prudish when it came to this sort of thing. If no one else was going to see it, why bother? 

Still, some part of her—a deeply buried part—felt intrigued. It wasn’t about anyone else, was it? Maybe it was about feeling... something for herself.

She sighed and tried on one of the simpler pieces, a satin bralette and matching shorts in a deep navy blue. Looking at her reflection, she felt a flush of embarrassment creeping up her neck. The outfit was flattering, even elegant, but it was so far outside her comfort zone.

She tried on a black lace set after that, studying her reflection with a mix of discomfort and curiosity. It wasn’t bad , exactly—it was just... a lot.

“You’re such a prude,” she muttered to herself, rolling her eyes at her own reaction

She decided she was done with whatever this stupid game was. But as she was changing, something caught her eye. 

A purple lace set.  

It was bold, almost scandalous, with intricate floral patterns that barely concealed anything and delicate straps that criss crossed in the back. She hesitated, her hand hovering over it before she quickly grabbed it.

“This is ridiculous,” she muttered to herself, but she couldn’t look away.

The set felt both daring and alluring in a way she couldn’t explain. It wasn’t something she’d normally choose, if ever, but there was something captivating about it. Instead of trying it on, she folded it neatly and set it aside to buy, deciding it was too much for even her to confront in the store.

When she finally emerged from the dressing room, Wanda was waiting, her arms full of her own finds. “Well?” she asked, raising an eyebrow.

Agatha stood there, her mind racing as she considered her options. She could tell Wanda the truth—that out of all the pieces, she’d only found one thing she liked—and risk her friend’s inevitable curiosity leading to her seeing the scandalous purple set. Or, she could avoid the conversation entirely by buying everything Wanda had picked out for her, even the items she had no intention of ever wearing. The thought of admitting she’d liked something as revealing as the purple lace was mortifying; she didn’t want Wanda to know she’d been captivated by it. She couldn't believe it herself if she was honest. 

The decision felt ridiculous, but her pride won out. She gave a quick nod to herself, her cheeks flushed. Wanda would never know, and that was all that mattered.

 “Don’t make a thing out of it.” she said while refusing to meet Wanda's eyes.

Wanda laughed, clearly enjoying herself. “Oh, I’m absolutely making a thing out of it. Look at you, branching out. I’m proud.”

“Let’s just pay and go,” Agatha said, grabbing the shopping bag and striding toward the register, her face still warm.

As Agatha stood in line, shifting uncomfortably under the weight of the lacy bundle in her arms, a prickle of awareness ran down her spine. The sensation of being watched was unmistakable, and she froze momentarily, her heart skipping a beat. Subtly, she glanced to the side, catching the faintest hint of brown hair in her peripheral vision. Her breath hitched.

Agatha turned her head sharply to confirm, her stomach twisting in a mix of dread and embarrassment. But when she scanned the store, she saw no familiar figure, just a cluster of shoppers bustling about, entirely indifferent to her and the stack of lingerie in her hands.

She swallowed hard, heat creeping up her neck. I’m imagining things. I have to be . The thought didn’t do much to calm her nerves, though. Her pulse thundered, the mortification settling in heavy and hot.

Wanda leaned against the counter as they shuffled forward in line, her sharp eyes narrowing as she studied Agatha’s pale face and darting gaze. “Okay, what is with you?” she asked, a smirk tugging at her lips. “You look like you’ve just seen a ghost.”

Agatha stiffened, clutching the bundle of lingerie to her chest as though it might shield her from further scrutiny. “I didn’t see anything,” she said firmly, though the tremor in her voice betrayed her. “ I thought I saw someone I knew, but it was nothing.”

Wanda’s grin widened, clearly not buying her nonchalance. “Uh-huh. You’re as white as a sheet, Agatha. Don’t think I didn’t notice that little jump you did back there. You practically dropped your... delicates .” She raised an eyebrow suggestively, glancing at the stack of lingerie in Agatha’s arms.

Agatha groaned, her cheeks burning. “It’s nothing, Wanda. Drop it.”

But Wanda wasn’t done. “Oh, no, this is definitely something. Did you see someone who shouldn’t know you’ve got a secret stash of lacey confidence boosters?”

Agatha’s head snapped toward Wanda, her mortification now fully on display. “Wanda!” she hissed. “Keep your voice down!”

Wanda barked a laugh, throwing her head back dramatically. “I knew it! You’re terrible at hiding things, Harkness. Come on, who was it?”

Agatha pressed her lips together in a tight line, refusing to give Wanda the satisfaction. “I didn’t see anyone,” she repeated. “Just... leave it, okay?”

Wanda studied her for a moment longer, her amusement only growing. “Fine,” she said finally, though her tone was anything but sincere. “But if you start hyperventilating over there, don’t expect me to revive you. I’d hate for the paramedics to find you clutching your stash like your life depended on it.”

Agatha groaned again, wishing the line would move faster so she could escape. I’m never going shopping with Wanda again.

As they left the store Agatha's cheeks burning as if everyone in the store could see through the bag.

Wanda was still grinning, and Agatha couldn’t help but shake her head at her friend’s persistence. But deep down, she had to admit—just barely—that maybe Wanda had a point.

Wanda couldn’t resist one last comment. “You know,” she said, her tone light but knowing, “sometimes it’s the things we think are too much that end up being just right.”

“Save the wisdom for your wedding vows,” Agatha shot back, though her tone lacked any real bite.

Wanda smirked but let it go, clearly satisfied she’d nudged Agatha out of her comfort zone. 

Deep down, she couldn’t stop thinking about the purple set. It felt like a tiny rebellion—a risk, just as Wanda had said. Maybe that wasn’t such a bad thing.

Chapter End Notes

I'm currently editing the next chapter and hoping to finish it by tomorrow as a Christmas present. It's a long one, so we'll see how it goes. Thank you for reading :)

Chapter 11

Chapter Notes

Christmas miracle incoming! I managed to push through editing this chapter while escaping the chaos of Christmas dinner with my family, so here it is. Merry Christmas to those who celebrate—enjoy!

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Agatha and Nicky arrived home late that evening, the day’s excitement still buzzing faintly in the air. Nicky ran inside, chattering about the arcade games and how much fun he had with Billy and Tommy. Agatha followed, carrying her only bag with a sense of relief to finally be home. After a quick dinner and bedtime routine, Nicky fell asleep, leaving Agatha alone with her thoughts. She unpacked the shopping bag, her eyes lingering on the purple lace set for a moment before shoving it into a drawer, her cheeks warming at the memory of picking it out.

The next three days passed in a blur of routine. Agatha slipped back into her life as though the break at Disney on Ice had been a dream. Mornings were spent waking Nicky, getting him ready, and dropping him off at daycare before heading to the hospital. Her days were packed with surgeries, patient rounds, and the endless mountain of administrative work that came with her job. She terrorized the residents as usual, demanding precision and discipline in every aspect of their work. They scrambled under her sharp gaze, and she allowed herself a sliver of satisfaction at their growing competence.

Lunches and coffee breaks occasionally broke up the monotony. Wanda and Mariah became her frequent companions during these moments, their easy banter a welcome distraction. Wanda, in particular, had a way of making Agatha laugh when she needed it most, though she never let herself enjoy it too much outwardly. Mariah’s grounded, no-nonsense attitude balanced out Wanda’s playful teasing, creating a strange but comforting trio that Agatha found herself growing accustomed to.

Rio was there, of course. Agatha saw her in passing, their schedules overlapping just enough for their paths to cross. Rio didn’t approach her, but her presence was impossible to ignore. That infuriating smirk was a constant, as if Rio knew exactly how to get under her skin without saying a single word. Agatha hated how aware she was of her, her mind fixating on those fleeting encounters far more than she cared to admit.

The days were busy, leaving little time to dwell on anything outside the hospital. Yet, the absence of updates on the woman and baby from the accident lingered at the back of her mind. Every time she checked their charts or consulted the ICU team, it was the same response: no significant changes. The mother remained in a coma, her prognosis uncertain, while the baby’s condition, though slightly improved, was still precarious.

By the third evening, Agatha sat in her quiet living room, sipping a glass of wine and staring at her phone. This life in Minnesota—this new routine—was beginning to feel familiar. Almost normal.

As the hum of her evening routine settled around her, Agatha’s thoughts drifted to Nicky’s upcoming birthday. The realization hit her like a wave—she hadn’t done anything to prepare yet. There were decisions to be made: the theme, the guest list, and, of course, she needed to call her ex husband. 

Her stomach twisted at the thought of calling him. They weren't exactly on speaking terms. The idea of hearing his voice, of navigating the delicate balance of civility for Nicky’s sake, filled her with dread. It wasn’t just the pain of their failed marriage that lingered; it was the anger, the resentment, and the lingering wounds she tried to keep buried. But she knew this call couldn’t be avoided. Daniel was still Nicky’s father, and their shared love for him meant Agatha had to set aside her pride, at least for now.

She let out a long, frustrated sigh as she sank into the couch. The thought of Daniel’s presence at Nicky’s birthday, of him seeing her was almost unbearable. She had worked so hard to build a life outside of their fractured past, a life that felt like it was finally hers. Inviting him into that new world, even if it was for Nicky’s sake, felt like a betrayal to the version of herself she was trying so desperately to hold on to.

She didn’t want him to see the way her life had taken shape without him in it. It was one thing to share custody of Nicky, to remain civil when it came to their son. But this….this was different. This was an invitation to let him back in, if only for a day. It felt like opening a door she had worked so hard to lock.

But Nicky was relentless. He wanted his father there. He specifically asked her. Agatha couldn’t bring herself to deny him that, no matter how much the thought of it made her stomach churn. Her son deserved both of his parents to be there, even if it meant pretending for a few hours, even if it meant biting her tongue and swallowing the bitter taste of regret.

As she picked up her phone, her fingers hovered over the screen. The message she was about to send felt like a weight on her chest.

 "Hi, Daniel. We’re planning Nicky’s birthday . He’d really like for you to be there. Please let me know when i can call you so we can figure something out" 

She hated the simplicity of it, hated how it made her feel like a mother caught between two worlds. But there was no other way.

Agatha hit send, the action too quick to stop, but she couldn’t bring herself to read the message again. Instead, she tossed the phone onto the couch beside her and buried her face in her hands.

"Why does it always come back to him?" she whispered, frustration bubbling in her chest.

She knew the answer: Nicky. Because, despite everything, he was their son. And this was the world they had to navigate for his sake.

And then there was Nat. She had been reaching out steadily over the past two months since she quit her job at NYU. Agatha had avoided every call, ignored every text. It wasn’t that she didn’t want to talk to Nat—it was that she couldn’t. Not yet. There was too much to say and too many feelings she didn’t know how to put into words.

Still, the ache of their silence gnawed at her. Nat had been there through everything, thick and thin. She didn’t deserve the radio silence. Agatha set her jaw, grabbed her phone, and scrolled through her contacts until she found Nat’s name. The sight of it made her chest tighten. With a deep breath, she tapped the call button.

The line rang twice before a familiar voice, warm and tinged with surprise, answered.


“Agatha?” Nat’s voice was bright, the kind of bright that made it clear she’d been waiting for this call.

“Hey, Nat,” Agatha said, her voice soft and hesitant. “It’s been a while.”

“You fucking bitch !” Nat exploded, not missing a beat. “Are you shitting me right now? Seriously , Agatha. You’ve been MIA for months , and all I get is a goddamn ‘Hey, Nat, it’s been a while’? What the actual fuck is wrong with you? I should fucking murder you right now. I swear to God, I hope you’re sitting down because I’m about to verbally eviscerate your sorry ass.”

Agatha blinked, holding the phone slightly away from her ear as Nat’s words came rapid-fire, each one landing like a slap.

“I called you, what, like a thousand fucking times? Texted you more than that. I was fucking worried, Agatha. Do you have any idea how much that pisses me off? Any? Of course you don’t, because you’re a goddamn coward who thinks she can just fucking disappear and everyone will be fine with it. Well, newsflash to you asshole: we’re not fine. I’m not fine. You’re not allowed to ghost me, you absolute fucking piece of shit.”

Agatha opened her mouth to respond, but Nat was on a roll.

“And Minnesota ? Really? Are you fucking kidding me? You move halfway across the fucking country, and I find out from your Instagram ? Which, by the way, looks like it’s from the goddamn Stone Age because you haven’t updated that shit since 2009. What the fuck, Agatha? What the actual fuck? Do you have any idea how it feels to realize your best friend has dropped off the face of the Earth and didn’t think to clue you in?” 

Agatha winced. “Nat, I—”

“No, don’t ‘Nat, I’ me,” she snapped. “I’m not done. So youre gonna have to shut your mouth and let me finish.  You’ve been my best friend for, what, more than two decades? And you think it’s okay to pull this silent-treatment crap? Like, what the hell am I supposed to do with that? I thought you and your pathetic ass were dead for a hot minute! But then I remembered—oh, right—Agatha is too much of a stubborn bitch to die without leaving some passive-aggressive bullshit behind.”

Agatha couldn’t help it—she laughed, a small chuckle that grew into full-on laughter.

“I’m sorry, okay? You’re right. I’m an asshole. I should’ve called sooner,” she admitted, her voice tinged with guilt.

“Damn fucking straight , you should’ve,” Nat snapped, though her voice softened slightly. “You don’t get to ditch me just because life gets hard. That’s not how this works, you fucking disaster excuse of a human being.”

 

“I know,” Agatha said, her voice quieter now. “I just... I needed some space. Things have been messy, and I didn’t want to dump all of that on you.”

Nat let out an exaggerated sigh, the kind Agatha knew well, the one Nat used when she was both frustrated and amused. “Honestly, you’re so dramatic. Agatha, I don’t care how messy things are. You don’t get to decide I can’t handle it. That’s not your call to make. I’m not fragile, Agatha and you’re not a burden and I’m not going anywhere. If you needed space, I get it. I’ve been through everything with you. You really think I can’t handle a little more chaos?”

Agatha swallowed hard, the lump in her throat making it difficult to speak. “I’m sorry, Nat. I mean it. I just... I didn’t know how to talk about everything.”

“Start with the basics,” Nat said, her tone gentler now but still firm. “Are you okay? Is Nicky okay?”

“Yeah, we’re okay,” Agatha said, a small smile tugging at her lips. “He’s doing great. He loves Minnesota. I think he likes the snowy weather more than you do.”

Nat laughed. “Of course he does, I taught him well. So, what’s the deal? Are you finally ready to act like I exist again, or is this a one-time pity call?”

Agatha hesitated, then took a deep breath. “Actually, I was calling for a reason. Nicky’s birthday is coming up, and I was hoping you could make it. He misses you, and, well... so do I.”

Nat was quiet for a moment before she said, “Of course I’ll come. Like hell I’d miss it. Just give me the date, and I’ll be there. But Agatha, if you ever ghost me again, I’m showing up at your house and making your life a living hell. Got it?”

Agatha laughed again, feeling the weight of the past few months start to lift. “Got it. No more ghosting. I promise.”

There was a brief pause before Nat’s voice softened. “ Tell him I’ll be there. And don’t you dare make me come to that party without some good cake, okay?”

Agatha laughed, a sense of warmth spreading through her. “Deal. It wouldn’t be a party without cake. I’ll make sure it’s good.”

“Good. Now, tell me everything,” Nat said, her voice lighter now. “And don’t you dare leave out the messy bits. You know those are my favorite.”

They talked for nearly an hour, the conversation a balm for Agatha’s weary soul. Nat caught her up on her life in New York—her chaotic schedule, a tricky surgery she’d performed, and a funny story about a clueless intern who mistook a scrub nurse for an attending. Agatha laughed, genuinely laughed, at Nat’s spot-on impression of the mortified intern trying to backpedal.

When it was her turn, Agatha shared snippets of her new life: how much Nicky loved his new daycare, the charm of the small Minnesota town, and the slightly slower pace of the hospital compared to her previous job. She even mentioned Wanda and Mariah and how she terrorized the residents.

But she avoided the more vulnerable parts. She didn’t mention how lonely the nights could feel or how she sometimes doubted her decision to leave New York. Most of all, she didn’t mention Rio. It was too raw, too complicated, and she wasn’t ready to unpack it—not even with Nat or herself even.

Nat seemed to sense Agatha’s guardedness, but she didn’t push. Instead, she filled the silences with light-hearted anecdotes, seamlessly steering the conversation whenever it veered too close to dangerous territory.

“And the weather” Agatha said at one point, shaking her head even though Nat couldn’t see her. “Don’t get me started. Nicky loves it. Meanwhile, I’m slipping on ice every time I step outside. It’s like nature’s way of telling me I don’t belong here.”

Nat chuckled. “You? Slipping on ice? That’s a mental image I’m going to treasure. Did you get snow boots?”

“I did,” Agatha admitted. “And they make me look like a Yeti.”

“Better a stylish Yeti than a bruised one,” Nat quipped. “I’ll get you a matching parka.”

The conversation meandered, touching on everything and nothing. By the time they said their goodbyes, Agatha felt lighter, like she’d set down a weight she hadn’t realized she was carrying.

“Thanks, Nat,” she said softly, just before they hung up.

“For what?” Nat’s voice was warm, teasing but kind.

“For being you,” Agatha said.

There was a pause, and then Nat replied, her tone playful again, “You’re damn right. And don’t you forget it. I'll see you in a few days”

As Agatha set her phone down, a small smile lingered on her lips feeling a small sense of relief. Reconnecting with Nat hadn’t solved everything, but it was a start. And even though she still had to face Daniel and the looming task of planning Nicky’s birthday, for now, she felt a little less alone.

Agatha fell asleep that night with an unfamiliar but welcome sense of ease. For once, her mind wasn’t buzzing with unfinished tasks or tangled thoughts. The warmth of her conversation with Nat lingered, and she let it carry her into a deep, dreamless sleep.

When morning came, it wasn’t the shrill beeping of her alarms that woke her—it was the sunlight streaming through the window and the realization that something was off. Very off.

She jolted awake, her heart racing as she glanced at the clock on her nightstand. 6:47 a.m.

“Shit!” Agatha bolted upright, panic flooding her system. Her shift started at 7:00.

How had she slept through all three alarms? How had she not heard a single one? She scrambled out of bed, her thoughts a blur as she yanked on the first pair of scrubs she could find, threw her hair into a messy ponytail, and splashed cold water on her face.

Her phone buzzed on the counter, and Agatha snatched it up, squinting at the screen. A text from Mariah lit up the display:

“Are you on your way? Chaos here. The shift was shit. I need to hand it over to you today apparently. Dr. Mahomes called in sick. Call me.”

Agatha groaned, dragging a hand over her face. Chaos. Of course, it would be chaos today. And of course, the on-call OB GYN had decided not to show up. Typical. “Useless idiot,” she muttered, already imagining the mess waiting for her at the hospital.

There wasn’t time for breakfast or even coffee. She barely paused long enough to text Nicky’s nanny, explaining that she’d need to cover for her this morning. The guilt came in waves as she realized she hadn’t even said good morning to Nicky. She’d barely glanced at his door in her rush to leave.

“Get it together,” she muttered to herself, slinging her bag over her shoulder and grabbing her coat.

The drive to the hospital felt like a blur of traffic lights and frustrated glances at the clock. 7:27 a.m. She should’ve been there half an hour ago, at least. She prided herself on being the one who never faltered, who had everything under control. This? This was unacceptable.

Her grip on the steering wheel tightened as she whispered. This wasn’t like her. Agatha prided herself on punctuality, on being the one who had everything under control. She didn’t do late. She didn’t do oversleeping.

She parked her car crookedly in the hospital lot, barely taking the time to lock it before racing through the sliding doors. Inside, the energy was palpable—residents were darting down hallways, nurses looked harried, and the air buzzed with the chaos of an overbooked and understaffed shift.

“Morning, Dr. Harkness!” nurse Kale called out as she passed.

“Hold that thought,” Agatha snapped back. “Rounds will have to wait.”

She headed straight for her office, not even sparing a glance at her reflection in the glass walls as she tossed her bag inside. Her ponytail was half-falling apart, her scrubs slightly wrinkled, but there wasn’t time to care.

Mariah intercepted her at the door, her face a mixture of relief and pure exhaustion.

“Thank god you’re finally here,” Mariah said, pushing a tablet into Agatha’s hands. “We’ve got three women in labor, one of them already fully dilated. There’s also a possible pre-eclampsia case in triage, and the residents are...” She trailed off, gesturing vaguely in a way that screamed lost cause .

“Fantastic,” Agatha deadpanned, scanning the list of patients. “Any other catastrophes I should know about?”

Mariah rolled her eyes. “Just the usual. Oh, and Dr. Mahomes? He didn’t even call the nurses. I had to cover his post-op follow-ups before my shift ended.”

Agatha muttered a curse under her breath. “Coward.”

Mariah smirked but quickly sobered. “Are you good to jump in? I mean, you look like you haven’t had coffee in days, and—”

“Never better,” Agatha interrupted, tying her hair back and heading toward triage with long, purposeful strides. “Hand it over, Mariah. You’re officially off OBGYN duty. Go back to peds”

As she pushed through the doors to triage, a frazzled-looking resident practically skidded to a stop in front of her, holding out a chart like it was a shield. His face was pale, his expression uncertain.

“Dr. Harkness, the pre-eclampsia patient is asking for her husband, but he’s stuck in traffic—”

Agatha snatched the chart without breaking stride, barely sparing him a glance. “Then inform her that I’m not only the next best thing—I’m the best thing. And unless her husband has a medical degree and a scalpel in hand, I’m all she’s got right now. Now get the fuck out of my way”

The resident blinked, stunned, before scrambling out of her way. Agatha rolled her eyes, muttering under her breath, “I swear, they get greener every year.”

The first delivery was underway before she even had time to catch her breath. The laboring mother was panicked, clutching the side rails of the hospital bed with white-knuckled intensity. Agatha swept in, calm but commanding, barking instructions to the nurses while gently reassuring the patient.

“You’re doing great,” she said firmly, positioning herself. “Now, I need you to push like you’re evicting a bad tenant. No half measures. Got it?”

The woman gave a shaky nod, and within minutes, the cries of a newborn filled the room. Agatha handed the baby off to the waiting nurse with a rare, fleeting smile.

The pre-eclampsia patient was next. Agatha moved quickly, her mind already cataloging the potential complications. The patient was young, terrified, and trying to keep herself together while clutching her swollen belly.

“Dr. Harkness,” she rasped, her voice shaky. “Am I going to be okay?”

“You’re in the best hands possible,” Agatha replied without hesitation, her tone brisk but reassuring. “I’ve got this, and so do you. Now, we’re going to get that blood pressure down and make sure your baby gets to meet their badass mom.”

The procedure went smoothly, despite the initial tension. By the time Agatha stepped out of the room, her scrubs were damp with sweat, but her mind was clear. She’d done what needed to be done.

Agatha’s phone buzzed just as she finished scrubbing out. Pulling it from her pocket, she saw a message from Dr. Calderu.

“Agatha, I hope you’re doing great. Dr. Gulliver from St. Cloud hospital came in and is taking over your rounds now. She’ll handle the shift afterward so you can focus on your cases. Let me know if you need anything else!”

Agatha let out a breath she hadn’t realized she’d been holding. The chaos of the morning was finally starting to untangle itself. 

She quickly typed a reply:

“Thanks, Dr. Calderu.”

Shoving her phone back into her pocket, Agatha adjusted her coat and turned toward the staff lounge. She needed a moment to regroup before diving back into the whirlwind of her cases.

It was shaping up to be a long day, but at least she could now give her full attention to her patients without worrying about the rest of the ward falling apart.

As Agatha headed down the hallway, she nearly bumped into Mariah, who was walking briskly toward the lounge with a clipboard in hand.

“Hey, finally caught you,” Mariah said, eyeing her with a mix of curiosity and amusement. “How’s the morning treating you? You looked ready to murder someone earlier.”

Agatha let out a sharp exhale. “It’s been... something. But Dr. Calderu just texted. Apparently, Dr. Gulliver from another hospital is taking over rounds and the rest of the shift. So I can focus on the cases that are piling up.”

Mariah’s eyebrows shot up. “Oh, Alice Gulliver? She’s cool. We like her. She covers for OBGYN all the time when things go sideways.”

Agatha curled an eyebrow ignoring that Mariah called Dr Gulliver cool. “We like her? Since when do you hand out seals of approval to other doctors?”

Mariah smirked, crossing her arms. “ Relax. She’s chill. Doesn’t pull rank unnecessarily, knows her stuff, and doesn’t leave a mess for us to clean up. Plus, she comes out for drinks with us sometimes”

Agatha snorted. “Well, as long as she’s good for your after-work happy hours, I suppose I can trust her with the department.”

“Damn right,” Mariah replied with a grin. “Maybe we should go out tonight. We’re overdue for a drink, and I’m pretty sure even Alice has seen more of our team socially than you have.”

“I’m flattered,” Agatha said dryly. “But I think I’ll leave the bonding to you and your favorite backup OB-GYN for now.”

Mariah shook her head, laughing as she walked away. “Suit yourself. Don’t say I didn’t try!”

Agatha allowed herself a small smile as she watched Mariah disappear down the hall. 

Agatha made her way to the NICU, her mind already shifting to the cases she needed to check on. The familiar hum of machines and soft beeping sounds greeted her as she entered the ward. She scanned the room, her eyes landing on a group of residents and nurses gathered around a bassinet.

A steady, confident voice was leading the rounds, explaining a patient’s progress with calm authority. The atmosphere was notably serene—no squirming residents, no flustered nurses. It was almost... unsettling.

She couldn’t see who was speaking, but the tone carried an air of command that piqued her curiosity. Agatha approached, her heels clicking softly against the floor. “Good morning,” she said, her voice cutting through the quiet like a blade.

The air shifted instantly, the circle of medical staff parting to make way for her. And that’s when she saw it—a flash of vibrant orange hair.

What the fuck.

Agatha’s eyes traveled downward, taking in the figure leading the group. Combat boots. Jeans. A black tank top, of all things, under a rumpled white lab coat. It wasn’t just the hair—black with streaks of bright orange —it was the whole aesthetic. She looked like she’d wandered off a music festival stage and straight into a hospital ward.

The doctor turned, catching sight of Agatha, and smiled brightly, extending a hand. “You must be Dr. Harkness. I’m Dr. Gulliver. We’ve already finished rounds—just going over a few finer details with the team.”

Agatha’s hand reflexively met hers in a firm shake, but her mind was reeling. Dr. Alice Gulliver, apparently. The name clicked—Mariah had mentioned her.

“Welcome,” Agatha said, her voice carefully neutral. Her eyes, however, flicked to the group, noting their unusually relaxed postures. Everyone seemed uncharacteristically calm, as if Gulliver had sprinkled some kind of rebellious fairy dust over the ward.

Dr. Gulliver gestured toward the bassinet they’d been discussing. “This little one is holding steady. No major changes since the last report, which, in our world, is good news. We’re keeping an eye on oxygen saturation levels, but the trend is positive.”

Agatha nodded stiffly. “I see. Thank you for stepping in.”

As Gulliver turned back to the residents, Agatha couldn’t stop her thoughts from spiraling. What kind of self-respecting doctor dressed like that? Combat boots. Tinted hair. A tank top. She wasn’t just unorthodox; she was outright defying every unspoken rule of professional appearance Agatha held dear.

And the Mayo Clinic allowed this?

Agatha’s jaw tightened as she folded her arms, leaning against the nearest counter. She watched Gulliver address the group with easy confidence, her tone warm but authoritative. The residents hung on every word, nodding attentively. It was infuriating.

Infuriating because it was clear they liked her.

Agatha couldn’t decide what unsettled her more: Gulliver’s complete disregard for decorum or the undeniable fact that she seemed competent. 

As Dr. Gulliver breezed into her shift, the NICU seemed to hum with an odd blend of calm efficiency and the faint ripple of chaos that came with change. Agatha took a moment to survey the residents still lingering after rounds. Their postures were too relaxed, their expressions bordering on smug.

Agatha stepped forward, her tone brisk. “Alright, people. You’re still on the clock. NICU isn’t a place for complacency. Let’s review protocols for neonatal resuscitation, and I want assessments of every patient in your care before the end of the hour. Move.”

The residents scrambled, tension snapping back into place under her firm command. She folded her arms, a small, satisfied smile tugging at her lips. Authority restored.

After another sweep of the ward, Agatha decided to grab a late lunch. She was halfway to the cafeteria when she spotted Rio sitting at a table near the window. As usual, Rio exuded that effortlessly confident air, casually leaning back in her chair, munching on a sandwich while scrolling through her phone. Agatha hesitated for a moment, then quickly made her way into the line, hoping Rio hadn’t noticed her. They hadn’t spoken since that dinner, and Agatha was certain the last thing she needed today was to deal with that infuriating woman.

She kept her head down as she grabbed a tray, mentally preparing herself for the chaos of the shift ahead. The last thing she wanted was to get roped into another one of Rio’s games.

Agatha was midway through grabbing a coffee in the hospital cafeteria when she heard the sound of footsteps behind her. Her heart sank. She didn’t need to turn around to know who it was. Of course, she would show up just when Agatha was trying to have a moment to herself.

“Well, well,” Rio’s voice rang out, loud and teasing enough to turn a few heads. “If it isn’t Dr. Harkness herself, descending from her tower to grace us mere mortals with her presence.”

Agatha stiffened, her grip tightening on her cup. She’d been hoping for a quiet break, but of course, Rio had to ruin it.  She turned slowly, taking in the sight of Rio leaning against the counter  with infuriating ease, one arm casually slung over it. Her smirk was there, as usual—lopsided, confident, and entirely too knowing. For the first time since they met she was wearing scrubs. Not the hospital baggy ones. She was wearing black ones. The fitted material clung to her form in a way that Agatha hadn’t expected, highlighting the toned muscles in her arms.  They fit a little too well, hugging her frame in a way that left very little to the imagination.

“Do you even drink coffee, or do you just come here to look busy?” Rio quipped, her eyes glinting with amusement.

There was something about the way Rio moved now in those scrubs. Fluid, confident, like she belonged in them more than anyone else in the hospital.

Agatha narrowed her eyes, trying her best to stay composed. The way those scrubs fit her, the way her muscles moved effortlessly under the fabric—it should’ve been irrelevant, but Agatha couldn’t help the way her gaze lingered for a second too long before snapping back to her usual sharp, dismissive demeanor

"I come here for coffee, not to be interrogated by you," Agatha said, her voice flat but carrying the bite she always put in it around Rio. “And just so you know I drink coffee just fine, thank you for your concern,” 

She grabbed her cup, pretending to focus on it, but the pressure of Rio’s presence, her teasing energy, was like a magnet pulling her attention back.

“Of course you do,” Rio said, stepping closer, her smirk deepening. “But let’s be real, coffee’s just a prop, isn’t it? You’re way too controlled for caffeine to actually do anything. This is all part of the act, right? The ice queen routine?”

Agatha groaned audibly, pinching the bridge of her nose. “Why is it physically impossible for you to take anything seriously? Do you even know how to have a normal conversation, or do you just go around annoying everyone you meet until they give up and leave?”

Rio shrugged, unbothered. “Annoying you is my favorite pastime, actually. And judging by how much you’re talking, I’d say I’m doing a damn good job.”

Agatha’s jaw tightened, and she fought the urge to roll her eyes. "I’m not sure who you think you’re impressing with that smug attitude, but it’s definitely not me," she shot back, her tone sharper than usual. Agatha inhaled sharply and shot Rio a glare. “You don’t know a damn thing about me,” she said, her voice colder than the iced coffee in her hand.

“Oh, I know plenty,” Rio replied, her voice dropping just slightly, like she was letting Agatha in on a secret. “I know you hate being interrupted, but here I am. I know you’d rather be anywhere else right now, and yet, here you are. And I know…” She paused, her eyes raking over Agatha in a way that made her skin heat, “…you can’t stand how much I’m getting under your skin right now.”

Agatha’s jaw tightened. “You’re not getting under my skin,” she hissed, though even to her own ears, it sounded unconvincing.

Rio grinned, taking another step closer, close enough that Agatha could see the faint hint of freckles across her nose. “Sure I’m not. That’s why you’re gripping that cup like it owes you money. Want me to let you borrow a stress ball?”

Agatha rolled her eyes, her patience wearing dangerously thin. “Do you ever shut up?” she snapped.

“Not when I’m having this much fun,” Rio replied smoothly. “And right now? I’m having a blast.”

Agatha’s hand twitched like she wanted to throw the coffee at her, but instead, she forced herself to take a slow, deliberate sip. “You must be desperate for entertainment if this counts as fun for you,” she said, her voice cutting.

“Not desperate,” Rio said, her smirk growing impossibly wider. “Just highly motivated. Watching you try not to lose your shit? Highlight of my day.”

Agatha’s glare could’ve melted steel. “I’m sure that says more about your pathetic existence than it does about me.”

Rio chuckled, tilting her head as though considering. “Maybe. Or maybe it just means you’re the most interesting thing in this place. You should be flattered, really.”

“Flattered?” Agatha barked out a humorless laugh. “I’m irritated. There’s a difference, though I doubt you’d understand.”

“Sure, sure,” Rio said, nodding mock-seriously. “I mean, if I were in your shoes, I’d probably be irritated too. Having to fight this hard to pretend I’m not into someone? Exhausting.”

Agatha clenched her jaw and took a slow sip of her coffee, the bitterness matching her mood. “You might want to stop now before you embarrass yourself further,” she said coolly, though her hand gripped the cup just a little too tightly.

Rio let out a low, amused hum, stepping closer still, now barely an arm’s length away. “Embarrass myself? Sweetheart, I thrive on embarrassment—other people’s, mostly. But if you think you can phase me, by all means, give it a shot”

Agatha raised an eyebrow, her tone dripping with sarcasm. “Ah, so that’s it. You bother me because your life is boring. What a tragic little existence you must lead. I’ll light a candle for you later—if I remember.”

Rio threw her head back and laughed, loud enough that several staff members glanced their way, though Rio clearly didn’t care. “Wow, a candle? That’s generous for you. Didn’t think you had a charitable bone in your body. Must be an early Christmas miracle.”

Agatha’s cheeks flushed, her voice rising. “Excuse me?!”

“Oh, don’t worry,” Rio said, her tone practically dripping with fake reassurance. “Your secret’s safe with me. I know admitting things isn’t exactly your strong suit.”

Agatha took a step forward, her voice low and venomous now. “You are the most insufferable person I have ever met.”

“And you,” Rio said, leaning in just enough to invade her space, her smirk bordering on predatory now, “are the most fun person to mess with.”

Agatha groaned audibly, pinching the bridge of her nose. “You need a goddamn hobby.”

Rio’s laugh was loud and genuine, drawing more attention from the staff around them. “This is my hobby, Harkness. And judging by how riled up you are, I’m really good at it.”

“I think you’ve spent too much time being the center of attention.”

“Me? The center of attention?” Rio laughed, stepping closer again, her teasing nature unrelenting. “Look, Harkness, you’re the one who can’t seem to get enough of me. It’s fine. I don’t mind the attention.” She leaned in, her voice lowering just a little, her words almost a challenge. “But don’t lie to yourself. I know I’m on your mind. I’m always on your mind.”

Agatha’s face flushed with frustration, and she couldn’t decide if she wanted to slap Rio or walk away. Instead, she clenched her jaw, trying to keep her cool.  "Nice try, but you’re still the same annoying pain in my ass." she said, but even as she spoke, she could hear the lie in her own voice.

Rio’s grin widened, and she crossed her arms, leaning lazily against the counter like she had all the time in the world. “That’s creative. Do you sit at home coming up with these, or do they just pop into your head when you see me? Be honest, I’m flattered either way.”

Agatha glared, heat rising to her face. “Believe me, I don’t waste a single thought on you outside of these unfortunate encounters.” she said. 

Liar her subconscient said.

Rio’s smile was smug, and she raised her eyebrows. “Yeah, sure. Whatever you say, Harkness. ”

Without another word, Agatha turned and walked away, her pulse racing, her thoughts a tangled mess. She could feel Rio’s eyes on her back, the teasing, relentless energy following her like a shadow.

“Bye, sweetheart!” Rio called after her, her voice laced with mock sweetness. 

Agatha didn’t turn around, but her ears burned as she stormed off, her pulse racing and her thoughts a tangled mess. Behind her, Rio’s laughter echoed like a victory bell.

She huffed while she marched out, her appetite evaporating. She retreated to her office, locking the door behind her. Lunch, such as it was, consisted of a granola bar and coffee while she reviewed charts in solitude.

Later that afternoon, Agatha headed to the weekly department head meeting. The conference room buzzed with chatter as chairs filled, and Agatha quickly spotted Wanda at a table near the back. She made her way over, grateful for a friendly face. 

“Mariah got lucky with a free evening,” Wanda remarked, sipping her coffee.

“Don’t remind me,” Agatha muttered, glancing around the room.

As Agatha settled into the seat beside Wanda. Her eyes landed on Rio, seated near the middle of the room who was still casually flipping through papers, completely unbothered by the presence of anyone around her. Agatha gritted her teeth, forcing herself to turn away. The last thing she needed was to let Rio's mere existence throw her off again.

Dr. Calderu finally entered the room, cutting through the chatter like a calm authority. She gave a small nod to the group, her glasses catching the light as she adjusted them.

“Good afternoon, everyone,” Dr. Calderu greeted, her voice steady and composed, effortlessly quieting the room. “I trust everyone’s had a productive week?”

A few murmurs of assent filled the air, but Agatha couldn’t help but glance at Rio again. Her posture was relaxed, one arm casually draped over the back of her chair as she gave the impression that nothing could phase her.

“Let’s get down to business,” Dr. Calderu continued, her eyes sweeping over the room.

As the meeting began, Agatha forced her focus onto the agenda, though it was nearly impossible to ignore the occasional glance Rio threw her way, always paired with that infuriating smirk.

Agatha couldn’t deny the way her body seemed to take notice, the way her eyes lingered on the defined muscles in Rio’s arms as she reached for a file from the nearby shelf. 

Agatha felt a strange flutter in her chest, quickly suppressing it with a sharp breath. Why do I care? she asked herself, trying to dismiss the feeling. 

It wasn’t like it was anything new. She’d seen plenty of people in scrubs, plenty of doctors, and it wasn’t as if Rio’s presence here had any bearing on her day.

She shook her head, quickly turning her focus to Dr Calderu, forcing herself to look away from Rio before she could let her thoughts linger too long. It’s just the scrubs, Agatha told herself, but her pulse betrayed her, thrumming a little faster than it should’ve.

“We have other important items on the agenda today. Let's  go over staffing updates. Rio would you be so kind to brief us on any changes?”

Agatha’s gaze immediately shifted to Rio as Dr. Calderu motioned toward her. Rio’s lips curled up into a smile, but it wasn’t her usual teasing grin—it was more calculated, like she knew exactly how everyone was watching. She lifted a hand slightly, acknowledging the request.

“Sure, Lilia” Rio replied smoothly, her tone confident and casual, as always. “We’re a bit short this week, but we’ve got things under control. I’ll make sure we don’t miss a beat, as usual.” She glanced briefly toward Agatha, the glint in her eye unmistakable. “I'll keep ortho running like a well-oiled machine.”

Agatha’s eyes narrowed, but she didn’t respond. She knew Rio liked the attention, loved playing the role of the cool, collected one, and Agatha wasn’t about to give her the satisfaction of reacting.

Dr. Calderu cleared her throat, pulling the group’s attention back to him. “Thanks Rio. Now, let’s move on to the patient care reports. I’ll hand it over to Agatha”

Agatha tensed as she was called on. She straightened in her seat, gathering her thoughts quickly before she spoke, forcing her focus back to the task at hand. "We’ve had a busy week in the maternity ward, but everything’s under control. We’ve seen a spike in high-risk pregnancies, so we're closely monitoring those cases. I’ve been overseeing a few potential complications, but nothing out of the ordinary for this time of year.”

Her voice was sharp and direct, cutting through the tension in the room as she scanned her notes. She could feel Rio’s eyes on her again, but this time, Agatha didn’t let it distract her. Not now, not here.

“Good work, Harkness,” Dr. Calderu nodded, giving her a small but genuine compliment. “Now, onto surgical outcomes. Dr. Hunt, if you can provide an update?”

As Dr. Calderu continued leading the meeting, Agatha’s attention began to wane, the rhythm of the discussions blending into a dull hum.

Her phone buzzed quietly in her pocket. Agatha glanced down, her heart skipping a beat when she saw the name on the screen—Daniel.

Hello Agatha. Nice to hear. I'll be there. Call me tonight so we can arrange the details.

The words were simple, yet they hit her like a sudden, unexpected wave. Her chest tightened, a mix of longing and confusion swirling within her.

Will do she typed and pushed the phone back into her pocket, her fingers brushing the screen with a slight tremor. 

Oh god.  

She needed a drink. Going out with Mariah and the highlighter haired doctor started to look more appealing.

The voice of Dr. Calderu snapped her back into the present. "Agatha?"

She blinked, looking up in confusion. Wanda's hand was lightly resting on her arm. Agatha’s mind scrambled to catch up with the conversation.

“Yeah” Agatha said quickly, trying to shake off the weight of the moment. 

Dr. Calderu nodded, her expression neutral. "Alright, great to hear it's settled then." She said with a smile and then moved on, seamlessly shifting to the next topic in the meeting, and Agatha sat there, still trying to piece together what the hell had just happened. What did I just agree to?

She glanced over at Wanda, who was holding back a laugh, her lips twitching with amusement. Agatha narrowed her eyes, leaning in slightly. "What the hell did I just agree to?" she whispered, barely containing her frustration.

Wanda’s smile widened. "Trauma certification for the first-year residents," she said, her tone a mix of sympathy and amusement.

Agatha felt her stomach drop. "Trauma certification? For the first-year residents?" she repeated, as if saying it aloud would somehow make it more logical. “Fuck”

She could feel her pulse quicken, the heat of frustration creeping up her neck. Her brain was a jumbled mess, processing the words from earlier, trying to put the pieces together. And then, of course, the message from Daniel.

Agatha gritted her teeth. She didn’t even realize she was clenching her jaw until it hurt. Oh god, she thought, fuming inside. She could feel the anger bubbling up—anger at herself, at the chaos of the meeting, and especially at Daniel for throwing her off course.

It was his fault. All of it. If he hadn't texted her, if she hadn’t been so damn distracted by the message, she wouldn’t have been caught off guard in the meeting, agreeing to whatever this trauma certification thing was. She didn’t need this right now. Not with everything else on her plate.

Wanda’s voice broke through her seething thoughts. "You good, Agatha?" she asked, her tone teasing.

Agatha forced a tight smile. "Yeah," she said, trying to keep her voice steady. "Never been better" Her sarcasm was thick, but Wanda didn’t seem to mind.

Wanda leaned back in her chair, her expression almost too casual. "You’ll do great," she said with a sly grin. "And don’t worry. At least you won't have to do it alone. You and Rio will do well together."

Agatha froze. "Wait, what?" she sputtered. 

“She volunteered before Lilia asked you” Wanda said oblivious to the turmoil that was growing inside of agatha. "You two will do fine. No need to worry about it. You’re both capable, and it’ll give you a chance to work closely together.

Agatha felt a wave of dread wash over her. Oh, she was fucked.  

Her mind raced, the words feeling like they were being absorbed through a fog. Rio volunteered? The realization hit her like a punch to the gut, making her momentarily dizzy. How in the world had this become her reality? She could feel the heat rising in her chest, her frustration mounting as everything started to crash down on her. 

Rio.

Again. 

The idea of being paired with her for something as intense as trauma certification sent a jolt of annoyance through Agatha, tightening her shoulders and making her fists clench under the table.

She volunteered. Why would anyone willingly volunteer to teach those hopelessly incompetent first-year residents? Agatha’s mind churned with disbelief, the pieces not fitting into place. The chaos of the meeting, Daniel’s text, and now this— no —this couldn’t be happening. She didn’t want to be anywhere near Rio, especially in such a professional capacity. And yet, now she was stuck with it.

Agatha’s jaw tightened as she forced herself to focus on whatever Lilia was saying, but her brain was still screaming.

She glared across the room and her heart skipped a beat as, for the first time since she’d agreed to this nonsense, Rio caught her eye. The instant their gazes locked, Agatha’s breath caught in her chest. Rio’s eyes sparkled with a hint of amusement, and that infuriatingly confident smirk stretched across her lips. The kind of smirk that was equal parts arrogant and playful.

The air between them seemed to crackle with some invisible tension, and Agatha could feel her pulse quicken. Her stomach churned as the weight of it all sank in. This was going to be a nightmare.

Rio didn’t look away, not for a second, and Agatha felt the heat rush to her face. Her mind screamed at her to look away, to focus on the meeting, but she was paralyzed. All the anger she’d been trying to tamp down flared again, this time with an undercurrent of something else she refused to acknowledge.

Rio’s eyes were still on her, the amusement clear in them. It was like she could sense the discomfort, the annoyance, and she was soaking it all in, savoring it. Agatha had half a mind to glare back, but the last thing she needed was to make this worse.

Agatha had to look away, her irritation growing by the second. The universe was laughing at her.

She definitely needed a drink now. 

Or ten.
