Right now, I’m working on chapter 21 for this one, and I’m nowhere near finished, so there’s plenty more Agatha and Rio to look forward to in the weeks ahead. As always, thank you for reading!

Chapter 12

Chapter Notes

I'm back! It took me way longer than I expected to edit this chapter. Almost 2000 words were added in the process. I couldn’t stop myself. Also, going back to work leaves me no time to write, so it’s just me, myself, and I doing it at 3 a.m. Anyway, enjoy!

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Agatha wasted no time leaving the meeting, her shoes clicking sharply against the sterile tile floor in a staccato rhythm that echoed her mounting frustration. The cold evening air hit her face as she stepped outside, sharp and biting, but it didn’t do much to calm the storm brewing inside her.

As she approached her car, her phone buzzed in her pocket. She froze for a moment, the vibration against her hip pulling her attention from her swirling thoughts. Fishing it out with one hand, she glanced at the screen, and her stomach churned.

Daniel.

His name alone was enough to sour her mood further. She hesitated, thumb hovering over the screen. A part of her wanted to let it ring out, to pretend she hadn’t seen it, but another part knew better. Ignoring him would only give him an excuse to weasel his way back into her day later. With a resigned breath, she swiped to answer.

“Daniel,” she said, her tone clipped and cold.

“Agatha,” came his reply, smooth as ever, laced with that infuriating combination of charm and smug entitlement that used to catch her off guard—but not anymore.

“I wanted to confirm,” he continued, his words slow, deliberate. “I’ll be there for Nicky’s birthday next Saturday.”

Agatha’s grip on the phone tightened. Her knuckles turned white as she fought to keep her voice level. “Fine,” she said curtly, her words measured, controlled. 

But she wasn’t done. 

“You’re staying in a hotel,” she added, her voice dropping an octave into a sharper, more dangerous tone. “And Daniel...” She let the pause stretch just long enough for him to feel the weight of what she was about to say. “You’re not bringing her. I won’t have Vanessa here.”

The silence on the other end was deafening. She could practically hear him grinding his teeth, his fragile ego bristling at her defiance.

“Agatha, that’s” he started, his voice tinged with indignation.

“No.” Her voice cut through his like a blade, sharp and unyielding. “This is about Nicky. It’s not about me, its not you, and it’s definitely not about your fucking little mistress.” She spat the last word like venom, her chest tightening as the anger bubbled to the surface.

Another pause. This one was longer, heavier, filled with the weight of things left unsaid.

“Fine,” he said finally, his voice tight and clipped. The charm was gone now, replaced with a sharp edge that hinted at his own frustration. 

“Good,” she snapped, not giving him the satisfaction of softening her tone. Without waiting for a response, she ended the call and shoved the phone back into her pocket with a force that made her hand sting.

Leaning against the car, she closed her eyes and exhaled sharply, her breath forming a visible cloud in the cold air. Her fingers were trembling, not from the chill but from the residual adrenaline coursing through her veins. She pressed her palm to her forehead, trying to massage away the pounding headache that was beginning to form.

Her anger swirled, sharp and raw, but beneath it was a familiar ache—a gnawing resentment and a weariness that came from years of dealing with Daniel’s selfishness. How dare he? How dare he try to talk to her as if everything was fine, as if he hadn’t shattered their family and walked away without looking back? And Vanessa. Just the thought of her name sent a fresh wave of bitterness coursing through her veins.

Vanessa had been the final blow, the wrecking ball to their already faltering marriage who turned into ash. And yet, Daniel still had the audacity to think he could parade her around like some prize, that she’d tolerate having that woman near her son’s birthday. Not a chance.

Agatha’s hands curled into fists at her sides, the sharp bite of her nails digging into her palms grounding her slightly. She needed to calm down, to focus, but her emotions felt like a runaway train—wild, uncontrollable. Her chest rose and fell in uneven breaths as she tried to shake off the tension.

But it wasn’t just anger. Beneath the fury was something she didn’t want to admit—hurt. Hurt that Daniel’s betrayal had left a scar she couldn’t seem to cover, no matter how much time passed. Hurt that she still had to deal with him at all, tethered together by the one good thing that had come from their marriage: Nicky.

She opened her eyes and stared out at the dark parking lot, the cold air prickling her skin. She needed to get home. Nicky would be waiting for her, and she couldn’t afford to let Daniel’s nonsense seep into her time with him. He deserved better than that.

Her phone buzzed again, jolting her out of her thoughts. She fished it out and glanced at the screen: an incoming call from the person she wanted to see the least right now.

Rio. 

Agatha’s stomach flipped, but she quickly hit the button to silence the notification. Whatever Rio wanted, it could wait. She knew they needed to talk to plan out the trauma certification but she wasn’t in the mood to deal with her enigmatic colleague or whatever drama she might be carrying along.

Sliding into the driver’s seat, Agatha gripped the wheel tightly, her knuckles still white. She let out another sharp breath and started the car. The engine roared to life, filling the silence with a low hum. She wasn’t just driving away from the parking lot; she was leaving behind the lingering weight of that phone call and the infuriating meeting, determined not to let it ruin the rest of her night.

When Agatha finally got home, the familiar creak of the front door greeted her like an old companion. The warmth of the house wrapped around her, softening the edges of her frayed nerves—though only slightly. She shrugged off her coat, letting it fall onto the nearest chair, and kicked off her shoes with a small sigh of relief. The tension from the meeting, the call with Daniel, and the lingering frustration from the day still sat heavy in her chest, but the cozy glow of the living room offered some reprieve.

Nicky was there, sitting cross-legged on the floor with his building blocks scattered in a chaotic sprawl around him. His brow was furrowed in concentration as he carefully balanced a bright red block on top of his growing tower. Agatha stopped in the doorway, watching him for a moment, her heart softening at the sight.

“Hey, buddy,” she said, stepping into the room and ruffling his messy hair as she passed.

“Hi, Mama,” he chirped back, his voice light and carefree, though his eyes never left his masterpiece. The sound of his happiness loosened something tight inside her. No matter how turbulent her day had been, Nicky’s simple presence always reminded her of what truly mattered.

She crouched down beside him, studying his construction. “What’s this? A castle?”

Nicky shook his head, a small, proud smile tugging at his lips. “No, it’s a space station.”

“A space station, huh? Looks pretty advanced.”

“It is,” he said with the kind of certainty only a child could have. “It’s for the astronauts and aliens to live together.”

“Well, I think the aliens are lucky to have you as their architect,” she said, kissing the top of his head. His giggle followed her as she straightened up and headed upstairs.

Once in her bedroom, the weight of the day came crashing back down. She pulled her phone out of her pocket, intending to set it aside and disconnect for a while, but the screen lit up with a series of missed call notifications. Her stomach twisted when she saw the name staring back at her again: Rio.

The sight of it made her pause. Four missed calls. 

Now, seeing them, her pulse quickened with an unwelcome mix of emotions she couldn’t—or wouldn’t—name. 

Not tonight. She didn’t have the energy to untangle whatever fresh complication Rio was offering. Whatever she wanted would have to wait until monday.  Swiping the notifications away with a flick of her thumb, Agatha tossed her phone onto the bed with more force than necessary. It landed with a soft thud against the comforter, and she pressed her hands to her temples, willing the day to stop spinning in her mind.

What she needed the most right now was a drink. A strong one. Something to quiet the incessant buzz of frustration and uncertainty in her head.

Without giving herself time to second-guess, she snatched up her phone again and scrolled through her contacts. When she found Mariah’s name, she hit the call button and pressed the phone to her ear.

Mariah answered on the first ring, her voice bright and teasing. “Agatha! To what do I owe the pleasure?”

“You mentioned a bar?” Agatha said, her voice still sharp around the edges. 

Mariah laughed softly. “You’re in, then?”

“I need a drink,” Agatha said bluntly, skipping any preamble. 

Mariah laughed, the sound warm and familiar. “Oh, honey, you must be psychic because I was just about to call you. A few of us are hitting that new bar downtown tonight. Perfect timing.

“I’m in,” Agatha confirmed, exhaling heavily. “Just tell me where and when.”

Mariah hesitated for a second. “Don’t worry—I’m not dragging you to some dive. We’ll have fun”

Agatha paused, her instincts kicking in. Mariah’s tone carried a familiar mischievous edge. She knew her friend well enough to catch it. “Who’s coming?” she asked cautiously.

“You’ll see when you get there,” Mariah replied, her voice lilting with amusement. “Don’t worry about it.”

Agatha’s stomach tightened at the lack of specifics, her thoughts immediately jumping to Rio,  but she shoved them aside. She almost pressed further, but she stopped herself, unwilling to give Mariah any ammunition to tease her with. The last thing she needed was for Mariah to pick up on how much she was overthinking this.

“Fine,” Agatha said finally, her voice even. “I’m in.”

“Good girl,” Mariah said, and Agatha could practically hear the grin in her voice. “Nine o’clock. I'll text you the details. Don’t be late.”

“Yeah, yeah,” Agatha muttered before hanging up.

She set the phone down and exhaled slowly, staring at the ceiling. The idea of going out didn’t exactly fill her with excitement, but staying in with her swirling thoughts felt unbearable. She needed a distraction—anything to pull her out of the rut she’d been stuck in all day.

Downstairs, Nicky was still engrossed in his space station, his blocks now forming a sprawling, colorful base. Agatha watched him for a moment before calling over, “Time to get ready for bed, buddy.”

“Aww,” Nicky groaned but didn’t argue. He began carefully dismantling his creation, mumbling about how he’d rebuild it even bigger tomorrow.

After tucking him into bed and reading a chapter from his favorite book, she kissed his forehead and lingered in the doorway, watching as his eyes fluttered shut. Her heart squeezed, a familiar ache blooming in her chest.

Quietly closing his door, Agatha pulled out her phone again and calledone of Nicky’s babysitters, quickly arranging for someone to come over for the evening. 

Tonight wasn’t about overthinking or reliving the mess Daniel had left behind. Tonight, it was about escape—even if just for a little while. Whatever tonight had in store, she wasn’t sure she was ready for it. But she’d face it anyway—with a stiff drink in hand.

Agatha stood in front of her closet, arms crossed, her lips pressed into a thin line. Rows of neatly hung clothes stared back at her, mostly neutral tones and practical cuts—her usual uniform for blending in rather than standing out. Normally, she would reach for her go-to black turtleneck and jeans, a look that said, “I’m here, but I’m not making an effort.” But tonight, something stopped her.

Maybe it was Mariah’s teasing tone on the phone, or the residual frustration still simmering in her chest from the day, but Agatha felt an urge to step out of her comfort zone. Just a little. Nothing drastic, she told herself, scanning the hangers with a more discerning eye. Her fingers hovered over a soft, tight-fitting black long-sleeve she hadn’t worn in ages. The fabric clung to her curves in a way that always made her feel simultaneously powerful and exposed.

She pulled it out and held it against her body in the mirror, tilting her head as she considered it. “Why not?” she muttered, tossing it onto the bed. Next came the question of what to pair it with. After a moment’s hesitation, she grabbed a sleek leather skirt—knee-length but fitted, with a subtle slit up the side. It wasn’t something she wore often, but tonight it felt right.

Agatha slipped into the outfit, smoothing the fabric over her hips as she turned to examine herself in the mirror. The woman staring back at her looked...different. A little bolder, a little sharper. She wasn’t sure if she liked it, but she didn’t hate it either.

Now for the finishing touches. High heels. The thought made her wince, and she almost reached for the black stilettos on the front of her closet. But then she remembered the boots.

Nat had gifted them to her for her 40th birthday, insisting they were “sexy as fuck” Agatha had laughed at the time, but the boots had remained unworn, tucked away in their pristine box, waiting for the right occasion. Tonight felt like the moment.

She smirked faintly and reached for the black leather ankle boots with sharp, sleek heels. The polished leather gleamed under the dim light as she slipped them on, the fit snug and perfect. She stood carefully, wobbling for just a second before straightening up, the extra height making her feel bold and commanding.

Her reflection gained a few inches of confidence, the boots adding a sultry edge to her look. They were bold, attention-grabbing—and exactly what she needed tonight.

For her makeup, she kept things simple but deliberate—a touch of eyeliner, a sweep of mascara, and then, for the final flourish, she reached for a bold red lipstick. The tube felt foreign in her hand, almost like a weapon. She hesitated before leaning closer to the mirror and applying it with slow precision. The color transformed her face, making her blue eyes stand out and her lips impossible to ignore.

Finally, she let her hair down, the dark waves cascading over her shoulders. She ran her fingers through it, fluffing it out just enough to give it some volume. When she stepped back to take in the full effect, she barely recognized herself.

The Agatha in the mirror looked like someone who had her shit together, someone who didn’t take nonsense from anyone. But more than that, she looked sexy. 

That realization made her pause. Sexy wasn’t something she often felt—commanding, yes, powerful, always—but sexy? That was a rarer sensation, one she hadn’t fully embraced more than a handful of times in her life.

For a moment, she stood there, staring at her reflection as if trying to reconcile this version of herself with the one she was used to. A slow, wry smile curved her lips.

Maybe I should channel her for the night, she thought dryly.

By the time she arrived at the bar, the night was in full swing. Music pulsed through the air, a low, steady beat that thrummed in her chest as she stepped inside. The place was dimly lit, with a sleek, modern aesthetic—exposed brick walls, warm golden lights, and a long, polished bar lined with stools. Groups of people clustered around high tables, their laughter and conversation blending into the music.

Agatha spotted Mariah near the back, waving enthusiastically. Her friend was surrounded by a small group of people, some familiar faces, others not. Agatha’s heart gave a nervous flutter as she scanned the group, but there was no immediate sign of Rio. 

“Look at you!” Mariah exclaimed as Agatha approached. Her eyes swept over Agatha’s outfit with open admiration. “Hot damn, Harkness. You clean up well.”

Agatha rolled her eyes, though a small smile tugged at her lips. “Don’t make it a thing.”

“Oh, it’s already a thing,” Mariah said with a grin, sliding a drink across the table. “Here. You’re going to need this.”

Agatha took the glass, the coolness grounding her as she glanced around the room. The tension in her shoulders began to ease. For now, the night felt manageable. She sipped her drink, letting the warmth spread through her chest.

It was time to let go—at least a little—and see where the night would take her.

She had barely finished her drink when she spotted her first red flag of the evening: Nurse Kale. The bright-eyed, overly chipper nurse was perched at the end of the group, her laughter rising above the din of the bar like an obnoxious birdcall. Agatha froze mid-sip, her lips hovering over the rim of her glass.

What the fuck is she doing here?

Nurse Kale noticed her at the same moment and beamed. “Dr. Harkness! Fancy seeing you here!” she chirped, waving like they were old friends.

Agatha’s stomach sank. Of all the gin joints in all the world… She forced a tight smile and gave a half-hearted wave, but there was no escape. Mariah was already pulling her toward the group, oblivious to the silent prayers Agatha was sending to every deity to intervene.

“Didn’t expect to see you out of scrubs,” Nurse Kale said brightly, her gaze sweeping over Agatha’s outfit. “And that outfit is to die for.”

“Uh, thanks,” Agatha replied, her tone as flat as her drink suddenly felt. A nurse calling her outfit “to die for” felt like some kind of cosmic joke. She shot Mariah a glare that said, Explain. Now. But Mariah only smirked, sipping her cocktail with infuriating calm.

“Agatha, do you remember Alice?” Mariah said, nudging the woman seated next to Nurse Kale. Alice, with her shock of neon-orange hair and ripped leather jacket, turned and gave Agatha a cheeky grin. “She’s Jen’s girlfriend.”

Girlfriend.

Agatha blinked, the pieces clicking into place like a too-loud puzzle. Her gaze darted from Kale—Jen, apparently—who was positively glowing, to Alice, who looked like she’d stepped out of a punk rock music video. Kale... and Alice?

She bit the inside of her cheek to keep from laughing. Of course. The bubbly pink ray of sunshine and the walking highlighter. Opposites attract, right? She glanced at Mariah, who was suddenly very interested in her drink, and thought, You planned this, didn’t you?

“So... you’re dating Nurse Kale,” Agatha said, tilting her head toward Alice. Her voice dripped with disbelief as she motioned vaguely toward Jen. “This Kale?”

Alice chuckled, clearly unfazed by Agatha’s tone, her grin as sharp as her eyeliner. “It’s just Jen outside the hospital,” she corrected, slinging an arm around Kale’s shoulders like she was claiming a prize. “And yup. She’s mine.” Her eyes sparkled mischievously. “Why? Are you jealous, Doctor Harkness?”

Agatha blinked, taken aback. Jealous? Of Kale? Seriously? She almost choked on her drink but managed to keep her expression neutral. Barely. “Hardly,” she said flatly. “Just... surprised.”

Alice’s smirk widened, and Agatha couldn’t decide what irritated her more—the smugness radiating off the happy couple or the fact that she was stuck here witnessing it.

Kale—or Jen—leaned into Alice, her eyes shining with that annoying, sickeningly sweet adoration that made Agatha want to roll her eyes hard enough to see her brain. “She’s the best, isn’t she?” Jen said, her voice dripping with pure affection.

Agatha raised an eyebrow, her drink hovering near her lips. “Sure,” she said slowly, the words dragged out like they physically pained her. “Let’s... go with that.”

Alice burst out laughing, and Jen giggled like they were sharing an inside joke Agatha wanted no part of.

She shifted her weight, the heels she’d dared to wear suddenly feeling like a terrible idea. Her patience was wearing thin. The bar was too loud, the lights too dim, and the last thing she wanted was to be stuck in this sitcom-worthy meet-cute scenario. I came for drinks and distraction, not this.

“So,” she said, clearing her throat and setting her glass down harder than she intended. “How long have you two been together?”

“Oh, just a couple of months,” Alice said, her grin growing impossibly wider. “Met Jen when I covered a shift at Mayo. Instant connection.”

Agatha side-eyed Jen, whose cheeks flushed as she nodded eagerly. “It was kind of romantic,” Jen added, twirling a strand of her hair between her fingers. “You don’t always meet people who get you, you know?”

Agatha resisted the urge to groan. “Mmhmm,” she murmured, draining her glass in one long sip. Her mind screamed for an escape route, but none presented itself. She glanced at Mariah, hoping for rescue, but Mariah’s smirk made it clear she was enjoying every second of Agatha’s discomfort.

This was going to be a long night.

Thankfully, the conversation shifted to work soon enough, and Agatha found herself reluctantly pulled in. Jen started recounting the last chaotic shift in the ER, her eyes lighting up as she talked about the series of mishaps—a misplaced bedpan, a patient who insisted on wearing his Crocs through surgery, and a near disaster involving a confused intern and a broken IV pump. Alice chimed in occasionally, clearly enjoying the behind-the-scenes gossip and laughing at all the ridiculousness of their day-to-day life in the hospital.

“By the way,” Agatha said, setting her glass down after an absurd story involving a bedpan and a very unfortunate janitor. She wiped her mouth and raised an eyebrow, her curiosity finally getting the better of her. “Where’s Wanda? I figured she’d be here, dragging me into tequila shots or something equally catastrophic.”

Jen exchanged a glance with Alice before smirking.  "Oh, Wanda?" she said, raising an eyebrow. "She’s not coming tonight. She and Vision are having a date night."

Agatha’s ears perked up. “A date night?” she repeated, leaning in slightly. “Without the kids? That’s... I mean, good for her,” she added, though the words tasted faintly bitter. There was a sharp twinge of envy that crept in, something Agatha wasn’t proud of.  A night with no kids and a partner who wasn’t a walking disaster? That sounded practically mythical.

“Yeah,” Alice said, her grin widening. “They even booked a sitter. Vision’s cooking her dinner tonight.”

“Vision? Cooking?” Agatha raised an eyebrow, her tone dripping with sarcasm. “What’s on the menu? A candlelit bowl of microchips?”

Mariah snorted into her drink, and Alice chuckled, but Jen crossed her arms with a mock-serious expression. “Don’t underestimate Vision,” she said, smirking. “He’s got serious skills in the kitchen. His quinoa salad is life-changing.”

Agatha rolled her eyes, the corner of her lips curling into a half-smile. "Quinoa salad?" she repeated, feigning horror. “What’s next—romantic readings from Better Homes and Gardens ?”

Alice elbowed Jen, laughing. “You see? This is why Wanda needs to be here. She’d be throwing back shots to drown out all this quinoa talk.”

“She would,” Agatha muttered under her breath, though she couldn't help but chuckle at the thought.   “And she’d have the entire bar doing them too.” For a moment, the memory of Wanda’s chaotic energy tugged at her, and she couldn’t help but smile. Wanda always did know how to make everything a little more... lively.

Mariah leaned in, her eyes sparkling with mischief. “You should be happy for Wanda,” she said, her voice laced with amusement.  “She’s got it all figured out—date night without the kids. Hell, she’s probably getting laid right now. Something we can all aspire to.”

Jen and Alice exchanged looks, and for a moment, Agatha felt a twinge of discomfort. It wasn’t that she wasn’t happy for Wanda—hell, part of her genuinely was—but she’d never been great at being self-aware when it came to her own life. The idea of a peaceful, uncomplicated night felt like an alien concept, and that pang of envy only seemed to grow.

Agatha shrugged, trying to push it down. “Yeah, good for her,” she said, a little too dryly. "The rest of us are over here, getting our life advice from a woman who thinks quinoa salads are a good time."

Alice laughed, the sound a bit too loud for Agatha’s liking, but it wasn’t unkind. "You’re just mad you don’t have a date night to look forward to," she teased.

Agatha’s eyes flickered over to Mariah, who was smiling knowingly.  “Oh, I’ve got plenty to look forward to,” she said, her tone airy but sharp. “Like figuring out what drink I’m on and wondering if my boots will kill me before the night is over.” She wasn’t about to reveal too much. Not tonight. Or ever if it was up to her. 

Jen, sensing the shift, chimed in with a grin. “At least the tequila shots will come later. Whether we’re celebrating or drowning our sorrows, they’ll do the job.”

Agatha let out a soft laugh, her tension easing just a little.

"If Wanda were here, we'd have the whole bar's worth of tequila in front of us by now," Mariah said, shaking her head. 

Agatha snorted, her tension easing slightly. "This night’s not terrible, but I’m starting to wonder if I need to plan my own escape," she added, glancing at her glass.

Kale grinned. “It’s not that bad, is it? You just need a few more drinks. And maybe your own date night. What are you, forty-something? Prime time, right?”

Agatha’s eyes widened slightly at the jab, but she quickly regained her composure, her lips twitching. “And you’re what? Thirty-something? Prime time for bad decisions and realizing you can’t metabolize tequila like you used to.”

The group burst into laughter, and even Agatha couldn’t help but crack a genuine smile. For now, the tension dissolved, leaving her with the faintest flicker of hope that the night wouldn’t be a total disaster. Then again, it was still early.

And she knew better than to expect things to stay calm for long.

The conversation carried on, the drinks flowing freely as the night stretched on. Agatha found herself loosening up, despite the strange tension between her and her colleagues. Jen was loudly recounting a particularly ridiculous incident involving a forgotten patient chart, while Alice and Kale laughed along. Mariah was just tipsy enough to start making her usual playful comments, and Agatha couldn't help but appreciate the diversion.

But then, just like clockwork, Rio appeared.

She strutted into the bar, late as always, her entrance somehow commanding without even trying. Agatha’s eyes locked onto her immediately, drawn in as if by some magnetic force she couldn’t shake. Rio was wearing her usual uniform of careless rebellion—well-worn Doc Martens, a black Metallica shirt so faded it looked vintage, and impossibly tight black jeans that highlighted every lean curve. Her wavy hair framed her face in an artful mess, and her smoky eye makeup had just the right amount of smudge to suggest she didn’t care, even though it was obvious she did. Everything about her screamed defiance. She was effortlessly cool, the kind of person who didn’t even need to try.

Agatha’s stomach tightened, a mix of irritation and something she didn’t care to name bubbling up inside her. How did Rio always manage to look so effortlessly... everything ? She was defiance personified, a walking declaration of “screw the world”.

She watched as Rio scanned the room with that practiced air of disinterest. For a split second, Agatha braced herself, convinced Rio’s eyes would land on hers, that there would be some acknowledgment—a nod, a smirk, something.

But Rio’s gaze flickered right past her.

Agatha froze, her breath catching in her throat. It was as if she didn’t exist. Her jaw tightened instinctively, the rejection landing harder than she expected. She felt a strange, sharp pang in her chest, something uncomfortably close to hurt. The heat of it crept up her neck, threatening to color her cheeks, and she hated how visible her emotions always seemed to be.

She couldn’t believe Rio was ignoring her so blatantly.

“Oh, what was that?” Mariah whispered, nudging Agatha sharply in the ribs. Her voice was dripping with intrigue, her eyes practically sparkling as she followed Agatha’s line of sight.

“Nothing,” Agatha muttered, her tone clipped and dismissive. She tore her eyes away from Rio, glaring at the rim of her glass instead.

“That didn’t look like nothing,” Mariah pressed, leaning in closer. Her grin was insufferable, and it made Agatha want to throw her drink at her—though, realistically, she’d just order another.

“I don’t care,” Agatha said, more forcefully this time, though even to her own ears, it sounded laughably unconvincing.

Mariah snickered, clearly delighted by the reaction.

Jen, ever the observant one, glanced between the two of them, her brow arching slightly. “Didn’t know Rio was such a sore subject,” she remarked dryly, taking a sip of her drink.

Agatha’s mouth opened to snap back, but she caught herself, unwilling to give anyone the satisfaction. She clenched her jaw instead, swallowing the retort along with the lump forming in her throat.

Her eyes betrayed her, darting back to Rio against her will. Rio was now leaning casually against the bar, her posture the perfect blend of laziness and poise. She was talking to someone—Agatha couldn’t remember their name, didn’t care to, really—but the easy way Rio tilted her head and let out a low chuckle made her stomach churn.

And yet, Rio didn’t even glance her way.

Agatha tightened her grip on her glass, the condensation slipping against her fingers. A small, ridiculous part of her wanted to storm over there and demand acknowledgment, to disrupt Rio’s infuriating indifference and remind her she existed. But she didn’t. She knew better. Any attempt to confront Rio would only backfire spectacularly. She’d end up looking desperate— weak —and she refused to give Rio the satisfaction.

Instead, she swallowed hard and turned back to Mariah and Jen, forcing her expression into something resembling indifference.

“You’re awfully quiet,” Mariah said, her voice light but probing.

“I’m just... observing,” Agatha replied, lifting her drink and taking a longer sip than necessary. The alcohol burned its way down her throat, grounding her momentarily.

In truth, she felt like she was unraveling. There was an ache beneath her skin, an irritation she couldn’t quite place. She told herself it wasn’t Rio. It couldn’t be. Sure, Rio had ignored her, but why should that matter? She wasn’t the type to care about such things.

Except, apparently, she was.

Rio’s laughter carried across the room, low and warm, and Agatha’s ears burned with the sound. She didn’t realize she was glaring until Jen raised an eyebrow at her.

“Seriously, Agatha, what’s going on?”

“Nothing,” she snapped, too quickly. Her voice had an edge now, sharper than she intended.

Mariah leaned back, clearly enjoying herself. “Oh, it’s definitely something. Did Rio do something to you? Say something?”

Agatha sighed, setting her drink down with a soft thud . “Not everything has to be about her” she said flatly, though her tone lacked its usual conviction.

Jen smirked knowingly, and Mariah shook her head with a laugh.

Agatha ignored her, reaching for her drink again. 

As if on cue, a bartender appeared with a drink in hand, placing it in front of Agatha. She blinked, momentarily startled, and glanced up. The bartender, a wiry young man with a cheeky grin, nodded toward the other side of the bar, where a man was leaning casually against the counter.

“He sent this over,” the bartender said with a wink, his tone conspiratorial. “Said he’d like to talk to you.”

Agatha stared at the drink—a deep amber cocktail garnished with a twist of lime. It looked expensive, deliberate, and completely out of place in the chaotic clutter of the bar. Her eyes flicked toward the man, who was grinning at her like he’d just pulled off some grand romantic gesture. He was tall, dressed in business-casual attire, and radiated a kind of forced confidence that immediately set her on edge.

Mariah, of course, was the first to break the silence. “Oh, this is golden,” she crowed, leaning in with a wide grin. “Agatha Harkness, you’ve still got it! Look at him—sending drinks your way like you’re a movie star or something.”

Jen’s eyes sparkled with mischief as she set her own drink down with a decisive clink. “Oh, this is happening. You’re going to talk to him, right?” she said, practically bouncing in her seat. 

Agatha rolled her eyes, groaning. “Not happening,” she muttered, her tone dry. “I’m not interested.”

“Not interested?” Jen pressed, feigning shock. “Why not? He’s good-looking, clearly interested, and gasp—a man! That’s your type, right?”

Agatha froze, her jaw tightening as she shot Jen a glare. “What’s that supposed to mean?” she snapped, her voice sharp enough to cut glass.

Mariah, sensing the sudden shift in tone, looked between them with a mixture of curiosity and amusement. “Oh, now this is getting interesting,” she said, grinning.

Jen smirked, clearly enjoying herself. “I’m just saying,” she teased, raising her hands in mock innocence. “You’re hot, and single and you’re not exactly swooning over Mr. Tall, Dark, and Handsome over there. So, maybe you’ve got a different preference? You know, maybe you’re into girls?”

Agatha’s cheeks flushed with heat, and her hand tightened around the glass. “Oh, for God’s sake” she snapped. “I’m straight. Always have been, always will be. Just because I don’t want to fawn over some random guy doesn’t mean—ugh, just drop it, alright?”

Jen raised an eyebrow, clearly unfazed by Agatha’s defensive tone. “Alright, alright,” she said, holding up her hands again. “No need to bite my head off. But seriously, Agatha, if you’re not interested in him, what’s the deal? Too busy being mysterious and brooding for a little harmless flirting?”

Mariah chimed in with a grin. “Or is it because you’re secretly holding out for someone else?”

Agatha glared at her. “Don’t start.”

Mariah smirked, unbothered. “Just saying. You’ve been in a mood all night, and now you’ve got a perfectly good drink and a guy who’s clearly into you. What’s stopping you?”

Agatha opened her mouth to retort but found her eyes drifting, almost involuntarily, toward Rio.

And there she was, standing across the room, mid-conversation with someone Agatha didn’t recognize. But her attention wasn’t on the conversation. It was on Agatha.

Rio’s gaze was smoldering, sharp and unrelenting. It pinned Agatha in place, made her heart race in a way that infuriated her. The look wasn’t friendly. It was possessive, territorial—like Rio was daring her to do something about it.

Her eyes were locked onto her with an intensity that made Agatha feel like she was being pierced with a thousand daggers. The smoldering look was sharp, uncomfortable. Rio was clearly pissed off, and it only made Agatha’s annoyance grow. Agatha’s lips pressed into a tight line, her irritation flaring. She couldn’t believe she was letting Rio get under her skin like this.

“I’ll tell you what’s stopping me,” she said suddenly, her voice light but laced with a dangerous edge. She grabbed the drink the man had sent over, feeling the chill of the glass seep into her hand. “Absolutely nothing.”

Jen gasped dramatically, clapping her hands. “Oh, here we go!”

Mariah leaned forward, her grin widening. “This is a historic moment. Someone alert the media.”

Agatha ignored them, standing abruptly. The heels of her boots clicked against the floor as she turned toward the man. The noise felt louder than it should have, punctuating the shift in the room.

Behind her, she could feel Rio’s eyes burning into the back of her neck.

Agatha didn’t look at her. She didn’t have to. She could feel the weight of that gaze, the heat of it spurring her on. 

This wasn’t about the man, not really. It was about proving a point—to Rio, to Jen, to herself.

She approached the man slowly, deliberately, her steps measured. Each click of her heels felt like a declaration, each step an answer to the unspoken challenge hanging in the air.

When she reached the man, his smile widened, a little too eager, a little too polished.

“Hey there,”  he said, his voice warm but entirely forgettable. “I wasn’t sure if you’d come over.”

Agatha smirked, leaning casually against the bar. She raised the glass he’d sent her, swirling the amber liquid inside. “Well,” she said, her tone cool and cutting, “you’ve got my attention—for now.”

Behind her, she could feel Rio’s gaze intensify, a storm brewing in silence. The satisfaction was fleeting but sharp, like the edge of a blade.

“I'm Stephen by the way,” he added.

Agatha took a long sip of her drink, eyeing him carefully. “Thanks, Stephen” she said, her tone a little colder than she intended. “But I’m not really interested in... whatever this is.”

He raised an eyebrow but smiled anyway, the rejection seemingly rolling off him with ease. “Fair enough. Just thought I’d give it a shot.”

Agatha gave him a polite smile, but the weight of Rio’s glare was becoming unbearable. It prickled at the back of her neck like static electricity, and her cheeks flushed with the sheer intensity of it.

The tension in the air was thick, almost stifling, but the longer she thought about it, the more the idea of pushing Rio’s buttons appealed to her. If Rio wanted to glare daggers, Agatha was happy to hand her the blade. Her pulse quickened, a mix of annoyance and exhilaration thrumming through her veins.

“Actually,” Agatha said, a sly smile curling at the corners of her mouth, “maybe I’ll take you up on another drink after all.”

Stephen’s eyes lit up with pleasant surprise, and a broad grin stretched across his face. “I’m glad to hear that.” He leaned in slightly, and Agatha caught a hint of his cologne—woodsy and warm, with an edge of spice. It was a far cry from the chaos of the bar, and she found it oddly grounding.

He gestured toward the bartender, signaling for another round. As the second drink was placed in front of her, he asked, “So, what’s a woman like you doing in a place like this? Something tells me you’re not here for the karaoke.”

Agatha chuckled, surprising even herself. “Oh, you’d be surprised,” she said, her tone light, teasing.

He laughed, his head tipping back slightly.

“So,” Agatha said, leaning in just a fraction, “what brings you here tonight? Looking to score points with a lonely drinker, or is this just your usual routine?”

Stephen grinned, his eyes bright with amusement. “Honestly? I came out with some coworkers, but they’re all married and boring. Saw you across the room and figured, why not? Life’s too short not to take a chance, right?”

Agatha arched an eyebrow, swirling the new drink in her hand. “A bold move. Most people would’ve settled for a smile from across the room.”

“Well,” he said, leaning closer, his voice dropping slightly, “a smile wouldn’t have done you justice.”

She laughed, a genuine sound that startled her for a moment. “Careful, Stephen. Lay it on too thick, and I might start thinking you’re a serial flirt.”

“Only on special occasions,” he replied smoothly, a playful twinkle in his eye.

For a moment, Agatha let herself relax. Stephen was easy to talk to—handsome, confident but not overly cocky, and quick with a joke. It felt... nice. The kind of nice that didn’t demand anything from her, didn’t weigh her down with complications or unresolved tensions.

“So,” he said, leaning his elbow on the bar as if settling in for a longer conversation, “what’s your story? You’ve got that look—you know, like there’s a novel’s worth of secrets hidden behind those eyes.”

Agatha raised an eyebrow. “A novelist? That’s a new one. Usually, people just go with ‘mysterious.’”

Stephen laughed again, shaking his head. “Guilty as charged. But seriously, what’s your name? Or do I have to guess?”

She hesitated for a split second, then offered a small smile. “Agatha.”

“Agatha,” he repeated, as if testing the weight of her name. “I like it. Unique, strong... suits you.”

“Is this where you start guessing my star sign?” she quipped, her smirk returning.

“Only if it’s a dealbreaker,” he shot back with a wink.

As she spoke to him, her focus shifted away from Rio and the tension she had been feeling, and for the first time in hours, Agatha found herself genuinely enjoying the conversation. They talked about everything and nothing at all—work, life and random things that came to mind. 

She even laughed—a real, unguarded laugh that felt foreign but welcome.

For the first time all day, she felt her shoulders relax, the weight of everything—Rio’s glare, her own frustrations—fading into the background. He wasn’t perfect, but he was... uncomplicated. Easy.

After a while, Stephen leaned closer, his voice almost playful. “Have you ever played pool?”

Agatha raised an eyebrow, intrigued. “Never. I’m not much for games.”

Stephen grinned, his teeth white against his tan. “I think you’d be great at it. Let me show you.”

Before Agatha could protest, he was already standing, his hand gently brushing hers as he led her toward the pool table. The contact sent a shiver up her spine, and she found herself following him, a strange thrill bubbling up. She wasn’t used to this—someone being so... forward with her. The touch of his hand on hers was electric, an unfamiliar warmth that made her feel almost flustered.

He handed her the cue stick and stood behind her, adjusting her grip on it. His fingers brushed her arm as he showed her the proper stance. “Like this,” he said, his voice quiet but warm. His hand lingered on hers for a moment too long, and Agatha could feel the heat radiating off of him, his closeness making her heart beat a little faster. She hadn’t realized how much she missed being touched by someone who wasn’t tangled in layers of complication, someone whose touch didn’t come with baggage.

"Like this?" Agatha asked, glancing up at him through her lashes, now acutely aware of his breath on her neck. She shifted slightly, feeling a mix of curiosity and discomfort—she wasn’t used to this kind of attention. It felt nice, but at the same time, it was so unexpected.

“Exactly,” Stephen said, a slight smirk on his lips. He moved even closer, his body pressed against hers as he guided her through the motions, his hand still on her arm. The closeness felt... good. She hadn’t realized how much she’d missed being close to someone in a way that didn’t feel strained or artificial.

As Stephen moved to take his shot, Agatha glanced up, half expecting to see Rio’s seething glare still fixed on her from across the room. The weight of it had been like a constant, gnawing presence at her back, but when she scanned the crowd, she realized—Rio was gone.

The tension, the sharp, biting awareness that had been gnawing at her for the past hour, evaporated. Rio was no longer watching. Agatha was free to breathe again, to let herself enjoy the moment without that oppressive awareness dragging at her every movement.

She turned her attention back to Stephen, letting herself laugh and tease him as he lined up for his shot. For the first time tonight, Agatha felt... relaxed. The game, his attention, even the easy way he made her feel as if she belonged in the moment—it all combined to make her feel something she hadn’t in a while: at ease. She didn’t need to keep her guard up anymore. For the first time that night, the world felt less sharp, more forgiving.

Agatha played for a while with Stephen, her concentration split between the game and the subtle touches that lingered just a second too long each time he helped her adjust her stance. His fingers brushed hers with an ease that felt almost calculated, like he knew exactly how to make her feel a little off balance. Every time he leaned in close to show her how to line up a shot, she could feel the heat of his presence behind her, his hand resting on her waist for a second too long, his body brushing against hers when he reached past her. She couldn’t deny that she was enjoying the attention, even though it made her feel like she was venturing into unfamiliar territory.

She found herself laughing more than she expected, teasing him about his pool skills, something light, something fun. For a moment, it seemed like nothing could spoil the night. Rio’s absence, her earlier tension, the weight of everything that had been eating at her—it all seemed to fade into the background, replaced by the easy rhythm of the conversation and the simple game before her.

But even as she let herself enjoy the moment, a small part of her wondered just how far she’d let this go. The attention, the closeness—it felt good, but was it something she could trust? Or was she just too tired to question it, just too tired to keep wondering whether she was being played, whether this was all just another distraction from what really mattered? For now, though, Agatha was content to simply let herself be in the moment.

But eventually, she excused herself, needing a moment away from the pulsing energy of the bar. The weight of the night had started to creep in, and she needed a break, even if just for a few minutes. She slipped away from the pool table and headed toward the bathroom, her heels clicking rhythmically against the floor. The steady cadence of her steps seemed to match the erratic thrum of her pulse as she walked, and when the door shut behind her, the buzz of conversation outside faded into an almost welcome silence.

She leaned against the cool tile for a second, breathing in the quiet, letting the stillness wrap around her. But before she could even collect herself, she heard it.

Heavy breathing. A soft whimper.

Her brows furrowed in confusion. What the hell? She froze, her hand hovering just inches from the lock, her mind struggling to process the sounds. They were unmistakable, but completely out of place in a bar bathroom. Agatha’s first instinct was to call out, to demand to know what was happening, but then, the voice came.

“Oh yes, right there.”

The words were low, almost a growl—raw, needy. It sent a chill down Agatha’s spine. Her body went rigid, paralyzed in shock, her breath hitching in her chest. She couldn’t move, couldn’t speak, couldn’t make sense of it. 

Her blood ran cold, the realization hitting her like a truck.

She knew that voice.
