The saleswoman approached them with a smile, a friendly, helpful look on her face. “Can I help you find anything today?”

“Yeah,” Agatha said, glancing down at Nicky. “He’ll need everything. Skates, pads, the whole setup. He’s going to be doing the full six-day program, so I’d like to get him everything he’ll need.”

The woman nodded and led them toward the back of the store, where the higher-end skates were displayed. “These are our most popular options for kids starting figure skating. For his level, I recommend something supportive and durable, since he’ll be on the ice a lot. We also have skate sharpening available, so don’t worry about that.”

Agatha nodded, trying to focus on the details as the woman guided her through the choices. Nicky, meanwhile, was in his element, trying on pairs of skates, his eyes lighting up every time he found one that felt “just right.”

After a bit of back-and-forth between sizes and colors, Agatha finally made her choices: custom-fit skates, protective gear, socks, and a practice outfit. She didn’t blink an eye as the total climbed higher and higher. It was a lot, but it didn’t matter. It wasn’t every day that Nicky found something that made him this happy, something he could really invest his energy into. She would make it work. It wasn’t as though her doctor salary didn’t afford her the ability to treat her son to the best.

They were led to the counter, where the final tally made Agatha’s stomach tighten. The number came to well over $1600. She swallowed hard, but the feeling was fleeting. She wasn’t worried about the money. She would be fine. After everything with the divorce and the stress of balancing work and motherhood, this was one area where she felt like she could give Nicky the best. The investment in his happiness was worth every cent.

Nicky, oblivious to the cost, grinned widely as the woman carefully packed everything up. “Thanks, Mama!” he said as she handed him the new skate bag, his joy spilling out in every word.

“Anything for you, kiddo,” Agatha said, squeezing his hand as they walked out of the store, the weight of the bag heavy but the feeling in her chest light. It wasn’t just the price tag that made it worth it. It was the look on Nicky’s face, his utter joy and excitement for this new adventure.

They made their way back to the car, Nicky talking nonstop about how he couldn’t wait to go back to the rink and show off his new gear. Agatha listened, smiling, but in the back of her mind, the thoughts about the cost, the time commitment, and the other things that seemed to be piling up were always there, lurking.

For now, though, she let herself enjoy the moment. Nicky was happy, and that was all that mattered. She would figure out the rest.

When Agatha got back to the house, the familiar sense of chaos and order collided in her mind. Nicky was already talking about something else—his new skates, his excitement for the next lesson, how he wanted to get better than the other kids. Agatha tried to focus on him, but a nagging thought kept poking at the back of her mind, slowly pulling her attention away from her son’s jubilant chatter.

She hadn’t checked her emails in a while, but she knew there was something waiting for her. The trauma certification. The one she had to prepare for— with Rio. The thought of it made her stomach churn, and the dread pooled in her chest like a stone. It was from Wednesday through Friday according to Lilia’s email she received yesterday. Just three days. But the time, the preparation, the possibility of working alongside Rio again—it all felt like a weight, one that threatened to suffocate her as she stood in the kitchen, half-listening to Nicky’s excitement.

She could already feel the tension from the bar creeping back into her mind, like a low hum. The night she’d spent there, the odd encounter with Stephen, the strange flirtation that had spiraled out of control. Rio’s presence in the background, her stony silence, her seething glances. The way Agatha had felt caught between two worlds, one where she was just trying to move on, and the other where Rio had found a way to worm her way back into Agatha’s head, even when she wasn’t there.

And then there was the bathroom. That moment after the bar when Agatha had felt the heated rush of confusion, guilt, and something far more dangerous stirring inside her. She could still feel the echo of that heat, how it had left her weak, how the dream had felt too real. 

She had spent most of the afternoon convincing herself not to call Rio, the weight of guilt pressing heavy on her chest. She hadn’t meant to stay and listen in the bathroom that night—at least, that’s what she told herself. But the truth was, once she’d realized Rio wasn’t alone, she’d been rooted to the spot, unable to move, unable to stop herself from hearing every muffled laugh and intimate word exchanged through the thin walls. It was invasive, shameful, and it made her stomach churn every time she thought about it. The guilt burned brighter because she knew she’d lingered longer than she should have, caught in some twisted mix of anger and self-loathing. The memory of it made her skin crawl, and the idea of speaking to Rio, knowing what she’d overheard, felt unbearable. Every interaction would be tainted now, the unspoken knowledge wedged between them like a splinter she couldn’t pull out. 

With a sharp exhale, Agatha forced herself to step away from the kitchen and into the quiet of the hallway. She could hear Nicky babbling in the background, lost in his excitement, but Agatha knew she needed to confront this. She couldn’t ignore it any longer. The certification. Rio. The looming work they had to do together. She had no choice but to face it head-on, no matter how much it made her want to shrink away and hide.

Agatha grabbed her phone, unlocking it with a trembling hand. The glow of the screen illuminated the room as she stared at the name glaring back at her: Dr. Vidal. The bold letters seemed heavier than they should have, as if the very presence of her name on the screen carried a weight Agatha wasn’t ready to bear. Every time she saw it, a strange shiver ran down her spine, something caught between unease and intrigue.

Why did everything seem more complicated when she was involved? Why couldn’t she just move past this gnawing, unresolved tension? Focus on her work, on Nicky, on anything that wasn’t this . But no. She couldn’t. Not when it felt like an invisible thread was still pulling her toward Rio, tightening whenever she tried to move away. It was maddening.

Her thumb hovered over the screen, and for a long moment, she debated with herself. Yet here she was, her finger trembling over the call button, fighting the sick knot of guilt and the stubborn refusal to admit just how deeply it had unsettled her. Against her better judgment, she tapped the call button. 

The phone rang once. Twice. Agatha’s breath hitched, her thumb hovering over the “end call” button, but before she could retreat, Rio’s voice came through, sharp and clipped.

“Dr. Harkness,” Rio said, her tone curt, devoid of warmth. “What do you need?”

Agatha swallowed hard, her carefully rehearsed words dissolving under the weight of Rio’s voice. She cleared her throat, determined to sound composed.

“I—" she began, but her voice faltered. She clenched her fist, grounding herself. “We need to talk about the trauma certification. It’s this week, and we’re running out of time to get everything sorted.”

A brief silence followed, heavy and expectant. Agatha’s grip on the phone tightened as the seconds stretched. She could almost feel Rio’s pointed scrutiny through the line, and it sent her stomach twisting.

Finally, Rio’s voice returned, quieter but still firm. “Wednesday to Friday. I’ve seen Lilia’s memo. Research, protocols, case studies—we’ll need to finalize everything. Do you have the materials ready?”

“Yes,” Agatha replied, her tone a touch defensive. “I’ve gone through them. It’s just... I don’t know. It’s been a lot lately.” She hated how raw her words sounded, like she was peeling back layers she didn’t want Rio to see. “I just need some time to get into the right headspace for this.”

Another pause. Agatha’s heart pounded in the stillness, her mind racing. Was Rio annoyed? Was she about to make some cutting remark? Or worse—dismiss her completely?

“You’re avoiding this,” Rio said, her voice cool but with an undertone of exasperation. “We need to get it done. The residents are counting on us, and so is the program.”

“I’m not avoiding it,” Agatha snapped, her frustration bubbling to the surface. She hated how defensive she sounded. “I’m just trying to figure things out. We both know this isn’t exactly... straightforward.”

“No,” Rio agreed, her tone softening slightly, though it still carried that frustratingly calm authority. “It’s not. But dragging your feet is only making it harder—for both of us.”

Agatha let out a slow breath, the tension in her chest easing just enough to speak without snapping. “I’ll be ready,” she said, her voice firm but quiet. “But we need to keep this professional. Focus on the certification, nothing else.”

Rio’s response was immediate, but her tone had shifted slightly, laced with something that sounded almost amused. “Professional? When have we not been, Dr. Harkness?”

Agatha’s lips pressed into a thin line at the faint teasing edge in Rio’s voice, but she didn’t bite. “I’m serious,” she said firmly.

“Understood,” Rio replied smoothly, though the tension between them lingered. “I’ll be in touch to finalize the schedule. See you Wednesday, Dr. Harkness.”

The line went dead, and Agatha was left staring at her phone, her mind racing. She tossed the device onto the couch and pressed her palms against her face, groaning softly into them.

Why did it always have to be like this? Every interaction with Rio felt like walking a tightrope, every word carefully measured yet always falling short of the balance she sought. The cold, detached nature of their conversation did nothing to ease the storm of emotions raging inside her. The dread, the guilt, the anger at herself for even feeling this way—about Rio, about the situation, about everything.

But even as she tried to convince herself, that familiar shiver returned, lingering like an echo she couldn’t quite shake.

She rubbed her forehead, trying to calm her breathing. The day ahead—preparing for Nicky’s birthday, working through the certification—seemed like an endless list of things to do. But the worst part was how alive Rio’s presence still felt, even through the phone. Agatha had hoped she’d gotten some distance, but it was clear that, with each interaction, that thread pulling her toward Rio only tightened.

And she hated it. 

Agatha sat back on the couch, staring blankly at the phone screen. She could still feel the tension from her call with Rio, the coldness and distance that she couldn’t shake. Her heart was racing in her chest, her mind tangled in confusion and regret. 

The phone buzzed again in her hand, startling her. It was a message from Rio.

“Looking forward to our professional rendezvous on Wednesday, Dr. Harkness. Let’s try to keep it that way, yeah?”

Agatha scoffed, feeling a mix of irritation and something else she couldn’t quite place. It was less teasing than usual, but it still carried that sharp edge, the one that made Agatha’s pulse quicken. She typed out a quick reply, trying to suppress the conflicting emotions roiling inside her.

“Sure,” she typed, hitting send before she could second-guess herself.

Seconds later, Rio’s reply came through:

“Good. I’d hate for you to unravel at the last minute.”

Agatha’s breath caught in her throat. There it was again—the teasing, but with just enough distance to make it sting. She wanted to call her out, snap back with something witty, but instead, she just stared at the screen, fighting the urge to let her emotions bubble over.

She quickly shoved her phone into her pocket, feeling a strange mix of frustration and... something else. Her mind raced, her chest tightening as the familiar guilt crept in. She knew she was overthinking everything. Rio’s words didn’t mean anything beyond what they were, just another layer of the complicated professional relationship they shared.

But still, there was something about her. 

Agatha sighed, running a hand through her hair. She needed to focus. She couldn’t let this mess with her head anymore. There was too much to do—Nicky’s birthday, the certification, everything else. She was a professional. She’d handle it. She’d keep it together.

But a part of her—despite everything—was already dreading the week ahead, especially Wednesday.

Chapter End Notes

This past year was hard, but I have so much to be grateful for. One of those things is rediscovering my passion for creating and writing, and with that, all of you. This story has been incredibly fun to write, but also challenging to put into words. There’s so much emotion, unresolved issues, and self-discovery happening with our girls, and I’m doing my best to do it justice.

On a brighter note, the next three chapters have been my favorites to write so far! I’m so excited to start editing them and for you to read them.

So... happy New Years and see I'll see you next chapter!

Chapter 15

Chapter Notes

Ok listen....this chapter ended up at fourteen thousand words while I was editing it (and I had only edited half!). It was too much, so I had to cut it in half.
On the bright side, you’re getting this sooner than I intended
Enjoy!

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Monday and Thursday blurred together in a chaotic whirlwind of surgeries, deliveries, and a constant stream of patients that never seemed to end. The 24-hour shift on Monday had been particularly draining. Agatha had barely had a chance to sit down, let alone catch her breath. She’d been running from one emergency to another, her mind constantly racing to keep up with the demands of the hospital. There was no time to think, no time to process anything. Everything was a blur of sterile rooms, beeping monitors, and the constant pressure of saving lives.

What was supposed to be an exhausting but routine shift felt like an endless marathon. Her body ached, her mind was foggy from lack of sleep, and yet, somehow, she pushed through. There was no room for weakness when people were relying on you to make split-second decisions that could change their lives. In those moments, everything outside of the hospital—everything personal—faded into the background. She didn’t have time to think about the nagging feelings that had been bubbling up inside her, or the dream she couldn’t shake. No, her focus was entirely on the task at hand. She had no choice but to keep moving.

The thought of Wanda teasing her about Friday night had crossed her mind in the midst of all the madness. Agatha had expected Wanda to make some kind of comment, to joke or ask about what had happened, but it never came. Instead, they barely saw each other, their worlds revolving around the chaos of their shifts and the patients that needed them. And when they crossed paths, it was brief. A quick exchange of pleasantries, the passing acknowledgment of another busy day ahead. It was a relief, honestly. As much as she hated being caught in that awkward space, the busy nature of her job gave her the distance she needed.

Thursday rolled around with its own challenges. Surgery after surgery, delivery after delivery. Agatha barely had time to eat. The hospital was a constant whirlwind, the sounds of the emergency room, the low hum of conversations between colleagues, the scurry of nurses moving from one room to another. She moved in a blur, performing her duties with the precision and care that had earned her respect in her field. But inside, she was numb, her mind constantly jumping from one thing to the next, unable to focus on anything beyond the immediate task.

The exhaustion was getting to her. Every night, she crawled into bed feeling like she had just run a marathon,  her body heavy and her mind foggy. Sleep came quickly, but it was never the peaceful kind. She would wake hours later, feeling like she had barely slept at all, her heart pounding, the taste of her restless dreams lingering like smoke in the air. It was a cycle that left her feeling frayed, but at least it served its purpose. It kept her mind distracted. And it kept her from thinking too much about Rio.

She hadn’t seen Rio since Friday night, and honestly, Agatha was starting to wonder if that was a good thing or a bad thing. On one hand, it was a relief. She didn’t have to deal with that gnawing feeling in the pit of her stomach every time they crossed paths. She didn’t have to face the quiet tension that seemed to hang between them. On the other hand, it made her realize just how much she missed their interactions, the way Rio challenged her, the way she pushed her buttons.

Agatha shook her head, pushing those thoughts away. There was no time for that. She had work to do. And right now, all she could focus on was the certification she and Rio were working on for the first-year residents. The endless stream of emails and messages between them about the details was all they’d really shared. No personal exchanges, no teasing, no quiet glances across the room. Just the work. Just the professional tasks that needed to be completed.

In some ways, it was easier this way. The distance between them, the strictly professional interaction—it made things simpler. Or at least, that’s what Agatha told herself every time she found her thoughts drifting toward Rio. But the truth was, it didn’t make her feel any better. She couldn’t shake the feeling that something had changed between them, even if she wasn’t quite sure what it was.

The days passed in a blur, each one more exhausting than the last. But in the back of her mind, she knew what was coming. Wednesday. The certification. The looming tension that would undoubtedly hang between her and Rio, no matter how professional they tried to keep things. She couldn’t escape it. 

For now, though, all she could do was keep her head down, focus on the work, and hope that whatever was brewing inside her—whatever was making her feel this way—would just fade away. She couldn’t afford to get distracted.

But deep down, she knew it wasn’t that simple.

Amidst the whirlwind of her own life, she barely had time to see Nicky. The long hours at the hospital left her with little energy for anything else, and her guilt gnawed at her every time she thought about it. She had made arrangements for his care, of course, with his nanny, but it didn’t feel the same. There were moments when she would catch herself scrolling through pictures on her phone, sent by the nanny, and each one hit her with a bittersweet pang. 

 

There was a picture from yesterday—Nicky in his little helmet, grinning ear to ear on the ice, clearly loving the lessons. His nanny had written in the message, "He’s getting so good at it!" The image of his wide smile made Agatha’s heart ache. She wished she could be there, watching him, cheering him on, but it felt like the universe was conspiring against her ability to be present in his life. Even though Nicky was thriving, enjoying his activities, it didn’t stop the sting of regret that she wasn’t the one to witness it firsthand. It was as if the world kept moving forward, and she was constantly running behind, just trying to keep up.

And then just like that Wednesday arrived. Agatha was dreading it, but she’d pushed her fears to the back of her mind, focusing on the task ahead. It had been a long morning already, filled with prep work and last-minute adjustments. She had opted for a purposefully sharp outfit : purple pants that hugged her legs perfectly, paired with a light blue blouse that accentuated her frame. The heels added just the right amount of confidence she needed, though she could feel the nerves beneath the surface.

As Agatha walked into the conference room that morning, her pulse quickened the moment she spotted Rio standing near the podium, her posture effortless, her presence commanding. It was the first time they’d been in the same room since that night at the bar, and the bathroom incident that Agatha couldn’t seem to scrub from her mind no matter how hard she tried. The memory was vivid. Agatha’s stomach twisted, guilt gnawing at her for staying to listen, for invading a moment she hadn’t been meant to witness.

As she walked through the conference room her heels clicked sharply against the polished floor, the sound almost too loud in the silence that surrounded her. She noticed that Rio was dressed impeccably in a deep blue suit, tailored so perfectly it looked as though it had been made just for her. The soft fabric hinted at polish and power, and the slightly undone white shirt underneath gave off an air of effortless elegance. The blue brought out a calm sharpness in her demeanor, but the faint glint in her eyes as she met Agatha’s gaze spoke of something more—challenge.

Now, as Rio turned and their eyes briefly met, Agatha felt a rush of unease.

“Nice of you to finally show up,” Rio drawled, her tone smooth and edged with a teasing lilt that only she could master. “I was starting to think you’d chickened out”

Agatha rolled her eyes, crossing her arms as she leaned slightly against the edge of the podium. Her voice was dry as she shot back, “Please, I’m not the one who thrives on theatrics, Vidal. And speaking of nerves, you might be overdressed for the occasion. Should I be worried you’re compensating for something?”

Rio smirked, clearly unbothered. Her response came quickly, the teasing edge still intact. “Oh, no. I just figured someone had to bring a little flair to this dry lecture. You’re the one who insists on delivering the tough love speech anyways. Very old school, by the way.”

Agatha straightened, brushing off the comment with a flick of her hand. “Old school works. Unlike fluff, it actually gets results. But don’t worry, I’ll make sure these residents are too busy sweating to notice your fashion parade.”

Before Rio could retort, the room began to fill with first-year residents. They were eager and wide-eyed, their nervous energy almost palpable. Agatha’s eyes narrowed slightly as she surveyed them, mentally sorting through their postures, their faces, their tells. Half of them wouldn’t make it through the year. The other half had no idea what they were in for.

Rio stepped aside, gesturing grandly toward the podium with a faint smirk. “All yours, Dr. Harkness. Break a leg. Though, knowing you, you’d probably just reset it and keep going.”

Ignoring her, Agatha ascended the podium with deliberate, steady clicks of her heels against the polished floor. The room hushed completely, and she let the silence linger, her gaze sweeping across the room with the kind of authority that made even the most confident of them shift uncomfortably in their seats.

“Good morning,” she began, her tone brisk and no-nonsense. She let the greeting hang for a moment before continuing, her voice sharper now, slicing through the air like a scalpel. “For those of you who haven’t already Googled me, and I know you have, I’m Dr. Agatha Harkness. And no, I’m not as intimidating as you’ve heard.” she paused “Im worst”

A few nervous chuckles rippled through the group, but Agatha’s raised eyebrow silenced them instantly.

“Let me make one thing clear,” she said, her voice steady and commanding. “As you've already noticed in the two months that you've been here this isn’t medical school anymore. There are no do-overs, no extra credit, and no professors to hold your hand. You’re here to learn how to save lives, and that means dealing with the messy, brutal reality of trauma. It’s not glamorous. It’s not neat. And it sure as hell isn’t forgiving. People bleed. People cry. And sometimes, people die. If you’re here looking for a comforting pat on the back, you’re in the wrong profession.”

She paused, her gaze locking on one resident who looked particularly pale. “Trauma doesn’t care if you’re tired, if you’re scared, or if you’re having a bad day. The only thing that matters is whether you can pull yourself together and do your damn job. Can you?”

Her words hung in the air, heavy and unyielding. The room was silent.

“Good,” she said, her lips curling into a faint, predatory smile. “Because if you can’t, I’ll find out. And I’ll make sure you don’t get the chance to waste anyone else’s time or life  on your mistakes.”

“Any questions?” Agatha challenged, her gaze sweeping the room like a hawk surveying its prey. Not a single hand went up. She allowed a satisfied smirk to tug at the corners of her mouth before turning toward Rio. “Your turn, Vidal.”

Rio’s grin was slow and deliberate as she stepped forward, but before she could take the podium, Agatha leaned in close, her voice low and laced with challenge. “Let’s see if you can keep their attention without scaring them to death.”

Rio arched a brow, her grin widening. “Scaring them? Oh, you’ve got that covered, Harkness. Don’t worry, I’ll soften the blow.”

Agatha snorted quietly, stepping back to lean against the wall, her arms crossed as she watched Rio with a sharp, assessing gaze.

Rio turned to the residents, her tone light and disarming, a stark contrast to Agatha’s cutting precision. “Good morning, everyone. I’m Dr. Vidal. Think of me as the good cop in this partnership.”

Rio leaned casually against the podium, her demeanor an almost alarming contrast to Agatha’s sharp-edged authority. She flashed a charming smile, one that immediately eased some of the tension in the room. “Good cop might be a bit generous,” she said. “But let’s just say I’m here to make sure Dr. Harkness doesn’t chew you up and spit you out on day one.”

A ripple of relieved chuckles spread through the room, and Rio let it hang for a moment before continuing, her voice taking on a steadier tone. “Now, just because I’m a little easier on the ears than Dr. Harkness doesn’t mean I’m any less serious about what we’re doing here. Trauma is chaos. It’s fast, unforgiving, and it demands nothing short of your absolute best every single time. If you can’t give that, it’s not just your pride on the line—it’s lives.”

Agatha rolled her eyes but didn’t interrupt, content to let Rio have her moment.

“Now,” Rio continued, her voice smooth and steady, “you’ve just been handed a reality check, and trust me, you needed it. Trauma is exactly as brutal as she says. But here’s the thing: it’s also where you’ll learn the most. Not just about medicine, but about yourselves. Who you are under pressure. What you’re capable of when it feels like the world is falling apart around you.”

Her gaze swept the room, lingering just long enough on a few residents to make them squirm. “And make no mistake, the world will feel like it’s falling apart. But you’re not alone in this. You’ve got us, and you’ve got each other. You’ll make mistakes. You’ll feel like giving up. But the ones who stick it out? They come out of this better, stronger, and ready to handle anything.”

She stepped back slightly, gesturing to Agatha with a small, knowing smile. “Now, Dr. Harkness and I might have different teaching styles—hers is a bit more… trial by fire. But we’re here for the same reason: to make sure you leave this certification as the best damn doctors you can be. And trust me, if you can survive her, you can survive anything.”

Agatha smirked faintly, pushing off the wall where she’d been leaning. She stepped forward, reclaiming the space beside Rio. “And just to be clear,” she said, her tone clipped but with a subtle edge of humor, “when Dr. Vidal says ‘survive,’ she means it literally. Because if you can’t handle this, someone else will pay the price. And I’m not in the habit of tolerating people who crack under pressure.”

The room seemed to collectively hold its breath as Agatha’s words hung in the air.

“Now,” she continued, her tone softening just slightly, “we’re not here to terrify you…well, not entirely. But we are here to push you. Hard. Because this is the job. It’s messy, it’s exhausting, and sometimes it feels impossible. But it’s also the most important thing you’ll ever do. So, if you’re ready to work, to learn, to fight through every doubt and every failure, then congratulations—you’ve come to the right place.”

Rio caught Agatha’s eye briefly, her grin turning almost conspiratorial as she addressed the room again. “You’re lucky, really. You’re getting the best of both worlds, someone to scare you straight and someone to remind you why you’re here in the first place. But don’t think for a second that I’ll go easy on you just because I’m not yelling. You’ve got a lot to prove, and we’ll be watching.”

Agatha let Rio’s words settle for a moment before straightening, her gaze sharp as ever. “The certifications start now. Break into your groups. I expect to see preliminary trauma assessments from all of you by the end of the day. If you’re not sure where to start—” She glanced at Rio, her smirk widening slightly. “Ask Dr. Vidal. She’s the nice one, after all.”

Rio shook her head, muttering under her breath.

Agatha didn’t bother hiding her satisfaction as the residents began to scramble into their assigned groups. The air buzzed with nervous energy, but also with purpose. And as she turned to head toward her workstation, she felt Rio’s gaze lingering on her.

When Rio stepped back, she turned to Agatha with a wry smile. “Think that softened the blow enough?”

Agatha shrugged, her tone dry. “We’ll see if they survive the day.”

The morning trudged on with back-to-back seminars, some led by them, others featuring invited specialists sharing their expertise. The sessions were intense and demanding, yet the real tension simmered beneath the surface. Agatha was acutely aware of Rio’s presence at every turn, like a magnetic pull she couldn’t seem to escape, even when they weren’t speaking.

By lunch, Agatha had reached her limit. She could feel her mind beginning to crack under  the weight of the day pressed down on her shoulders. She stood, brushing nonexistent crumbs off her blazer, and addressed the group with her usual calm, practiced detachment.

She turned on her heel, heading toward the door when Rio’s voice called after her, laced with teasing amusement.

“Leaving already? No lunch with the team? ”

Agatha paused but didn’t turn around, her back stiffening at the deliberate jab. “I prefer to eat in peace,” she replied coolly, her voice steady as steel. “Some of us don’t need a running commentary with every meal.”

The room tensed, some of the residents exchanging awkward glances, but Rio simply laughed, the sound light but with an edge of challenge.

“Suit yourself, Harkness. But don’t complain later if you’re left out of the fun. I hear the catering’s pretty decent,” Rio quipped, leaning back in her chair with a knowing smile.

Agatha didn’t respond. She stepped out of the conference room and let the door click shut behind her, the sound muffling the murmur of voices inside.She walked briskly down the hallway, her heels clicking loudly with each step, the tension in her chest tightening. 

It wasn’t that she didn’t want to spend time with Rio—it was more that she couldn’t handle it today. Not after everything that had happened between them, the mess that was still lingering under the surface.

She went straight to the nearest exit, ignoring the pang of guilt that followed her every step. She needed space. Just space.

The afternoon dragged on, each seminar blending into the next like a series of monotonous slides on a PowerPoint presentation, but Agatha couldn't escape the feeling that Rio was everywhere . Every opportunity was a chance for Rio to mock, tease, or simply poke at Agatha’s carefully constructed veneer.

As they moved from one session to the next, Rio would occasionally sidle up next to Agatha, her voice just low enough for only her to hear.

“So, Dr Harkness” Rio said during a particularly dry lecture on trauma resuscitation, leaning in with a fake whisper. “What’s the trick to giving the perfect speech? I mean, you had them on the edge of their seats. I’m sure they’ll all be just as thrilled for the next round of trauma nightmares.”

Agatha shot her a look, though she kept her cool. “I’m just trying to teach them what you can’t. How to scare the hell out of people without them running for the exit.”

Rio smirked, clearly amused. “Touché. But let’s be honest—your speech could’ve used more... showmanship. Maybe throw in some blood spattering, or a fake trauma dummy or two. You know, just to keep it interesting.”

Agatha let out a sigh, resisting the urge to roll her eyes but failing.

Later, when the group broke for a quick coffee break, Agatha found herself in line at the vending machine, trying to collect herself. Of course, Rio found her again, somehow managing to slip in just beside her.

“Dr Harkness, you’re looking a little tense. Too much ‘trauma’ talk for you?” Rio asked, her voice dripping with sweet venom. She leaned in slightly, lowering her voice to a mockingly sympathetic tone. “I mean, no one could be as cool as you under pressure. Right? You're the queen of ‘cool under fire.’"

Agatha raised an eyebrow. "I’m fine. But I’m sure you’re thriving in all this attention, huh?”

Rio grinned, nudging her playfully. “Thriving? Oh, sweetie, I live for this stuff. ” She gestured vaguely at the room, where the first-years were all looking at them with wide eyes. “These kids, they want to be like us. So calm. So collected. So... dispassionate. They’ll never survive in this field without a good dose of attitude. Just a heads-up.”

“I’m sure they’ll get by just fine with less attitude,” Agatha retorted, her patience waning.

At the end of the day, the conference room emptied as the session officially wrapped up at seven. For most, it meant the end of a long day, but not for Agatha. The hands-on portion of the trauma certification loomed over her—tomorrow would bring grueling practical exercises. Tonight, though, there was still work to do. Staying behind meant prepping materials, arranging surgical tools, and setting up the simulation dummies. And, of course, it meant doing all of that with Rio.

Rio was already heading back toward the conference room, her stride confident, her smirk firmly in place. She looked as though she was gearing up to turn the evening’s task into a personal challenge to test Agatha’s patience.

“Don’t think you can escape just yet,” Rio called, her voice cutting through the quiet hall. She stopped and turned, catching Agatha mid-step as she inched toward the exit. “We’ve got work to do”

Agatha stopped in her tracks, her hand stilling on the strap of her bag. She turned, fixing Rio with a cool glare. “I wasn’t planning on running away,” she said evenly, though her voice carried just enough of an edge to warn Rio not to push her further.

Rio raised a brow, her grin widening. “Good. I’d hate to think you couldn’t handle a little prep work.”

Agatha clenched her jaw, brushing past Rio and into the room without another word.

As Agatha stood outside the prep area a few minutes later, her nerves felt like taut wires ready to snap. The thought of being alone with Rio for the next few hours unsettled her. Guilt coiled tightly beneath her composed exterior, the kind that gnawed at her no matter how much she tried to push it aside.

It wasn’t just guilt. Rio had a way of getting under her skin, of prying at vulnerabilities until they were laid bare. Agatha could already imagine the barbs Rio would throw, particularly about her and Stephen. The rumors swirling that they’d hooked up had followed Agatha everywhere. She hadn’t, of course, but no one cared to believe that. And Rio wasn’t the type to let such a ripe opportunity pass by unnoticed.

The cruel irony of it all wasn’t lost on her. Rio hadn’t even been around when Agatha left the bar that night. She was otherwise... occupied. In a way that still made Agatha’s skin flush uncomfortably.  The memory of that night burned in her mind, sharper than she wanted to admit. 

Now, the idea of being alone with Rio felt like stepping into a minefield. Every glance, every word, carried the potential to unravel her carefully maintained control, and she wasn’t sure if she was ready to face the fallout. She inhaled deeply, steadying herself before finally pushing open the door.

Rio was already in the room, casually arranging the tools on a tray. Her posture was relaxed, but her eyes were sharp, flicking up to meet Agatha’s the moment she walked in. “You’re late,” Rio quipped, her voice carrying that trademark blend of amusement and challenge.

Agatha set her bag down with deliberate precision, meeting Rio’s gaze head-on. “I wasn’t planning on running away,” she said evenly, slipping off her blazer and draping it over the back of a chair. “It’s just… nice to imagine one moment of peace. You know, before the chaos resumes.” Her tone was cool, but her movements were taut, betraying the tension she carried. “Some of us take this seriously.”

Rio smirked and stepped closer, casually picking up a pair of surgical scissors and twirling them between her fingers like a baton. “Oh, I take this very seriously, Harkness. But let’s be honest, you’d rather be anywhere else right now.”

Agatha didn’t rise to the bait, focusing instead on organizing a stack of manuals. She slid a binder into place with a little too much force, the loud snap of the ring echoing in the quiet room. “Let’s just get this done,” she said sharply, pulling on her gloves.

Rio leaned against the table, watching her with an unhurried ease. “Fine by me,” she said lightly, though the gleam in her eyes told a different story.

The silence stretched as they each turned to their tasks, though it wasn’t long before Rio broke it. She glanced toward the surgical dummies laid out in neat rows, the scalpels and tools gleaming under the harsh fluorescent lights. “Okay,” Rio mused, running her fingers lightly over a pair of surgical scissors. “I think I’ll take the head this time.”

Her tone was casual, but her next words came with a teasing grin as she turned to Agatha. “What about you? You’re more of the… torso type, I assume?”

Agatha froze for a moment, the comment hitting her with an unexpected force. A flush crept up her neck, and she quickly turned her attention to a tray of tools, willing her hands to stay steady. “Let’s just focus on the prep,” she said curtly, refusing to meet Rio’s eyes.

Rio’s grin widened at Agatha’s reaction, but she didn’t press further—at least not yet. “Suit yourself,” she said breezily, but her gaze lingered, as though filing away the moment for later use.

The two of them worked in relative silence for the next few hours, the calm of their shared task punctuated only by the occasional banter. Despite the tension lingering between them, Agatha couldn’t help but grudgingly admit that Rio was damn good at what she did. Even if her ego was insufferable, her hands moved with practiced precision, her instructions sharp and efficient.

By the time they finished setting everything up, the room was nearly ready. The tools were in place, the dummies arranged, and the checklists completed. Agatha’s body ached from the day’s grind, her shoulders stiff as she straightened and glanced at the clock. It was almost ten.

“Alright,” Agatha said, stripping off her gloves and tossing them into the wastebasket with a sigh. “I’m going to try to get out of here before midnight. You know, some of us value our beauty sleep.”

Rio tilted her head, her smirk softening into something almost genuine. “Well, if you need beauty sleep, that explains a lot. All this time, I thought you were just naturally like this.”

Agatha raised an eyebrow, grabbing her blazer from the back of the chair. She slung it over her arm with deliberate ease, taking a moment to meet Rio’s gaze. “It’s cute how you think I need it,” she shot back, her tone laced with dry amusement. “But don’t worry, Vidal—if you stick around long enough, maybe I’ll share some tips. Heaven knows you could use a little polish.”

Rio laughed softly, leaning against the edge of the table. “Careful, Harkness. I might actually take you up on that.”

Agatha gave her a pointed look, a ghost of a smirk playing on her lips. “Good night” she said, turning toward the door.

As Agatha stepped into the cool night air, the tension in her chest began to ease, though only slightly. The quiet street offered a welcome reprieve, but her mind was anything but quiet. Rio’s teasing, her sharp eyes, and that maddening smirk lingered like the faintest echo of a song she couldn’t stop hearing.

It was all too much. 

And yet, somehow, not enough.

The next day, Agatha barely had time to collect herself after the chaos of yesterday. Her nerves buzzed with exhaustion and the usual sense of dread she felt when teaching something as intense as the surgical skills portion of the trauma certification. This wasn’t just a lecture; this was hands-on. This was the moment to see if the residents could cut it, and Agatha had no problem making sure they felt the weight of her expectations.

She stood at the front of the room, her heels clicking against the sterile floor as she paced. Dressed in a fitted black pencil skirt and a crisp white blouse tucked neatly at the waist, she exuded an air of sharp authority. Her hair, loose for once, framed her face in soft waves that contrasted starkly with the icy determination in her expression.

The residents stood in a line, their eyes wide and nerves palpable, like electricity in the air.

Agatha let the silence hang thick before speaking, her voice cutting through the tension like a scalpel. “Today is the day you either step up or step out,” she said, her tone commanding and uncompromising. “This isn’t a classroom. This is where you learn what you’re made of. If you can’t handle the pressure—if you can’t put everything else out of your mind and focus solely on the patient—then maybe you should consider a different line of work.”

She paused, scanning their faces. She could see the weight of her words sinking in, the nervous shuffling of feet as they braced themselves. Good. Nervousness made them sharp.

“And if I see anyone freezing up today, if I see anyone hesitate even for a second, I will personally make sure you’re off this certification. Are we clear?”

The room was silent, save for the soft rustling of papers and a muffled cough. Agatha liked it that way. Silence meant they were listening.

“Good,” she continued. “Because the only thing standing between you and an angry trauma surgeon on the other side of the operating table is your ability to act fast and without hesitation. Get ready.”

She turned toward the row of surgical dummies set up along the side of the room. Her voice remained sharp as she barked instructions. “This isn’t just theory. These are real scenarios. You’re going to be tested, not just on textbook answers but on your ability to think on your feet, to feel the patient, and, most importantly, to get your hands dirty when the situation demands it.”

Standing off to the side, Rio watched, her arms loosely crossed, an amused smirk playing on her lips. She was dressed impeccably, as usual today in a tailored black suit paired with a white shirt left just undone enough to look effortlessly polished and white sneakers. The sharp lines of the suit made her look like she belonged in a high-fashion magazine instead of a trauma skills seminar.

Agatha could feel Rio’s eyes on her as she finished her speech, and sure enough, Rio chimed in as the residents shuffled off to prepare. “You’re really giving them the full tough-love routine today, huh?” she teased, her voice light but her grin mischievous. “I don’t think you need to terrify them quite so much. I mean, they’re already scared of you as it is.”

Agatha turned slowly, her eyes narrowing, though a flicker of a smirk tugged at her lips. “You’re one to talk, Vidal. You’d probably prefer to put them through a series of pop quizzes and call it ‘character building.’”

Rio chuckled, her gaze sparkling with humor. “I don’t know. I think they’d survive the quizzes. It’s the pressure that gets them.  You’re good at making them sweat, though. Definitely your strong suit.”

Agatha rolled her eyes, brushing past Rio as she adjusted one of the dummies. “Some of us don’t believe in holding their hands,” she quipped, her tone dry. “But feel free to jump in with your charm offensive anytime. They’ll need it to recover after this.” She didn’t do soft encouragement, after all. Her philosophy was simple: if they couldn’t handle the heat, they didn’t belong in the kitchen.

Rio leaned casually against a nearby table, her grin widening. “Oh, don’t worry. I wouldn’t dream of stealing the show from you.”

Agatha turned away with a faint shake of her head, but a small, exasperated smile crept across her face despite herself. Rio might drive her insane, but she had to admit—her banter was annoyingly effective at cutting through the tension.

Refocusing, Agatha moved forward with the session. She stepped to the front of the room and began demonstrating a procedure. Her movements were sharp and efficient, the kind that came with years of experience and discipline. She didn’t bother explaining every minute detail; this was about showing, not coddling.

But Rio, predictably, couldn’t resist taking the opportunity to step in.

“Alright, everyone, watch closely,” Rio said, sliding in front of Agatha with dramatic flair, a glint of mischief in her eyes. “Let’s see how Dr. Harkness manages the elbow reduction. It’s one of the more delicate procedures, and as charming as she is, she’s certainly no stranger to handling delicate things.”

Agatha froze for a fraction of a second, willing herself to keep her composure as a faint blush threatened to rise. She forced herself to focus on the task at hand, but Rio’s words had landed squarely under her skin, as they always seemed to.

Stepping back, Agatha crossed her arms and watched, trying to ignore the heat creeping up her neck, as Rio demonstrated the reduction again. Rio placed her hands on the dummy’s elbow with the confidence of someone who knew exactly what they were doing, her voice calm and steady as she explained the process.

“You see, the trick is to apply gentle pressure, enough to realign the joint, but not so much that you cause further damage,” Rio said, her hands moving with precision. “Don’t rush, but don’t hesitate either. If you panic, it only gets worse. Confidence is key. Feel the joint. Listen to how it moves. If you don’t, well...” She paused, flashing a quick grin at the wide-eyed residents. “Let’s just say, your patient won’t be thanking you later.”

The residents nodded solemnly, their eyes glued to Rio’s movements. Agatha, meanwhile, stood off to the side, the heat in her cheeks finally subsiding. 

“Anything to add, Dr. Harkness?” Rio asked, glancing over her shoulder with an infuriatingly casual smile.

Agatha raised an eyebrow, stepping forward again. “No, I think you’ve thoroughly dazzled them with your theatrics. Now let’s see if they can actually do it themselves. Shall we?”

Rio chuckled, stepping aside as Agatha moved to address the residents. Her tone was as sharp as ever, but Rio’s teasing had done something unexpected: it had broken the tension, and the group seemed a little more at ease.

Even if Agatha wouldn’t admit it, Rio’s knack for knowing just when to push her buttons and when to back off was annoyingly effective.

The morning was already crawling toward noon, and the day’s seminars were becoming more intense. Agatha’s mind buzzed with the usual flood of medical knowledge, but Rio Vidal’s presence was impossible to ignore. Agatha was no stranger to Rio’s teasing and constant banter, but today, there was a different energy between them, an undercurrent of tension that made her nerves hum. She tried to focus, tried to bury herself in the task at hand, but Rio seemed determined to make that impossible.

Now it was time for Rio to demonstrate the reduction of a fracture, a procedure Agatha had done countless times. Still, when Rio stepped forward, something shifted in the air, and inside Agatha.

Rio shrugged off her tailored suit jacket with practiced ease, leaving her in a crisp white long-sleeve shirt. The fabric clung just right, outlining her toned frame and the subtle definition of her muscles. It wasn’t just the shirt, though, it was the way Rio moved, so effortlessly confident. Agatha’s breath hitched, but she forced her gaze back to the dummy, determined not to give Rio or her own racing thoughts the satisfaction.

“Alright, everyone,” Rio began, her voice rich with that casual confidence that always set Agatha on edge. “Let’s go over how to reduce a fracture. Precision is key. You need to apply pressure in the right places, stay controlled, and above all, don’t rush..”

Agatha’s eyes flicked to Rio despite herself, drawn to the easy grace with which she set up the mannequin. Her hands moved with an assurance that made the procedure seem deceptively simple, her fingers finding the break on the dummy’s leg with precision. Everything about Rio felt like a performance unintentional, perhaps, but utterly captivating nonetheless.

Rio caught her watching and smiled, a knowing curve of her lips that sent an unwelcome jolt through Agatha. “Pay close attention to this,” Rio said, her voice dropping just enough to feel intimate. “It’s a technique you’ll need in the field. Hands-on opportunities can be... unpredictable.” Her eyes locked with Agatha’s, and she winked.

Agatha felt her stomach tighten, heat rising to her face. She clenched her jaw and straightened her posture, refusing to let Rio rattle her further. 

Rio stepped closer to the table, her movements smooth and deliberate. She took hold of the dummy’s leg, positioning it with practiced ease. “Now, the key is controlled pressure,” she explained, her tone shifting to something more professional. Her hands moved expertly along the mannequin’s limb, fingers pressing firmly yet gently into the break. “You need to feel for the alignment. Too much force, and you’ll cause more damage. Too little, and nothing happens.”

Agatha watched as Rio adjusted the dummy’s leg, her movements precise and fluid. But she couldn’t help but notice the subtle flex of Rio’s muscles beneath her shirt, the way the fabric stretched as she worked. It was maddening—this mix of professionalism and an almost unconscious magnetism that Rio seemed to exude.

“See?” Rio said, her voice breaking through Agatha’s scattered thoughts. She pressed down on the joint with just the right amount of pressure, aligning the fracture perfectly. “Controlled, deliberate, and confident. That’s the difference between a successful reduction and a nightmare for your patient.”

The residents murmured their agreement, clearly impressed. Agatha, on the other hand, forced herself to take a calming breath. Rio was good at what she did, she couldn’t deny that, but her flair for turning a routine demonstration into an unwitting spectacle was another matter entirely.

The rest of the day passed in a blur of mockery, teasing, and surgical precision. Agatha managed to have lunch on her own again, though she couldn’t shake the sense that Rio was always just one step behind, watching her, waiting for her to slip up, and enjoying every minute of it. Agatha told herself she didn’t care, that she was used to Rio’s games, but deep down, she knew the truth. The games weren’t just continuing; they were escalating.

When it came time for Rio to demonstrate the shoulder reduction, Agatha prepared herself to observe with the same clinical detachment she always maintained. She stood at the back of the room, arms crossed, her sharp gaze fixed on the residents as they gathered around the demonstration table.

"Alright, first-years," Rio’s voice broke through the low murmur of conversation as she stepped forward. Her tailored light blue suit moved fluidly with every step, commanding attention with an ease that made Agatha’s teeth clench. "Let me show you how to handle this. The shoulder dislocation is one of the most delicate injuries you’ll encounter. It’s about precision, confidence, and most importantly connection with your patient."

Agatha shifted, maintaining her place near the edge of the group, her eyes fixed on Rio. But when Rio’s smirk started to form, her amusement unmistakable, Agatha’s shoulders tensed. Whatever was going on in this infuriating woman's head couldn't be good for her. 

Rio turned, her dark eyes glimmering with mischief. "I think this is better to demonstrate with a real person and not just a dummy. Dr. Harkness, would you mind helping me out with this one?" Her smile was too knowing and entirely infuriating.

Agatha stiffened, her mind racing. Demonstrating meant Rio would have to touch her, guide her arm, and... She didn’t know how to feel about that. She felt a shiver down her spine for sure, though she’d die before admitting it. She hesitated for a moment, but the quiet in the room made it impossible to decline without drawing even more attention.

"Fine," Agatha snapped, striding forward with a practiced air of indifference that masked the storm of emotions brewing inside her. "Let’s get on with it."

She reached Rio’s side, standing tall, though she avoided eye contact. It wasn’t until she noticed Rio’s arched eyebrow and the suppressed laughter in her gaze that Agatha realized she was still wearing her blazer.

"Are you planning to let me work through the jacket?" Rio teased, tilting her head.

Agatha flushed, her cheeks burning as she fumbled to remove the blazer. "Right," she muttered, her tone clipped. "Happy now?"

"Ecstatic," Rio said smoothly, her grin widening.

The room was silent, all eyes on the two of them, but Agatha’s mind was far from the other residents. Rio stepped closer, too close, her presence suddenly all-encompassing. When Rio gently took hold of Agatha’s arm to guide it into position, a jolt of warmth shot through her. Agatha’s breath hitched, her pulse quickening as she tried to keep her composure.

"Now," Rio began, her voice soft but firm as her hand slid up Agatha’s shoulder, “the key to a successful reduction is pressure, just the right amount. You have to feel where the joint is, let it lead you. If you’re too rough, you’ll cause damage. If you’re too soft…” She let her words trail off, her fingers lingering on Agatha’s shoulder for just a moment too long.

Agatha’s heart skipped a beat, her body betraying her in ways she found infuriating. The warmth of Rio’s touch was electric, each point of contact sending a sharp wave of awareness through her. She forced herself to focus on the procedure, but the flutter in her chest refused to subside.

Rio’s hand moved with controlled precision, her fingers brushing Agatha’s skin as she adjusted her arm. Every shift was deliberate, yet it felt intimate, like Rio was fully aware of how her touch lingered. When Rio finally applied the pressure, guiding Agatha’s shoulder “back” into place with a practiced twist, the closeness between them became overwhelming.

"You feel that?" Rio asked, her voice low and deliberate, her breath just barely brushing Agatha’s ear. "That’s the right amount of pressure. Just enough to get the joint back into place, no more, no less."

Agatha swallowed hard, nodding quickly. "I feel it," she replied, her voice more curt than she intended.

Rio’s fingers remained steady, her gaze lifting to meet Agatha’s. Her eyes held an intensity that made Agatha’s stomach twist, equal parts exhilaration and dread.

"Every patient is different," Rio continued, her tone softer now, almost intimate. "You have to listen to their body, feel what it’s telling you. If you can’t do that…" Her fingers pressed gently once more, sending a spark through Agatha. "...you’re in trouble."

The memory of Rio’s touch clung to Agatha long after Rio stepped back to address the residents. The ghost of her fingers curled around her like smoke, leaving Agatha acutely aware of how unsteady her breathing had become. She crossed her arms over her chest, desperate to regain control.

"Any questions?" Rio asked the group, her voice smooth, as though nothing unusual had transpired.

The room murmured in awe, but Agatha remained silent, unwilling to meet Rio’s gaze again. She knew Rio’s smirk would be there, infuriating and knowing.

Agatha tried to ignore the way her body was reacting to Rio’s touch, the lingering heat that had no place in this room. It wasn’t just Rio’s proximity—it was the fact that everything she did was so... deliberate. Every glance, every shift of her body, felt calculated, and it was all so damn effective to infuriate her. 

"Alright," Rio said, finally stepping back. "You get the gist. Now, who wants to give it a try first?"

Agatha’s hands were shaking slightly as she straightened up, trying to regain control of herself. She hated that she couldn’t stay unaffected, no matter how hard she tried.

As the other residents started to step forward, Agatha felt a mix of relief and frustration. She couldn’t keep letting Rio get to her like this. She couldn’t keep letting Rio’s teasing and her touch, however innocent, disrupt her focus.

But deep down, Agatha knew that was easier said than done. Because Rio Vidal, with her easy confidence and effortless charm, was impossible to ignore. And right now, Agatha was finding that more frustrating than ever.

The afternoon stretched on, a blur of demonstrations and discussions, but for Agatha, the tension from earlier lingered like an annoying echo. She kept herself at the edge of the room, observing rather than participating, her arms crossed tightly over her chest. Rio, of course, was in her element. Charming, composed, and entirely unfazed by the undercurrent of tension between them. Was there even tension between them or was it just Agatha's imagination playing tricks? She wasn't completely sure. 

Agatha busied herself with taking mental notes on the residents’ techniques, but her mind betrayed her, replaying the sensation of Rio’s touch, the way her voice had dipped into something almost too intimate. It had been professional and appropriate of course, and yet, it was all Agatha could think about.

When the day’s final session came to a close, Agatha didn’t bother sticking around to chat with the residents or exchange pleasantries with Rio. As soon as the last demonstration ended, she gathered her belongings and bolted from the room, her heels clicking sharply against the floor as she stormed down the hallway.

The fluorescent lights overhead hummed softly as she made her way to the exit, desperate for fresh air, for space to think. Just as she reached the quieter stretch of the corridor, her phone buzzed in her pocket. Agatha yanked it out, her irritation simmering just beneath the surface.

"Yes?" she snapped into the phone, not bothering to check who it was.

"Well, hello to you too," came Nat’s familiar, amused voice. "Hi, Nat. How are you, Nat? Good to hear from you, Nat." There was a pause, and Agatha could practically hear the grin in Nat’s voice. "Rough day, or is that just your usual bedside manner?"

Agatha sighed, pressing her fingers to her temple. "What do you want, Nat? I’m not in the mood for whatever this is."

"Clearly," Nat replied, her voice light but laced with teasing. "I was calling to confirm I’m coming down for Nicky’s birthday on Saturday. I already booked my flight."

Agatha’s frustration softened just slightly at the mention of her son, but her tone remained sharp. "Fine. I’ll see you then. But don’t expect me to roll out the red carpet."

Nat chuckled. "I wouldn’t dream of it. Though, judging by your tone, I’d say someone’s already gotten under your skin today. Care to share, or should I guess?"

"There’s nothing to share," Agatha snapped, walking briskly toward the exit. "Just a long day with incompetent first-years and... distractions."

"Distractions, huh?" Nat’s voice was thick with mock curiosity. Then, in a sudden outburst, she began shrieking like a madwoman, "Wait- are you seeing someone?? And you haven't told me?? You little bitch!"

Agatha froze mid-step, the image of Rio flashing unbidden in her mind. "Don’t start, Nat. I’m not."

"Oh, I’m starting," Nat replied with a laugh. "Come on, Aggie. You've got that tone. You’re flustered. It's almost cute."

"Don’t call me that disgusting name. I’m hanging up now," Agatha said, her voice tight as she resumed her brisk pace.

"Okay, okay, You’re out of the hook… for now anyways" Nat relented, still laughing softly. "I’ll see you Saturday. Try not to bite anyone’s head off before then, yeah?"

She ended the call without another word, stuffing her phone back into her pocket. She reached the hospital’s main doors and stepped outside, letting the crisp evening air wash over her. It didn’t do much to cool the heat simmering just below the surface, but at least it was quiet out here—no teasing voices, no infuriating smirks. Just her, the night, and a desperate need to sort through the chaos in her head.

Chapter End Notes
