Chapter 16

Chapter Notes

The inspiration for this chapter comes from Grey’s Anatomy 07x07. I used the clinical cases and some dialogue from the trauma certification scenes, as I don’t have enough medical knowledge to come up with this on my own lol .You should definitely check out the episode if you have time (I even left an Easter egg for my Grey’s fans, a certain someone. Nothing major, it doesn’t interfere with the plot, just something for my own amusement ). The rest of the chapter is my own creation.

With the news that came out today, I feel like many of us could use something to lift our spirits. Here’s my small contribution to brightening the day a bit. :)

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Agatha didn’t have any dreams that night. Not because her imagination was lacking, but because she didn’t sleep. 

At all. 

It was one of those nights where her brain seemed hell-bent on torturing her. Every time she closed her eyes, Rio’s stupid, smug face appeared. That infuriating smirk. Those hands.

She groaned and flipped onto her stomach, burying her face into her pillow like she could smother the memory out of existence. No luck. The ghost of Rio’s touch lingered on her arm, her shoulder, and, damn it all, even her wrist.

It was ridiculous. Infuriating. She wasn’t some lovesick teenager. She was a grown woman. A professional. A surgeon, for God’s sake! And yet, there she was, lying in bed, her heart racing over nothing.

She shifted positions for the hundredth time, punching her pillow into submission before flopping onto her back again, glaring at the ceiling as if it held the answers. Why did Rio get under her skin like this? She was just so full of herself. That was it . She had to be. No one needed to smirk that much or invade someone’s personal space with such… warmth.

Warmth? Ugh. What was wrong with her? 

She didn’t even like Rio. That much was clear. It wasn’t like she was sitting there thinking about how her eyes sparkled when she teased her or the way her voice dropped into that smooth, velvety tone. Nope. Not at all. Definitely not.

Agatha sat up abruptly, her hair sticking out in every direction, looking as frazzled as she felt. "I’m losing it,” she muttered. “I need therapy. Or a lobotomy. Something.”

She tried reasoning with herself. She was irritated, that’s all. Rio was annoying. Her smirk was annoying. Her touch was… ugh . Agatha buried her face in her hands, as if she could scrub the memory out.

Her brain tried to whisper something at the edge of her consciousness, but she shoved it aside with the force of a hurricane. Nope. No. Absolutely not. Whatever her subconscious was trying to say, whatever weird feelings were creeping up they could stay buried. She wasn’t about to sit there analyzing why Rio made her feel… anything. Because she didn’t. She felt nothing.

Her pulse quickened at the thought of Rio’s hands on her again, and she flopped back onto the mattress with a loud groan.

“Nothing,” she told herself firmly. “I feel nothing.”

Morning arrived far too quickly for Agatha, though “morning” was a generous term considering she’d spent the entire night wide awake, wrestling with her thoughts and losing spectacularly. The sun creeping through her curtains only served as a rude reminder that she had a full day ahead of her—a day that promised more time with her.

She groaned, shoving herself out of bed with all the enthusiasm of someone heading to their own execution. Today, she’d need scrubs, which she pulled on begrudgingly. The soft blue fabric felt like a cruel joke. She hated scrubs. They were baggy, unflattering, and far too comfortable for someone in her current mood. What she needed was armor, something sharp and stiff to match her attitude. Instead, she looked like the poster child for “Exhausted Resident Chic.”

Her reflection in the mirror wasn’t doing her any favors, either. Her eyes were shadowed with sleeplessness, her hair a tangled mess that she half-heartedly tamed into a bun. “Perfect,” she muttered to herself. “I look like I crawled out of a medical textbook on burnout.”

Breakfast was a granola bar she barely tasted, washed down with a bitter coffee that didn’t come close to improving her mood. The thought of the day ahead soured her stomach further. It was the last day of the trauma certification, which should’ve been a relief. But the fact that it was also the last day she’d be forced to work so closely with Rio Vidal? That left her with a strange, unsettled feeling she refused to analyze.

The certification finale promised to be grueling, a full-scale trauma simulation, complete with chaos, pressure, and the looming threat of public failure. It was the kind of thing Agatha usually thrived on, but today, she felt a simmering resentment bubbling beneath her skin. She was tired. She was irritated. And she was sick of Rio.

The woman had been a thorn in her side from day one, with her teasing, her smirks, her frustrating ability to make everything look so effortless. Agatha didn’t even know why Rio bothered her so much, only that she did. And after last night, after the memory of Rio’s touch refused to leave her alone, Agatha was in no mood to play nice.

She stalked out the door, her bag slung over one shoulder, her coffee cup clutched like a weapon. “One more day,” she muttered to herself, jaw clenched. “I just have to survive one more day.”

If she thought it hard enough, maybe she’d start to believe it.

She strode into the hospital with her usual briskness, though today her pace was more out of sheer determination not to collapse from exhaustion than any sense of purpose. The familiar hum of the hospital filled the air, but it only grated on her nerves. Her coffee cup, now empty, had done little to salvage her mood.

She turned a corner and nearly bumped into Wanda and Mariah, both looking infuriatingly well-rested and cheerful. Wanda was mid-laugh at something Mariah had said, but her smile shifted into concern the moment she saw Agatha.

“Oh, Agatha,” Wanda said, her brows knitting together. “Are you okay? You look...”

“Like hell,” Mariah finished with a grin, unapologetic as she gave Agatha a once-over. “Did you sleep in a dumpster, or is this just a new look you’re trying out?”

Agatha shot Mariah a withering glare, though she didn’t have the energy for a proper retort. “I’m fine,” she muttered, brushing past them toward the elevator.

Mariah, of course, wasn’t done. She fell into step beside Agatha, her grin widening. “I mean, don’t get me wrong, the whole ‘disheveled genius’ vibe could work for you. But the bags under your eyes? Those are doing a little too much.”

Agatha clenched her jaw, refusing to rise to the bait. “Some of us have real work to do, Mariah. Not all of us can waltz in looking like we stepped out of a skincare commercial.”

Mariah gasped theatrically, clutching her chest. “Ouch. Someone didn’t get their beauty sleep.”

“Enough,” Wanda cut in gently, though there was a hint of amusement in her tone. She turned to Agatha as the three of them waited for the elevator. “I wanted to ask about Nicky’s birthday tomorrow. Do you need help with anything?”

Agatha blinked, momentarily thrown off by the shift in topic. “Uh, yes. I mean, no. I’ve got it handled,” she said, a little more sharply than intended.

Wanda smiled patiently, unbothered by Agatha’s tone. “Okay. Let me know if you change your mind. I can bring something if you need extra snacks or decorations.”

Agatha sighed, pinching the bridge of her nose. “Thanks, Wanda, but it’s fine”

“Oh, it's the guy from the bar coming?” Mariah said, her eyebrows lifting.

Agatha shot her a warning look as the elevator doors slid open. “Don’t start,” she snapped, stepping inside.

Mariah smirked, stepping in after her. “Who, me? I wouldn’t dream of it.”

Wanda just shook her head with a small smile, following them into the elevator. “I’ll see you tomorrow, then. And try to get some rest tonight, Agatha. You’ll need your energy with all those kids running around.”

Agatha mumbled something noncommittal, leaning back against the elevator wall as it began to ascend. 

Agatha pushed open the door to the conference room, her exhaustion already fraying her patience. She expected to find the usual chaos of first-years milling about, but instead, the room was quiet, save for the infuriating presence of Rio Vidal.

Rio stood at the far end of the room, casually leaning against the table, clipboard in hand. She was dressed in red scrubs that, Agatha noted with immediate annoyance, fit her too well. The color popped against her dark complexion, her posture exuded confidence, and her hair was tied back just enough to reveal sharp cheekbones that should have been illegal.

Agatha hated it. She hated that Rio looked that good in scrubs. She hated that she even noticed.

And most of all, she hated the stupid smirk Rio wore as she looked up and caught Agatha glaring.

“Morning, Dr. Harkness,” Rio said, her voice carrying that maddeningly smooth lilt. “Sleep well?”

Agatha’s jaw tightened, and she set her bag down with more force than necessary. “Like a baby,” she deadpanned. “What’s on the agenda today?”

“Oh, you’re going to love it,” Rio replied, setting the clipboard down and straightening up. She walked toward Agatha with the kind of ease that only made her presence more grating. “We’re taking this certification outside. Field simulation. Realistic conditions.”

Agatha raised an eyebrow, trying not to look directly at Rio and her annoyingly good-looking scrubs. “Outside? It’s freezing. And it’s about to rain.”

“Exactly,” Rio said with a grin, clearly enjoying Agatha’s growing irritation. “Trauma doesn’t wait for sunny days, Harkness. Time to see how everyone handles a little adversity.”

Agatha crossed her arms, glaring. “This is a teaching hospital, not SEAL training.”

Rio shrugged, completely unfazed. “Think of it as a chance to test your limits. Or theirs,” she added, gesturing vaguely toward the door where the residents were beginning to gather.

Before Agatha could fire back, Rio leaned in slightly, her voice dropping to something almost conspiratorial. “Besides, I’m curious to see how you handle it. You’re not one to back down from a challenge, are you?”

Agatha’s cheeks burned, though she told herself it was from irritation. “I’ll handle it just fine, thank you,” she snapped, brushing past Rio toward the group of residents.

Behind her, she heard Rio chuckle softly, the sound low and infuriatingly pleasant.

As the group began to shuffle out of the conference room and toward the hospital’s outdoor training area, Agatha caught sight of the darkening sky. The clouds were heavy and gray, and the sharp smell of impending rain hung in the air. It was going to be a miserable day.

And Rio was only making it worse.

The group filed outside into the chilly, overcast air, their breath visible in the cold. Agatha hugged her arms close, wishing she’d brought a thicker coat. Rio, on the other hand, seemed impervious to the elements, standing at the head of the group clipboard in hand, looking far too energized for the circumstances.

“Listen up!” Rio’s voice cut through the chatter, immediately silencing the residents. Her tone was sharp and commanding, leaving no room for argument. “A charter plane was forced into an emergency landing and collided with a passenger bus. Mass-casualty situation. Thirty victims. Critical injuries. Your job? Stabilize them, prioritize their transport, and get them on the evac helicopter. Do I need to say it again?”

The group collectively blinked, some of the younger residents shifting nervously. Agatha crossed her arms, her irritation boiling just beneath the surface. She didn’t like the way Rio’s voice seemed to hold everyone’s attention, herself included.

Rio smirked. “No? Good. Let’s move.”

She led them toward the training area, her red scrubs vivid against the gray of the impending storm. Agatha followed, muttering under her breath as Rio opened the back of an ambulance loaded with supplies.

As they reached the designated area, the group came to a halt. Scattered across the muddy field were thirty mannequins, each grotesquely detailed to simulate trauma injuries, gaping wounds, fake blood, broken limbs twisted at impossible angles. The sight drew a collective groan from the residents.

Rio smiled, clearly enjoying herself. “Welcome to the final test of your trauma certification.”

“Great,” Agatha muttered, glaring at the macabre scene. “This is exactly how I wanted to spend my day.”

Rio ignored her, addressing the group. “You’ll work in teams of six. Each team is responsible for nine casualties. You may treat your patients using only what you can carry in your two hands from this ambulance. The evac helicopter is on its way. If your patients aren’t stable enough for transport, they don’t make it. Got it?”

The residents shuffled uneasily, their nerves visible. Agatha, however, was already bristling, her lack of sleep and Rio’s insufferable energy combining into a potent mix of frustration.

“Teams are color-coded,” Rio continued, pointing to a nearby assistant who was handing out colored tape to divide the group. “The clock starts now. Get your supplies, get to work.”

The residents hesitated for a beat too long, and Rio clapped her hands. “Move! People are dying.”

The group sprang into action, scrambling to the ambulance for supplies. Agatha reluctantly grabbed her own gear, scowling at the mud that clung to her shoes. Just as she was about to join her assigned team, Rio appeared at her side, her expression irritatingly calm.

“Excited to show off those skills, Dr. Harkness?” Rio asked, her tone teasing.

Agatha shot her a glare. “Thrilled,” she said, her voice dripping with sarcasm.

Agatha bit back the dozen scathing retorts on the tip of her tongue storming toward one of the teams to supervise. Behind her, she could hear Rio’s chuckle, low and maddeningly self-assured.

The rain started as a light drizzle, the cold drops soaking into their scrubs as the residents began to triage the dummies. Agatha focused on her assigned residents. This day was going to be miserable, and Rio was somehow both the cause and the aggravating highlight of it all.

The rain was coming down harder now, turning the training field into a muddy, chaotic mess. Residents scrambled to keep their “patients” dry, but the relentless downpour wasn’t making it easy. Agatha, standing off to the side with Rio, scowled under the hood of her raincoat.

Rio, on the other hand, looked entirely too pleased with herself. She clapped her hands once, drawing the attention of the beleaguered residents.

“Time check, people!” Rio’s voice carried over the rain. “It’s been three hours. Where’s your evac helicopter? Oh, that’s right. It’s not here yet. What’s your plan, hmm?”

One of the younger residents, clearly panicking, stammered, “We were keeping them stable—”

“Stable?” Rio cut in, her tone mockingly incredulous. “Is that what you call hypothermic mannequins lying in the mud? Because from where I’m standing, they look dead. And if they’re dead, guess what? No certification for you.”

Agatha crossed her arms, glaring at the chaos. “Do you have to enjoy terrorizing them so much?” she muttered.

Rio turned to her with a grin. “Funny coming from you Dr. Harkness. It’s education with flair.”

On the field, one resident, Smith, had improvised rain gear using a trash bag meant to keep the mannequins dry. Bishop, ever the rule-follower, looked horrified.

“Nice raincoat, Smith,” Agatha called out, striding over. “But shouldn’t you be more concerned about keeping your patient dry?”

Smith, unfazed, shrugged. “Well, they’re dummies, and I’m a person, so…”

She raised an eyebrow, clearly enjoying this. “Interesting logic. But here’s a fun fact: a dry patient is less likely to die of hypothermia or shock. Something to think about.”

Bishop immediately ripped the trash bag off Smith and used it to cover her mannequin. “There you go, little guy. No hypothermia for you.”

Smith threw up his hands. “Are you crazy? I’m soaked now!”

“That’s the point, Smith,” Rio said, smiling devilishly. “Adapt. Improvise. You think trauma doesn’t involve getting a little wet?”

Nearby, another resident groaned loudly. “We’ve lost two patients! This rain is impossible!”

Rio turned, her grin widening. “Oh, look. Green team’s casualties are stacking up. Only Blue team and Red team left in the running. Let’s see who survives.”

Agatha sighed, pinching the bridge of her nose as she watched Rio revel in the residents’ misery. The tables had turned completely—Rio was the one having fun, and Agatha was the one stewing.

“You’re enjoying this way too much,” Agatha muttered.

Rio’s smirk was unrepentant. “Come on, Harkness. Admit it. Watching them flounder is a little satisfying.”

Agatha didn’t respond, but her scowl deepened. Watching Rio lead the chaos with such flair was infuriating—and somehow distracting in ways she refused to examine too closely.

“Alright!” Rio called out, clapping her hands again. “Blue team, you’re about to lose another patient if you don’t stop bickering. Red team, let’s see if you can keep your last two alive. Clock’s ticking, people”

Agatha looked up at the stormy sky and sighed. It was going to be a long, wet day.

Agatha ripped off her gloves and tossed them into the nearest bin, her patience threadbare. The rain was relentless, soaking through every layer of clothing, and the entire ordeal had stretched far beyond what she deemed reasonable. She spotted Rio barking orders to a flustered resident and made her way over, her shoes squelching in the mud.

“I’m done,” Agatha said flatly, her tone brooking no argument. “I’m heading back to the hospital.”

Rio barely glanced at her, a smirk playing on her lips. “Oh, come on, Harkness. The day’s not over yet. You don’t want to miss the grand finale.”

Agatha tightened her jaw, gripping the edges of her rain-soaked jacket. “I’ve had enough of your ‘grand finale,’ Vidal. I’m leaving.”

Without waiting for a response, she spun on her heel, her shoes squelching in the mud as she marched toward the trauma bay doors in the distance. The rain lashed against her face, her hair clinging uncomfortably to her forehead, and her scrubs were a second skin, soaked and clinging with every step. The storm outside felt mild compared to the tempest of irritation roiling inside her.

“Hey!” Rio’s voice rang out behind her, muffled slightly by the rain. “Harkness, wait up!”

Agatha didn’t slow her pace, her irritation mounting. The last thing she wanted was Rio trailing after her. But, of course, the woman was relentless. Agatha heard the rapid footsteps splashing through the mud and resisted the urge to roll her eyes.

“Are you really running away because you’re wet?” Rio said as she caught up, her red scrubs somehow still managed to look infuriatingly good even drenched.

“Go back, Vidal,” Agatha snapped, tugging her jacket tighter around her. “I don’t need an escort.”

They were almost to the trauma bay doors when it happened. Agatha’s foot hit a particularly slick patch of mud, her boot skidding out from under her. Her arms flailed, her balance gone in an instant.

“Oh, for—”

Before she could hit the ground, Rio lunged forward, reaching out to catch her.  But the mud betrayed them both. Rio’s grip faltered, and with a startled yelp, she fell forward, landing squarely on top of Agatha with an audible thud.

For a moment the world seemed to freeze.

The rain poured down around them, but neither of them moved. Agatha lay on her back, her breath caught somewhere in her chest, utterly paralyzed by the proximity.

Rio’s weight pressed into her, warm and solid, anchoring her to the mud-soaked earth. Agatha’s pulse thundered in her ears, and she was acutely aware of every point of contact—the curve of Rio’s knee brushing her thigh, the press of Rio’s hand firm on her waist. Her own hands were trapped awkwardly between them, her palms against Rio’s chest.

And then there was Rio’s face, close enough that Agatha could count the raindrops clinging to her dark lashes, could see the faint hitch in her breath. The rain had plastered Rio’s hair to her forehead, stray strands dripping water onto Agatha’s cheek. Her scent—something clean and sharp, mixed with rain—filled the small space between them, intensifying the strange, dizzying heat building in Agatha’s chest.

“Are you—” Rio started, her voice quieter than usual, almost uncertain. The confidence that typically saturated her words was missing. She swallowed, her eyes searching Agatha’s face. “Are you okay?”

Agatha’s brain short-circuited, caught somewhere between mortification and an inexplicable awareness of how Rio’s hand had landed on her waist, her cheeks burning despite the chill of the rain. “I—yes,” she stammered, her voice a little too loud.

Rio blinked, her expression a mixture of amusement and something else—something that made Agatha’s pulse race against her will. “You’re welcome, by the way. For trying to save you.”

“You didn’t save me,” Agatha snapped, pushing at Rio’s shoulders. “You fell on me!”

Rio’s laugh was low, warm, and infuriatingly genuine. She shifted, her hand sliding slightly as she braced herself to stand. “Technically,” she said, her tone maddeningly playful, “I cushioned your fall.”

Before Agatha could shove Rio off her, a familiar voice sliced through the downpour like a blade, dripping with amusement.

“Well, isn’t this interesting.”

Agatha froze, her stomach dropping faster than her footing had earlier. Her head snapped toward the source, and there she was. Natasha standing a few feet away, a wicked grin plastered across her face and her phone held up, screen glowing.

“Oh, God no,” Agatha groaned, every ounce of blood in her body rushing to her face, her voice thick with mortification as she shoved at Rio, trying to dislodge her.“Put that fucking phone away now.”

But it was too late. Natasha’s thumb clicked, and the unmistakable sound of a picture being taken pierced the rain.

Rio, still sprawled on top of Agatha, tilted her head to look at the intruder, her smirk returning as though it had never left. “Friend of yours?”

Agatha’s response was immediate. “Get off me!” With a surprising burst of strength, she shoved Rio sideways, sending the other woman rolling into the mud with an indignant laugh.

Agatha scrambled to her feet, her dignity hanging by a thread. “What are you even doing here?” she snapped, brushing futilely at her scrubs. “You’re supposed to arrive tomorrow!”

Natasha, unbothered by the rain and the glare being sent her way, pocketed her phone with the satisfied air of someone who had just struck gold. “I was going to wait until tomorrow to make my grand entrance, but I thought, hey, why not surprise my dear Aggie?, get a sneak peek at the new glamorous life of Dr. Harkness you know” She grinned, ignoring Agatha’s groan of protest at the nickname. “Imagine my delight when I get to the hospital, and they tell me you’re out here in the mud. And then I find this,” she added, gesturing to the now-seated and mud-streaked Rio.

She turned to Rio, still lounging in the mud as though it were a chaise lounge. “Oh, relax, Aggie.” Nat clapped a hand on her shoulder, ignoring her flinch. “I came for Nicky’s birthday, remember? But if I’d known there’d be mud wrestling involved, I would’ve brought popcorn.”

Agatha fumed as she stomped toward the hospital, muttering curses under her breath, her soaked scrubs clinging uncomfortably to her. The humiliation of the fall still burned her cheeks, and she couldn’t shake the sensation of Rio’s weight pressing her into the mud. Her skin tingled where Rio’s hand had accidentally (or so she hoped) landed on her waist. It was infuriating.

Behind her, Rio climbed to her feet, shaking mud off her hands and smirking at Natasha, who was grinning like a cat that had just cornered a mouse. “I’m Rio by the way,” she said, extending a mud-streaked hand. 

Natasha took the hand without hesitation, her grin widening. “Natasha Romanoff. Nice to meet you, Rio”

“Likewise,” Rio replied, glancing slyly at Agatha, who shot them both a death glare.

Natasha gestured toward the muddy field behind them. “So, what exactly is going on here? Did you drag Aggie into some kind of outdoor wrestling match?”

“It’s trauma certification,” Rio explained with a chuckle. “Simulated mass-casualty training. Lots of mud, fake blood, and dramatic yelling. Pretty standard stuff.”

Natasha’s eyes lit up with mischief. “Sounds like fun. I’m always up for a challenge. Mind if I join?”

Agatha spun around, her jaw practically hitting the floor. “You’re not joining, Nat. You’re going back to my office with me. Better yet, we’re going home. ”

Natasha waved a dismissive hand. “Oh, come on, Aggie. You’re just mad because you fell.”

“I am not mad because I fell,” Agatha hissed, though her tone betrayed her lie. “I’m mad because you’re here causing chaos when you’re supposed to be arriving tomorrow!”

Natasha ignored her, turning back to Rio. “By the way, I’m a surgeon too. So, this is kind of my thing.”

Rio raised an impressed eyebrow. “A surgeon? Interesting. What’s your specialty?”

“Neurosurgery,” Natasha replied smoothly, clearly enjoying Agatha’s growing irritation. “This sounds like a walk in the park compared to some of the real-life mass casualties I’ve dealt with.”

Agatha threw her hands up in frustration. “You can’t just insert yourself into a certification, Natasha! That’s not how this works.”

Natasha placed a hand dramatically over her heart, feigning hurt. “You’re an awful person you know. Here I am, offering to help out your colleagues and contribute my expertise, and you just want to drag me away like a tyrant.”

Rio laughed, clearly enjoying the spectacle. “I think she’s got a point, Harkness. We could use an extra pair of hands, especially one with her credentials.”

“No, we couldn’t,” Agatha snapped, crossing her arms. “Nat, you are not staying.”

But Natasha had already turned toward Rio, her grin practically sparkling. “Lead the way, doctor. Let’s see what you’ve got for me.”

Rio smirked at Agatha one last time before gesturing toward the makeshift field hospital. “You’ll need scrubs for this,” she said, her tone lightly teasing as she gestured to her own mud-streaked outfit. “Follow me. Let’s get you geared up.”

Agatha, left fuming in the middle of the trauma bay  muttered under her breath, “Unbelievable.”

Agatha groaned, pinching the bridge of her nose as the two women walked off together, chatting like old friends. 

This was her personal hell. And it was still raining. Perfect.

The rain hammered down relentlessly, plastering everyone’s hair and scrubs to their bodies. Agatha stood a few feet away from the chaos, arms crossed, her scowl deepening with every passing second. She didn’t know what annoyed her more: the rain soaking through her clothes, or the sight of Natasha and Rio leading the trauma drill like a well-oiled machine.

“Okay, the red team’s patients have all died,” Rio called out, her voice slicing cleanly through the storm. She turned toward the blue team, her soaked red scrubs somehow still managing to make her look composed. “Only the blue team remains. Keep an eye on Smith. That’s what resourcefulness looks like.”

Natasha chimed in, her tone dripping with faux sympathy. “Oh, don’t worry. Resourcefulness isn’t contagious. You’re safe.” She smirked, brushing a stray piece of wet hair off her face.

Rio snorted, clearly amused. Agatha, watching from the sidelines, felt her stomach churn. They’re supposed to hate each other.  Natasha was her best friend. Rio was her... nemesis? Torturer? What even was Rio? Whatever the label, the woman had no business bonding with her best friend like this. And yet, here they were, completely in sync, their shared laughter adding salt to Agatha’s wounds.

Rio crouched by one of the blue team’s dummies, examining the incisions. “Good effort, Avery,” she said, her tone calm but firm. “But this incision is too wide. You lacerated the superior thyroid arteries.”

Jackson groaned, his frustration evident. “Well, I just—”

“Move on,” Rio interrupted, standing and wiping rain from her face with an air of finality.

“Damn it!” Jackson muttered under his breath as he begrudgingly complied.

“I hear it,” Bishop suddenly piped up, her eyes scanning the stormy sky. “I hear the helicopter!”

Jackson whipped around, incredulous. “You what?”

“I—I—I hear it! I hear it!” Bishop insisted, almost jumping in place.

“Oh, wake up!” Smith shot back from across the mud. “You don’t hear the helicopter because, ‘a,’ it’s imaginary, and ‘b,’ the imaginary helicopter is never coming!” He threw his arms up in exasperation. “They’re trying to break us! Teach us some B.S. lesson about how trauma isn’t fair or whatever.”

“We’re not done until they say these dummies are dead. The end!” Bishop retorted, her desperation bordering on manic. She was relentless, Agatha had to give her that.

“That’s not true!” Smith snapped. “It’s over! You’re just too stubborn to admit it.”

Agatha could hardly believe the chaos unfolding in front of her. She wanted to storm over and tell Natasha and Rio to wrap it up already. But no, Natasha was too busy reveling in her new role as co-leader. And Rio? She seemed to be thriving, her smirk firmly in place.

Her mind whispered the truth she didn’t want to face: This is your fault. Natasha didn’t even know about Rio. She hadn’t told her. She had thought it unnecessary, even petty. Now she could see how wrong she had been.

Her spiraling thoughts were interrupted by Jackson, who threw his hands up in frustration. “Screw this. I’m done,” he declared, abandoning his dummy and stomping toward the hospital.

Rio’s sharp gaze locked on him. “Avery, where are you going?”

“I’m done!” he shouted over his shoulder, not bothering to turn back.

“No?” Rio challenged, raising a brow.

“No, ma’am! ” Jackson shot back sarcastically before disappearing into the hospital.

Natasha gave an approving nod, completely unfazed by the outburst. “That was bold. Completely stupid, but bold.”

Agatha’s frustration bubbled over. She gritted her teeth, the rain masking the heat of her fury. She didn’t know how much more of this she could take.

Agatha’s hands balled into fists at her sides. She hated this. Hated how seamlessly Natasha and Rio worked together, how they communicated without hesitation, without any of the usual tension Agatha felt whenever she was near Rio. It felt like a betrayal, though Agatha couldn’t quite explain why.

She watched, her eyes narrowing, as Natasha and Rio moved around the patients, so in sync, so together —as if they’d been working as a team for years. Agatha wanted to tear her eyes away, but she couldn’t. It was like some sick punishment her mind had created. It felt like they were united against her, and the worst part was—she couldn’t do a damn thing about it.

This is ridiculous, she thought. I can’t even be mad at them. And yet, she was. She was furious.

The rain continued to pour, unrelenting, as the chaos reached its peak. Natasha stood at the edge of the scene, arms crossed, soaked to the bone but completely unfazed. Rio, equally drenched but just as composed, kept pace with Natasha’s energy, barking orders at the remaining trainees.

“Mam! You said the helicopter was gonna be here hours ago,” Bishop shouted, still performing CPR on her dummy. “And it’s not here, and I’m not complaining, but where is it?”

Rio glanced at Natasha, who shrugged theatrically. “Rain’s still bad,” Rio said, her voice steady despite the storm. “Probably got caught in a hailstorm.”

“Great,” Bishop muttered. She suddenly shot a look at Natasha fumbling with a card. “No! No! I know what that card is gonna say!” she exclaimed. “It’s gonna say he has cardiac tamponade with associated hypotension and bradycardia, but he can’t, 'cause I already did a pericardiocentesis and bolused him with I.V. fluids.”

Nat, holding the card mid-air. “She’s right. What do I do?”

“Grab his feet!” Bishop barked, spinning to Smith, who sighed but complied.

Agatha stood off to the side, her irritation mounting. She wanted to laugh at how ridiculous the scene had become, but the way Rio and Natasha managed to maintain their authority and composure grated on her nerves. They weren’t just good at this—they were too good. It made her feel like an outsider in her own disaster.

Bishop and Smith picked up their dummies and started hauling them toward the ambulance, splashing mud everywhere.

“Whoa, whoa, whoa!” Natasha called out, stepping forward to cut them off. “What do you think you’re doing?”

Bishop was undeterred. “This ambulance is in play!”

Rio raised a brow, her tone dripping with sarcasm. “Oh, it is, is it? I must’ve missed that memo.”

“It is now,” Bishop snapped, climbing into the driver’s seat. “Seven of my patients may have died today, but these two won’t!” She gripped the wheel dramatically. “And I’m gonna take them to that hospital right there!”

The trainees froze, uncertain whether she was bluffing. Rio sighed and stepped back, shaking her head. “Fine. Let’s see where this goes.”

Rio exchanged a glance with Natasha, who was clearly struggling not to burst out laughing. “This ambulance was in the accident,” Rio said, trying to maintain some semblance of order. “It doesn’t run.”

Bishop turned the key in the ignition, and the engine roared to life with a defiant growl. “Guess AAA can get here faster than your imaginary helicopter. Now move, or I’ll run you down!”

The trainees froze, their faces a mix of shock and confusion, unsure whether Bishop was bluffing.

Rio sighed, stepping back with an exasperated shake of her head. “Fine. Let’s see where this goes.”

For a split second, Agatha found herself wishing Bishop would go through with it and just nudge Rio out of her way. Nothing major, of course, just enough to take her down a peg. It was a fleeting, petty thought, but damn, it was satisfying.

The resident slammed on the gas, splashing through the mud as the ambulance sped toward the ER entrance. She leaned out of the window. “John Doe, multiple chest and extremity traumas! Still hypotensive despite two large-bore I.V.s started in the field!”

Rio and Natasha jogged behind, their exasperation barely concealed.

“Bishop, that’s enough,” Agatha finally called out, stepping forward as the trainees cheered.

The young resident was unfazed. “Call the OR and make sure there’s a room available!” she shouted, still in full character.

Smith turned to Rio. “Will you just tell her she won already? She’s never gonna stop.”

Rio sighed dramatically. “Fine. Blue team wins. Happy? Your patient lives for 40 years, has 15 grandkids, and a beach house in Malibu. Can we call it a day now?”

“Yes!” April jumped out of the ambulance, hugging Smith. “Yes, yes, yes!”

Agatha watched the scene unfold, finally allowing herself a small sigh of relief. Her personal hell was over.

Natasha walked over, her grin wide. “Well, that was fun. Who’s up for round two?”

Agatha’s jaw dropped. “You have got to be kidding me.”

Rio smirked, brushing rain-soaked hair out of her face. “Oh, come on, Harkness. You've got to admit it was fun”

Agatha groaned, her wet scrubs clinging to her as she trudged toward the hospital. She didn’t wait for them. She stormed ahead, her boots squelching against the rain-soaked ground as she made her way to the hospital’s changing rooms. The storm outside was nothing compared to the storm brewing inside her. Her personal hell was over—for now—but the fact that Natasha and Rio had somehow turned it into a bonding experience left her fuming.

She yanked open her locker, peeling off her soaked scrubs with a force that nearly tore the fabric. Mud and rain had soaked through to her skin, and the cold clung to her like a second layer. Agatha wasted no time, stepping into the shower and letting the hot water rinse away the grime.

By the time Rio and Natasha finally sauntered in, Agatha was already changed into a clean pair of hospital scrubs and her expression set in a grim scowl.

“Well, look who decided to ditch us,” Natasha said, her voice dripping with faux hurt as she tossed her drenched jacket onto a nearby bench.

Rio smirked, her damp hair falling into her eyes as she unbuttoned her soaked red scrubs. “She’s a runner, Nat. Gotta get used to it.”

Nat?? how dare she.

Agatha glared at both of them, crossing her arms tightly across her chest. “Oh, don’t even start with me. You two were having the time of your lives back there.”

“And you weren’t?” Rio teased, tossing her scrub top onto the bench. “You looked like you were having fun, Harkness. In a ‘storming off dramatically’ kind of way.”

“Fun?!” Agatha snapped, her voice rising. “You call that fun? Mud, rain, and two hours of watching the two of you get along like you’re best friends? No, thanks.”

Natasha chuckled, unzipping her jacket. “Don’t be so dramatic, Aggie. We’re not best friends.” She paused, glancing at Rio. “Yet.”

Rio grinned. “Give it time.”

Agatha let out an exasperated groan, grabbing her bag. “I’m waiting for you in my office. We’re going home as soon as you’re done.”

Natasha raised an eyebrow. “And where exactly is your office?”

Agatha’s eyes darted to Rio, who was in the middle of stripping off her muddy scrub pants. She sighed, her patience hanging by a thread. “She can show you,” she said curtly, slinging her bag over her shoulder and making her way to the door. “Try not to get lost.”

Rio leaned against the bench, watching Agatha’s retreating back with a sly grin. “She’s fun when she’s mad, isn’t she?”

Natasha chuckled as she unzipped her own boots. “Oh, you have no idea.”

Agatha, hearing their laughter echo behind her, muttered a curse under her breath and quickened her pace. Why couldn’t they just hate each other like normal people?

Agatha nearly made it to her office before Mariah intercepted her in the hallway.

“Wow,” Mariah said, stopping short. She looked Agatha up and down, her expression hovering somewhere between concern and amusement. “You look like you got run over by a truck. Twice.”

Agatha narrowed her eyes. “Thanks, Mariah. Always a pleasure.”

Mariah grinned unapologetically. “Truce?” she offered, holding up her hands in mock surrender. “How about I make it up to you with a coffee? You look like you need it.”

Agatha sighed, realizing her usual sharp retort wouldn’t get her far. “Fine. Coffee sounds good.”

A few minutes later, the two of them were sitting in Agatha’s office, steaming cups in hand. Mariah was chatting about some hospital gossip, and Agatha was just starting to relax when the door swung open with a flourish.

“Your coffee smells like dishwater,” Natasha announced as she entered, her voice dripping with mock disdain. She looked infuriatingly effortless despite the chaos of the day, her damp red hair cascading over her shoulders, and her hospital scrubs fitting far too well for Agatha’s liking.

“Finally. Took you long enough,” Agatha said, her tone sharp as her eyes flicked to Natasha.

Natasha ignored her entirely, her gaze locking on Mariah. Her lips curled into a smirk. “And who’s this?”

Mariah blinked, caught off guard by Natasha’s sudden attention. “Uh, Mariah,” she said, glancing at Agatha as though for guidance. “Mariah Hill.”

Natasha stepped forward, the smirk evolving into a warm, undeniably charming smile. “Mariah Hill. Strong name. I like it,” she said, extending her hand.

Mariah hesitated but eventually shook Natasha’s hand. “Nice to meet you.”

Agatha groaned inwardly, already bracing for disaster. “Nat, this is Mariah. Mariah, this is Nat. There. Introductions done,” she cut in briskly.

“Hey!” Natasha turned to Agatha with mock indignation. “You could at least try to make me sound interesting.”

“Fine,” Agatha said through gritted teeth. “Mariah, this is Natasha. She’s an irritating, overly dramatic surgeon who’s currently a pain in my ass”

Natasha ignored the jab, turning back to Mariah with a conspiratorial grin. “She’s always like this when she’s stressed,” she said, her tone dropping ever so slightly, smooth as silk. “But I’m sure you’ve already figured that out.”

Mariah stifled a laugh, her cheeks pinking slightly. “Oh I've gathered that”

Agatha narrowed her eyes, feeling her annoyance bubble dangerously close to the surface. “Okay, we’re done here,” she snapped, standing abruptly. “Nat, let’s go. Now.”

Natasha shot Mariah a lingering glance as she followed Agatha to the door. “It was lovely meeting you, Mariah,” she said with a wink.

As they walked down the hallway, Agatha's annoyance radiated off her in waves. “You couldn’t help yourself, could you?” she snapped, her eyes narrowing at Natasha.

“What?” Natasha asked, her tone a mix of amusement and innocence that made Agatha want to scream. “I was just being friendly.”

“Friendly,” Agatha echoed, her voice dripping with disbelief. “You were flirting. And on top of that you don’t even know if Mariah is into women.”

Natasha stopped walking, a grin spreading across her face as if Agatha had just delivered the punchline to a great joke. “Oh please” she said, shaking her head in mock pity. “Sweetheart, Mariah is about as straight as a rainbow.”

Agatha blinked, caught off guard. “What? How would you even know that?”

Natasha tilted her head, giving Agatha an incredulous look. “Oh, seriously?”

Agatha stood there, Eyebrow raised, arms crossed, waiting for an explanation.

Natasha sighed theatrically, as if explaining the obvious to a child. “Did you see the way she looked at me? It was practically a neon sign. Honestly it’s adorable how clueless you can be sometimes. You’ve been my best friend for how long? You should know how to read these things by now.”

Agatha groaned, rubbing her temples as if that might somehow make Natasha disappear. “You’re impossible. And why do you always have to flirt with everyone? It’s infuriating.”

Natasha’s smirk widened, her eyes gleaming with mischief. “Because it makes life more fun, obviously. Besides,” she added with a wink, “you’re cute when you’re mad.”

Agatha stopped dead in her tracks, her glare icy enough to freeze lava. “I’m serious, Nat! One day, your endless flirting is going to get you into trouble.”

Natasha just laughed, throwing an arm over Agatha’s shoulder as they resumed walking. “Trouble’s what keeps life interesting, Aggie. You should try it sometime.”

As they made their way through the hospital corridors, Natasha fell into step beside Agatha, her trademark smirk firmly in place. “So, about that trauma certification…” she began.

“Don’t,” Agatha warned, her tone sharp but not without humor.

“Don’t what?” Natasha asked, her voice dripping with mock innocence. “Congratulate you on your stellar performance? Or tease you about how you managed to look like a drowned cat by the end?”

Agatha groaned, glaring at her. “Both. Especially the second one.”

Natasha chuckled, her eyes twinkling. “Fine, fine. But let’s not forget. you owe me.”

Agatha raised an eyebrow, her annoyance flaring. “Owe you? For what?”

Natasha smirked, her expression far too pleased with itself. “For coming all the way here to rescue you from your post divorce hermit lifestyle. And, of course, for not abandoning you after you decided to go completely MIA.”

Agatha bristled, ready to fire back, but something about the way Natasha said it, half teasing, half serious made her pause. She sighed, her shoulders dropping. “I already said I was sorry.”

“Apology accepted!” Natasha announced brightly, spreading her arms wide. “Now, where’s my hug?”

Agatha rolled her eyes so hard it was a wonder they didn’t get stuck. “You’re unbelievable.”

“True,” Natasha agreed with a smug grin. “But I’m also right here, arms open. Come on, Aggie. You owe me.”

Despite herself, Agatha felt the corners of her mouth twitch upward. “Fine. But if anyone sees this, I’ll kill you. Slowly.”

Natasha beamed, triumphant. “Deal.”

Without giving herself time to overthink, Agatha stepped forward and let Natasha wrap her arms around her. The embrace was warm and firm, grounding her in a way she hadn’t realized she needed. For a moment, the chaos of the day faded into the background. 

In Natasha’s arms, Agatha felt her turmoil slow, her walls cracking just enough to let in the comfort of familiarity. She allowed herself to lean into it, into her best friend, into a feeling of home she hadn’t felt in forever. Nat held her tightly, and for the first time in what felt like ages, she felt herself exhale fully, as if she’d been holding her breath for months.

“If anyone sees this,” Agatha muttered against Natasha’s shoulder, “my reputation is ruined.”

Natasha laughed softly, the sound vibrating against her. “Oh, please. Let them talk. You’re hugging the hottest person in the hospital. It’ll only make you look good.”

Agatha snorted, unable to help herself. “You’re delusional.”

“Maybe,” Natasha said, leaning back just enough to grin down at her. “But I’m also your best friend. And you’re stuck with me.”

For the first time all day, Agatha felt herself relax completely. “Lucky me.”

“Exactly,” Natasha said, giving her a final squeeze before letting go. “Now, let’s go home before you start crying and ruin your reputation even more.”

“Nat!”

But Natasha was already walking off, laughing to herself, her victory cemented.

Chapter End Notes

This chapter was so fun to write, it had me giggling a lot of times.
I’ll be taking a break for a few days since I’m going back to college on Monday and need some time to adjust to my new schedule with school, work, and writing. I also need to start drafting the upcoming chapters and editing the seven I’ve already written.
I won’t slowburn them forever, we’re almost there, so bear with me!

Chapter 17

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

As they made their way to the car, Natasha, still grinning from her victorious hug, shot Agatha a sideways glance. “So, how’s the kiddo?”

Agatha pulled open the passenger door and slid inside, sighing as the warmth of the car’s interior started to thaw her rain-soaked skin. “Spending the night with his dad, he's picking him up from his figure skating lessons right now,” she muttered, shoving her wet hair back from her face.

Natasha had just buckled her seatbelt when she froze, her grin vanishing. “Wait—Daniel?”

Agatha exhaled sharply, bracing herself. “Yes, Natasha. Daniel. His other parent. Remember him?”

Natasha’s fingers tightened around the steering wheel, her usual playful energy darkening into something sharper. “Yeah, I remember him. I also remember what a shit-show he put you through.”

Agatha groaned, tilting her head back against the seat. “Not this again.”

“Yes, this again,” Natasha snapped, turning to face her fully. “You let him take him overnight? Are you serious?”

Agatha rolled her eyes, already regretting saying anything. “I didn’t let him. We have a custody agreement, and he’s his father. He has every right to spend time with him.”

Natasha scoffed, shaking her head as she turned the key in the ignition. “Sure, sure. But where was that fatherly devotion when he was too busy wrecking your life to be a decent parent?”

Agatha’s jaw tightened. “Nat.”

“I’m just saying—”

“Don’t.”

The car was filled with tense silence as Natasha pulled onto the road, her grip on the wheel still too tight. The rhythmic sound of the windshield wipers and the patter of rain against the glass did little to ease the weight pressing down on them.

Natasha's irritation didn’t seem to dissipate as she drove, her eyes fixed ahead, her lips pressed in a thin line. The longer the silence stretched, the more Agatha felt the suffocating weight of it. She couldn’t escape it, not now. Her mind was already racing with a thousand thoughts—Daniel’s return, Nicky’s excitement, and Natasha’s mounting frustration.

After a moment, Natasha exhaled through her nose, her voice quieter but no less frustrated. “I just don’t trust him, Ags.”

Agatha folded her arms over her chest, staring out at the rain-blurred city lights. “Yeah, well. Neither do I. But Nicky loves him, and it was his birthday wish. You’ll see him tomorrow and we’ll spend all weekend together.”

That admission seemed to take the fight out of Natasha—at least for now. She glanced over, eyes softer, but Agatha didn’t meet them. Instead, she stared out the window, watching the streets rush by, feeling the dull ache in her chest settle in.

The quiet between them thickened, filled only by the hum of the engine and the steady drum of the rain. Agatha's thoughts were scattered, consumed by the unsettling weight of her past with Daniel and the uneasy future that loomed ahead. The tension in the car mirrored the knot in her stomach—tight, unyielding. Natasha's palpable anger hung in the air, unspoken but clear. The storm outside seemed to match the storm inside, with no signs of easing.

As Agatha drove, her fingers still white-knuckled around the wheel, the silence between them stretched, thick and heavy. The rain continued its relentless assault against the windshield, the wipers swiping furiously as if trying to erase the tension in the car.

Agatha could feel Natasha staring at her, could sense the anger radiating off her in waves. It was only a matter of time before she exploded. She knew that look all too well—the one that preceded Natasha’s impatience giving way to something sharper, something more vocal. Agatha braced herself, knowing that Natasha wouldn’t be able to hold her tongue for much longer.

Agatha could feel Natasha staring at her, could sense the anger radiating off her in waves. It was only a matter of time before she exploded.

And then, predictably—

“You didn’t tell me that asshole was coming,” Natasha said, her voice razor-sharp.

Agatha exhaled slowly, already exhausted. “I didn’t think I had to.”

Natasha let out a sharp, humorless laugh. “Oh, you didn’t think you had to?” she repeated mockingly. “You let him—that asshole—come all the way from New York for Nicky’s birthday and didn’t think to give me a heads-up?” Her grip tightened on the steering wheel as she leaned forward slightly. “Are you kidding me, Agatha? After everything he’s put you through, you’re still playing nice?”

Agatha’s jaw clenched, but she kept her gaze fixed on the road, willing herself to stay calm. “It’s not that big a deal, Nat.”

“Not a big deal?” Natasha’s voice rose, incredulous. “Daniel is a lying, self-absorbed piece of shit who treated you like an afterthought the entire time you were together, and now you’re just letting him waltz back in? He’s playing the perfect dad for a weekend, and you’re okay with that?”

Agatha let out a breath, her hand gripping the steering wheel tighter. “He’s his father, Nat. He has a right to see him.”

“Right?” Natasha spat. “Right? That’s rich, Agatha. Where the hell was that fatherly devotion when you were practically raising Nicky on your own? When you were busting your ass at work, barely holding it together, while he was off screwing his student and telling you he was ‘finding himself’?” Natasha’s voice dripped with disgust. “Finding himself? More like finding someone to screw while you’re left to pick up the pieces.”

Agatha flinched, the old wounds reopening. Natasha had always despised Daniel, but now her fury was sharper, more personal. She could feel the anger in Natasha’s words like a physical blow.

“He wants to be in Nicky’s life,” Agatha said, trying to keep the emotion out of her voice. “And Nicky wants him there. It was his birthday wish, Nat. What was I supposed to do? Tell my son no?”

Natasha’s laugh was bitter and incredulous. “Tell him no? Damn right, you should’ve. Because he’s not some dad-of-the-year material. He’s a fucking joke. He doesn’t get to just come in and play the hero because it’s convenient for him. He never earned that right.” Natasha’s voice dropped lower, tinged with pure venom. “God, I hate him. I hate how he waltzed in like nothing happened, acting like you owe him something.”

Agatha’s eyes narrowed, her own anger flaring. “You think I don’t know that? You think I don’t hate that I had to watch Nicky’s face light up every time he sees him, knowing damn well Daniel hasn’t earned a damn thing?”

Natasha scoffed, shaking her head in disbelief. “And now he’s picking him up from figure skating?” she said, her tone almost mocking. “What’s next, huh? He’s moving to Minnesota? Suddenly he’s the perfect co-parent? Don’t make me laugh.”

Agatha’s lips curled into a bitter smile. “Oh, don’t worry. He’s not moving here. I made that very clear.”

“Of course you did,” Natasha muttered, her voice laced with sarcasm.

The silence in the car thickened once again, settling heavily between them. The rhythmic sound of the rain hitting the windshield only served to amplify the tension, and Agatha could feel the familiar weight in her chest, the ache of unresolved anger and frustration.

After a long moment, Natasha exhaled sharply, her voice quieter but still holding an edge. “I just don’t want you or Nicky to get hurt again,” she said, her concern cutting through the anger.

Agatha swallowed, her throat tight. “We won’t.”

Natasha didn’t look convinced. “I mean it, Ags. The second he fucks up—again—the second he makes Nicky cry, I swear to God I’ll make him regret ever thinking he could play the part of the dad again. I will fucking kill him.”

Agatha chuckled weakly, trying to deflect the emotion rising in her chest. “Noted, Nat. I get it.”

Natasha glanced over at her, still furious but softening a little. “You better, because if that asshole pulls any shit, I won’t let him off easy.”

Agatha’s lips twisted into a tired smile. “I know. I know you won’t.” She closed her eyes for a moment, trying to ignore the ache in her chest, the constant tug of old emotions, both anger and pain, that Daniel had left behind.

“Next time,” Natasha muttered, her grip on the steering wheel tight again, “you tell me when that bastard’s coming into town. Got it?”

Agatha nodded, her voice barely a whisper. “Fine.”

“Good.” Natasha’s voice was dark, but there was a flicker of something softer beneath it. “Because if he even thinks about hurting you or Nicky again, I will tear him apart. And I don’t care if I have to go to prison for it.”

Agatha let out a chuckle, closing her eyes for a moment. “Noted.”

“Good,” Natasha muttered, gripping the wheel tighter. “Because if he pulls any shit, I will kill him.”

Agatha let out a tired chuckle, closing her eyes for a moment. “Noted.”

Agatha let out a tired laugh, the sound carrying both weariness and a sense of resignation.

As soon as they pulled into Agatha’s driveway, Natasha was already unbuckling her seatbelt before the car had fully stopped. The rain had finally started to let up, but the wind was still howling through the trees, rattling the windows of the house as they stepped onto the porch.

The second Agatha unlocked the door, Natasha strolled in like she owned the place. “Ah, home sweet home,” she announced dramatically, kicking off her shoes and flopping onto the couch like a cat that had just discovered a new sunspot.

Agatha arched an eyebrow, watching her with a mixture of amusement and annoyance. “You do realize you don’t live here, right?”

Natasha stretched out, her arms behind her head, looking up at the ceiling like she’d never noticed it before. “You say that, but I don’t believe you.” She patted the cushion beside her. “Come on, Harkness. Join me in the land of comfort.”

Agatha snorted, shaking her head as she peeled off her damp jacket and tossed it over a chair. Natasha was so comfortable it was actually annoying—like a cat that had just waltzed into a new house and immediately claimed it as her own.

“First time seeing the place, Nat?” Agatha asked dryly.

Natasha hummed, pretending to take in the room with exaggerated admiration. “I’m really seeing it for the first time,” she said, her voice full of faux wonder. She paused dramatically, then turned to Agatha, dead serious. “When did you get that?” She pointed at a framed painting on the wall.

Agatha narrowed her eyes. “You got that for me.”

“Did I?” Natasha gasped, placing a hand over her heart like she was shocked to remember. “Wow. Incredible taste. No wonder you’re so insufferable with your high standards.”

Agatha groaned, pinching the bridge of her nose. “God, you are so exhausting.”

Natasha grinned, unbothered, as she sprawled even further across the couch, now taking up an entire section. “You love me.”

Agatha made a vague, noncommittal noise as she headed toward the kitchen. She’d grown used to Natasha's chaotic brand of comfort—because, somehow, it made her feel at home too. But at this moment, she was just trying to ignore the fact that her friend had already claimed her space.

Natasha followed closely behind, moving with the enthusiasm of someone who had never met a boundary they didn't want to cross. “So,” Natasha said, hopping onto the counter like a teenager who had no concept of personal space. “What are we doing tonight? We have a kid-free night, and as much as I love Nicky, I refuse to waste it.”

Agatha opened the fridge, rummaging around for something to drink, pretending she didn’t hear the not-so-subtle hint. She grabbed a bottle of water and twisted the cap off. “I don’t know, Nat. I was thinking of just—” She hesitated for a fraction of a second before continuing, “—crashing early. I barely got any sleep last night. My shift ran long at the hospital.”

It was a lie. A bold-faced, shameless lie.

She hadn’t slept last night, but not because of work. No, she’d spent the night thinking—about other things. Thoughts she didn’t want to acknowledge. Memories she definitely didn’t want to linger on. But there was no way in hell she was telling Natasha that.

Natasha’s eyes immediately narrowed, her gaze sharp and calculating. “Bullshit.”

Agatha winced but didn’t dare look at her, knowing Natasha would see right through the half-hearted attempt.

Agatha stiffened. “What?”

“Bullshit” Natasha repeated, crossing her arms. “You might be able to lie to other people, but not to me.”

Agatha huffed, turning away to grab a water bottle. “Believe what you want.”

“Oh, I will .” she said slowly  “And I believe you’re hiding something .”

Agatha swatted her hand away. “I’m just tired Nat”



“Oh, come on,” Natasha said, hopping off the counter and getting into Agatha’s personal space, a look of suspicion painted on her face. “You think I didn’t notice the haunted look in your eyes when we were driving here? You’ve got that ‘I’m-not-talking-about-it’ vibe, Harkness. Spill.”

Agatha glanced at the ceiling, as though the very paint might have a solution for her. “Really, Nat, it’s nothing. Just… stuff.”

“Stuff?” Natasha raised an eyebrow, her voice dripping with sarcasm. “You’re not a damn robot, Agatha. ‘Stuff’ doesn’t keep you up all night unless it’s something big. What, did you remember you accidentally killed your pet hamster in sixth grade? Did you break the only mirror that’s ever agreed with you and now you can’t live with yourself?”

Agatha shot her an incredulous look. “That’s… incredibly specific. And no, I didn’t kill any hamsters.”

“Alright, well, just tell me the real story then,” Natasha said, crossing her arms. “Because, honestly, if you say ‘stuff’ one more time, I might just have to pull up a chair and interrogate you in the most dramatic way possible.”

Agatha rolled her eyes, but the corners of her lips quirked. “You are so ridiculous.”

“You love it.” Natasha winked.

Agatha sighed, leaning against the counter, her posture exhausted but amused. “Fine, I’ll tell you. But only if you promise not to stage some dramatic intervention.”

“I make no promises.” Natasha grinned.

Agatha’s gaze shifted downward, unable to fully meet Natasha’s. “I’ve just been thinking… about a lot of things. Things I can’t really talk about right now. But that’s why I’m crashing early. I don’t want to think anymore.”

Natasha softened a little, noticing the change in Agatha’s demeanor. “You sure you don’t need something a little stronger than water for that?”

Agatha shook her head, managing a weak smile. “Yeah. But I’m good. I’ll figure it out.”

Natasha stared at her for a moment, then nodded as if she accepted the answer, even if it didn’t fully satisfy her. “Alright, alright. But next time, don’t lie to me, Harkness. I’m getting good at spotting that bullshit.”

Agatha chuckled lightly. “Noted, detective.”

Natasha gave her a long, scrutinizing look, then sighed dramatically. “Fine. You win.”

Agatha blinked. “Wait, what?”

“You heard me,” Natasha said, throwing her hands up. “I’m allowing you to win this round. But only because you look like you’re about ten seconds away from face-planting onto the floor.”

Agatha rolled her eyes. “Gee, thanks.”

Natasha pointed toward the hallway. “Go. Sleep. Doctor’s orders.”

Agatha scoffed. “You're incredible”

“I'm a doctor,” Natasha countered. “and I know things.”

Agatha sighed, rubbing her temples. “and I hate you.”

Natasha grinned. “I know. Now go sleep before I carry you to bed myself.”

Agatha opened her mouth to argue, but Natasha just raised an eyebrow, daring her to push her luck.

Agatha groaned. “Fine. But if you steal my blankets, I will smother you in your sleep.”

Natasha smirked. “Noted.”

As Agatha finally trudged toward her bedroom, she heard Natasha calling after her—

“Sweet dreams, Aggie!”

Agatha muttered a string of curses under her breath, but even as she flopped onto her bed, she couldn’t help but feel the ghost of a smile tugging at her lips.

Agatha groaned as she stirred, her body heavy with sleep. She blinked blearily at the ceiling, disoriented. What time was it?

She reached for her phone on the nightstand. Nothing. Frowning, she patted around the sheets, coming up empty. Great. Probably lost it in the mess of blankets.

With another groan, she sat up, rubbing the sleep from her eyes. That’s when she noticed it—her closet light was on.

She frowned. Had she left that on? She didn’t remember. But she was still in her ugly, damp hospital scrubs, which meant she had passed out the second she hit the bed.

Dragging herself up, she shuffled toward the closet, grumbling under her breath. “If this is another one of Natasha’s pranks, I swear to—”

She stepped inside—and immediately wished she hadn’t.

Natasha was standing there, casually rummaging through her things. But that wasn’t the problem.

The problem was that Natasha was basically naked.

She was wearing a transparent red dress—if it could even be called that. The sheer fabric clung to her, exposing everything, and Agatha’s brain short-circuited as she took in the fact that Natasha’s only attempt at modesty consisted of a thong and the transparent red fabric of what couldn't be called a dress.

Agatha gawked. “Natasha. What the fuck.”

Natasha turned around at the sound of her voice, completely unbothered. And, unfortunately, the front wasn’t any better. The dress was completely transparent as the back and she was wearing tiny star-shaped nipple covers.

“Jesus Christ, put something on!” Agatha yelped, throwing a hand over her eyes.

Natasha rolled her eyes, clearly amused by Agatha’s reaction. “Relax, prude. It’s just a dress.”

“That is not a dress,” Agatha spluttered, her voice rising in disbelief. “That is a war crime.”

Natasha smirked, striking a pose with exaggerated flair, completely oblivious to Agatha's shock. “You like?”

“No! I mean—” Agatha made a strangled noise, turning around so she wasn’t facing her directly. She planted a hand on her forehead as if that would somehow shield her from the sight. “Why are you even wearing that in my closet?!”

Natasha sighed, her voice casual as if this was an everyday occurrence. “I’m going out. Didn’t want to wake you up, but I was looking for those boots I got you for your birthday a few years ago.”

Agatha’s mouth dropped open as she processed the statement. “You’re kidding. You’re seriously wearing that—” she gestured to Natasha’s barely-there outfit, “—to go out in public?”

“Why not?” Natasha tossed her hair over her shoulder as she rummaged through the boots with a nonchalant air, completely ignoring the fact that Agatha was standing there, a mix of horrified and confused. “You know me, I like to make an entrance.”

“An entrance?” Agatha echoed, unable to contain a disbelieving laugh. “This is a crime scene, Nat. I don’t even know where to start with you right now.”

Natasha shrugged, still rifling through the closet, as if this entire exchange was no more exciting than picking out a pair of shoes. “Hey, it’s called fashion. You wouldn’t understand.”

Agatha’s eyes nearly rolled back into her head. “Fashion? You’ve lost your mind. You’re wearing... that,” she gestured again, “and calling it fashion?”

Natasha met her eyes with an exaggerated pout. “You’re just jealous because I’m pulling it off better than you ever could.”

Agatha’s eyebrows shot up. “No one’s pulling anything off in that outfit, Natasha.”

“Sure, sure. Keep telling yourself that.” Natasha winked, clearly having fun with Agatha’s discomfort. “By the way, can I borrow those boots or what?”

“After that? You’re lucky I’m letting you breathe in my house right now.” Agatha was starting to feel like she needed a drink—or a nap—just to process this whole situation.

“I’ll take that as a yes,” Natasha grinned, throwing her hands up in mock surrender. “I’m just going to borrow them for a couple of hours, don’t worry. They’ll be back in your closet before you even notice.”

“I swear to god, you’re insufferable.”

Natasha just gave her a lazy smile. “Yeah, yeah. I’ve heard that before.” 

Agatha blinked, the absurdity of the situation still sinking in. “Wait. Which boots? You've gifted me a lot of those. The ones I never wore?”

Natasha paused mid-rummage and shot her a pointed look, her lips curling into a knowing smile. “Exactly.”

Agatha turned just enough to see Natasha pointing an accusatory finger at her. “I spent good money on those boots, Harkness. And now I know for a fact that you’ve never worn them.”

“Because they’re impractical as hell!” Agatha defended.

Natasha scoffed. “They’re Prada.”

“They’re obnoxious.”

“They’re hot.”

“I’m in,” Agatha said, shoving her phone into the bin before she could overthink it.
