Chapter 18

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Agatha let out a deep breath as she followed the others inside, resigned to her fate. It wasn’t that bad. She could handle this. Barely. But she could fake it. 

How hard could it be right?

Inside, the place actually didn’t look like a strip club at all—at least not the kind she’d seen in movies. There was no cheap plastic furniture, and, most importantly, no immediate sight of half naked men. Instead, the lighting was low and atmospheric, casting everything in a sultry, intimate glow. The décor was sleek, almost chic—dark leather booths lining the walls, a polished bar with tall stools, and large mirrors reflecting the dim shimmer of gold chandeliers overhead.

The music was thumping, a slow, sensual bass-heavy beat that she could feel in her bones, but there wasn’t the expected chaos of people hooting and throwing dollar bills. People were laughing, chatting, and dancing in the large open space near the bar. It was more refined than she’d expected—elegant, even.

This isn’t so bad.

Maybe, just maybe , this was a normal night out. Maybe she’d overreacted. There was nothing scandalous happening, no sign of half-naked performers—

Her thoughts were interrupted by a low, almost purring voice from behind her.

“They’re in the private suites,” Rio murmured, almost as if reading her mind.

Agatha stiffened.

Of course Vidal knew exactly what she was thinking. 

Fuck her. How did she do that? 

Was she a witch? Some kind of supernatural seductress capable of slipping into Agatha’s mind at will? Or was Agatha just that obvious?

She was sure it was the first one. Agatha wasn't an obvious person. Never had been, never will be. 

Agatha gritted her teeth. Private suites? Fantastic. She wasn’t exactly eager to get a lap dance from some high-priced performer. But it was fine. Totally fine. She could just avoid the suites. All she had to do was keep her distance, stay faraway from whatever hidden debauchery was happening behind those doors.

Easy.

Mariah and Natasha had already weaved through the crowd, making a beeline for the bar. Agatha hesitated, scanning the sea of people, before following them. As uncomfortable as she was, she really didn’t want to be left alone in the middle of all this.

The bartender was a woman with a sleek bob and an amused smirk, clearly familiar with Mariah. The moment she spotted them, she was already reaching for the top-shelf tequila.

Natasha, ever the troublemaker, wasted no time. “ Shots, ” she announced, grinning wickedly as she placed her order, her voice echoing over the heavy bass of the music.

Agatha didn’t argue. At this point, tequila was her best defense mechanism.

The bartender poured four glasses with practiced ease, sliding them across the bar. Natasha grabbed hers immediately, raising it high. “To bad decisions and worse company,” she declared, eyes twinkling with mischief.

Mariah snorted. “Oh, you wound me.”

“To Agatha’s fucking excuse of a husband,” Natasha added, “well ex husband” voice dripping with venom as she threw her shot back.

Agatha groaned. “Oh my God, Nat. ”

“I will keep toasting to that asshole until you admit you deserve better,” Natasha replied, wiping her mouth with the back of her hand. “That man is a war crime in human form.”

Mariah let out a soft laugh, swirling the liquor in her glass before downing it in one smooth motion. “So we are here to celebrate, then.”

“Oh, absolutely,” Natasha said. “I’ve been waiting for the day Agatha finally starts acting like a divorcée instead of a grieving widow.”

Agatha scowled, throwing back her shot before she could say something regrettable. The burn slid down her throat, warm and sharp, but she barely flinched.

Mariah nudged her with a teasing smirk. “That’s the spirit, babe.”

Agatha exhaled, running a hand through her ponytail. Okay. Maybe the tequila was kicking in, or maybe she’d just accepted her fate, but for the first time since stepping foot in this place, she felt herself relax. A little.

She could do this. It was just a club, after all.

Agatha barely had time to process the warmth in her throat from the tequila before Rio leaned in just slightly to grab another drink from the bar, close enough that Agatha could smell her perfume—something dark and musky, with just a hint of something sweeter underneath.

“You look tense, Harkness ,” Rio said leaning back into her seat, her voice smooth, teasing, with just enough mock concern to make Agatha’s eye twitch. “What’s wrong? This isn’t your kind of scene?”

Agatha scoffed, rolling her shoulders back in an attempt to appear unbothered . “You think?”

Rio smirked, drumming her fingers against the polished bar. “Shame. You look like you belong here.”

Agatha turned to glare at her, fully expecting to see amusement dancing in her dark eyes—but it wasn’t just amusement. It was something else. Something slow and deliberate, the way Rio’s gaze dragged over her like she had all the time in the world .

Agatha refused to acknowledge the way her pulse stuttered under that scrutiny.

Instead, she raised an unimpressed brow.

Before she could respond, Natasha turned toward her with an almost predatory grin as she set her empty shot glass down.

“Well, now that we’re here,” Natasha said, her voice teasing, her eyes gleaming with excitement. “Let’s go have some fun!”

She barely gave Agatha a second to react before grabbing Mariah’s hand and pulling her toward the dance floor, leaving Agatha standing there—alone. With Rio .

Fantastic.

Rio, still seated on one of the high stools, stretched her legs out in that effortless, arrogant way she always did—like she owned the room, like she had every right to take up space and draw every wandering eye toward her.

She looked up at Agatha, slow and appraising, that smirk still playing at the corner of her mouth.

“Guess that leaves just the two of us,” Rio mused.

Agatha let out a breath. “Great.”

Agatha shifted uncomfortably, her fingers tightening around the edge of the bar. The music vibrated through the floor beneath her feet, heavy and pulsing, setting the atmosphere thick with something heady and charged. She could feel the heat rise in her cheeks as she glanced at Rio, the woman’s figure now all too close. 

It was just the two of them at the bar, the bass-heavy music vibrating through the floor beneath their feet. Rio was sitting next to her on one of the high stools, her legs stretched out in front of her in that effortless, arrogant manner.

And of course, Agatha couldn’t help herself—her eyes drifted down to Rio’s long, toned legs, the dark leather boots hugging her calves, ending in a dangerous, almost provocative heel. She was impossibly sleek—every inch of her radiated confidence, and Agatha, despite herself, found her gaze lingering on the curve of her legs, the way they moved under the flashing lights.

“You’re staring,” Rio said, her voice low, dripping with amusement as she noticed Agatha’s eyes linger. She leaned in slightly, her lips curling into a smirk, making her look even more trouble than usual. 

Agatha snapped her gaze back up to Rio’s face, already feeling the flush spreading across her cheeks. “I wasn’t staring,” she muttered, trying to recover some semblance of composure.

Rio’s smirk only deepened. “Sure you weren’t. But then again,” she teased, her voice smooth as silk, “I didn’t think you had it in you.”

Agatha rolled her eyes, the irritation bubbling up again. “I don’t know what you’re talking about, Vidal,” she said, trying to regain some control over the conversation, though her heart was hammering a little too loudly in her chest. “I’m just trying to survive the night without making a fool of myself.”

Rio leaned back, studying her with a lazily amused expression. Her hand grazed the edge of her drink, twirling it between her fingers. “Is that really your biggest concern? Or are you worried about making a fool of yourself around me?” she teased, her voice like velvet, each word dripping with playful menace.

Agatha could feel her pulse quicken, and she cursed herself for getting drawn into this. “I’m not worried about you. You give yourself too much credit Vidal” she shot back, though it was a bit too quick, too defensive. She could feel her nerves starting to fray.

Rio chuckled, resting an elbow on the bar. “You always this fun at parties?”

“I was planning on drinking in peace,” Agatha muttered.

Rio hummed, considering. “Well, if that’s all you wanted, you should’ve just stayed home with a bottle of wine and the latest crime novel.”

Agatha narrowed her eyes. “How do you know what I do at home?”

Rio smirked, slow and knowing. “Oh, sweetheart. You’re so easy to read.”

Agatha wanted to argue, wanted to tell Rio to fuck off , but before she could get a word out, the bartender slid another drink in front of her—a deep amber liquid in a glass tumbler.

Agatha frowned. “I didn’t order this.”

Rio raised a brow. “You did.”

“No, I—” Agatha paused, eyeing Rio suspiciously. “ You ordered it, didn’t you?”

Rio merely took a sip of her own drink, all false innocence.

Agatha stared at her, torn between suspicion and reluctant amusement. “And what is this?”

“Something strong.” Rio swirled the liquid in her glass. “Something to help you relax .”

Agatha sighed, picking up the glass.

Agatha shot her a glare, trying to keep her tone casual, but it came out a little sharper than intended. “Thanks, Vidal. I’m sure you’ll make sure of that, won’t you?”

“Don’t worry,” Rio said, her grin widening into something that made Agatha feel like she was walking into a trap. “I’ll keep an eye on you. Wouldn’t want you to get into any trouble without me.” She gave Agatha a once-over that seemed to assess every inch of her, making Agatha feel like she was being slowly dissected.

The heat in Agatha’s chest was starting to burn. What was wrong with her? Why was she letting Rio get under her skin like this? She needed to snap out of it.

“Do you ever stop talking?” Agatha asked, trying to mask the unease creeping up on her.

Rio chuckled, clearly enjoying herself far too much. “Only when I have to,” she said lightly. Her smirk deepened as she traced the rim of her empty shot glass with one finger. She tilted her head slightly, watching Agatha with lazy curiosity. “I think deep down, you like the attention.”

Agatha scoffed. “Please.”

“Oh, I don’t blame you,” Rio continued, clearly enjoying herself. “You pull off depraved and dangerous well. Wouldn’t be surprised if someone thought you were part of the club.”

Agatha’s stomach did an infuriating little flip before she could stop it. She hated that Rio had this effect on her. That she could say literally anything and make it sound suggestive.

“I’ll take that as an insult,” she muttered, grabbing the nearest shot and throwing it back.

“Don’t.” Rio hummed, tapping her fingers idly against the counter. “It’s not”

The weight of her stare was suffocating. Or maybe it was the tequila.

Either way, Agatha refused to let her win.

“You’re one to talk,” she shot back. “You showed up looking like a highly trained assassin with a side hustle in seduction.”

Rio chuckled, tilting her head. “So you have been looking.”

Agatha’s jaw clenched. She could only stare at her for a moment, unsure of how to respond. Rio’s presence felt too overwhelming, her proximity a constant reminder that Agatha was in way over her head. The world around her felt a little too small, the music a little too loud. 

But before she could say anything, Rio raised her glass to her lips and took a slow sip, her eyes never leaving Agatha’s. “Let’s see what kind of trouble you can really get into tonight.”

The words hung in the air like a challenge, and Agatha was frozen, unsure if she wanted to step into that fire or run from it entirely.

Rio slowly stood up, her movement deliberate and almost predatory, as if every step was calculated to make Agatha’s heart race faster. She took a slow step toward Agatha, her eyes never leaving hers, the heat in her gaze palpable.

"Come on," Rio said, her voice a soft, teasing invitation. "Let’s go dance. You’ve got the look like you could use a little bit of fun tonight."

Agatha felt the familiar weight of her nervousness settle in her chest. She couldn’t deny that Rio was magnetic, and the idea of dancing so close to her, in this chaotic and seductive atmosphere, was enough to make her stomach twist in both anticipation and dread.

But she wasn’t going to fall for it. Not tonight. Not with everything swirling around her.

"No, thanks," Agatha said, her voice coming out firmer than she felt. She took a step back, trying to distance herself from Rio’s allure, but her words weren’t enough to shake the tension that had formed between them.

Rio raised an eyebrow, clearly amused by the rejection, a half-smile curling at the corners of her lips. “Okay then,” she said lightly, her voice dripping with mock sweetness. “Guess I'll just have to have all the fun without you.” She turned on her heel, striding away with that confident swagger, heading toward the dance floor, leaving Agatha behind, her heart still racing.

Agatha let out a breath, feeling a small sense of relief wash over her. 

But before she could settle into the moment, the bartender—a woman with dark, striking features, and a confident, sultry presence—leaned over the bar, casting a glance at Rio’s retreating figure.

"She's hot, you're a lucky lady" the bartender said, her tone a mix of admiration and curiosity as she wiped down the counter.

Agatha nearly choked on the sip of her drink she was taking. “She’s not my date,” Agatha said, her voice flat, hoping to shut it down.

The bartender gave her an amused look, her lips curling into a sly smile. “Oh I'm sorry” She winked before walking off to attend to other customers, clearly not buying Agatha’s attempt at a denial.

Agatha sighed, rubbing a hand over her face. 

She stayed at the bar, her drink slowly becoming the anchor she clung to. The initial discomfort of being in this strange, high-energy environment was wearing off, replaced by the soothing buzz of the alcohol seeping into her system. Her fingers traced the rim of her glass absentmindedly, her thoughts fuzzy and disjointed. The music pulsed in the background, the rhythm syncing with the beat of her own heart, but she was too focused on the feeling of being slightly tipsy to care about anything else.

For a while, the noise and flashing lights seemed distant, and she was content with her own space, even as the others—Mariah, Rio, and Natasha—drifted in and out of her consciousness.

Then, a familiar voice broke through the fog of her thoughts.

"Alright loser, let's go," Natasha said, her voice carrying a playful edge. She was grinning wide as she approached Agatha, Mariah and Rio following her.

"The suit is ready," Natasha added, her eyes sparkling with excitement. "I reserved one for us."

Agatha blinked, trying to focus on what was going on. The room seemed to spin for a moment as she registered Natasha's words.Her stomach churned slightly at the thought of what that implied. 

Natasha, clearly oblivious to her inner turmoil, was already pulling her by the hand, not giving Agatha a moment to think about it. Mariah and Rio followed them, Nat´s energy infectious as she laughed and gestured for them to follow.

Agatha hesitated for a moment, feeling the weight of the alcohol pulling her into a haze of indecision. She should probably be more cautious, but something about Natasha’s infectious enthusiasm made her want to tag along. 

Besides, she wasn’t about to spend the rest of the night alone at the bar, looking like a wallflower. 

With a resigned sigh, Agatha let herself get dragged toward the suit. She could feel Rio’s eyes on her as she walked, but she didn’t dare look back.

As they reached the booth, Agatha slid into the plush seat, trying to make herself comfortable amidst the bright lights and throbbing music. She sank into the cushion, feeling the thrum of the bass in her bones, and glanced at the others. Mariah was already pulling her phone out to check something, Natasha was practically bouncing with excitement, and Rio was lounging casually in her seat, as if she owned the place.

Agatha took a deep breath, trying to keep her focus, trying to make the night feel like it was something fun and exciting, instead of the rollercoaster ride of anxiety and confusion it had become.

Agatha shifted uncomfortably in her seat, her body betraying her anxiety as she squirmed on the plush cushion. She wasn’t used to this. Hell, she had never been in a strip club before, and she definitely hadn’t imagined ever doing it, let alone at her age. 

Mariah leaned forward, her eyes wide with anticipation, while Natasha was practically glowing, her fingers drumming on the couch as she waited for the show to begin.

Agatha couldn’t shake the feeling that she didn’t belong here. She wasn’t cut out for this kind of atmosphere. She barely knew what to do with herself, feeling out of place in the skimpy outfit Natasha had dressed her in. And the last thing she wanted was to be one of the focus points of a stripper’s performance.

She glanced at the suit, her gaze darting nervously toward the door, as if she could somehow will the night to go differently. She hoped—no, she prayed—that the stripper wouldn’t choose her. She couldn’t handle that. 

Then, the lights suddenly dimmed, plunging the room into darkness. The pulse of the music shifted, deep bass thumping through the floor like the beat of a heart. For a moment, it felt like everything was suspended in time, the anticipation almost too much to bear. She leaned forward instinctively, the shadows around her heightening the tension. What the hell had she gotten herself into?

And then, suddenly, a spotlight snapped on, its intense white light slicing through the darkened booth like a blade. Agatha blinked, her eyes adjusting to the glare, and she caught her breath at the sight of a figure stepping into the spotlight.

It wasn’t a guy. 

The woman who appeared before them was... not what Agatha expected at all. She was covered head to toe in sparkling silver and black sequins, her outfit hugging every curve as she stepped confidently into the spotlight. Her skin was glowing under the lights, and she moved like she owned the room, a slow, deliberate sway to her hips as she surveyed the  small room.

Agatha’s mind reeled for a moment. A female stripper? Her pulse quickened, a wave of confusion crashing over her. Wasn’t this supposed to be a male revue? She glanced at Natasha, her eyes wide with disbelief.

And then, the realization hit her like a ton of bricks.

Natasha.

Of course. 

Agatha’s stomach twisted, her discomfort escalating. She hadn’t expected this. Not at all. She was not prepared for this. 

And now, she was sitting here, in this booth, watching a woman dressed in next to nothing getting ready to do who-knows-what to entertain them. It felt like a bad dream—one she couldn’t wake up from.

The stripper began to dance, her movements fluid and confident, but all Agatha could think about was how much she just wanted to leave. The heat of embarrassment crept up her neck. She glanced at Mariah, who was practically salivating at the sight, and Natasha, who was looking at the performance with that same mischievous glint in her eyes.

This was not Agatha’s world.

The stripper continued to sway, her body moving in time with the music. The beat of the sound pulsed in the air, heavy and insistent, and the glittering woman’s body seemed to shimmer with every movement, drawing the attention of everyone in the room. Her eyes locked with Agatha’s for a brief moment, and Agatha quickly looked away, her fingers digging into the plush booth as if it could somehow anchor her to something solid.

Mariah was practically on the edge of her seat, her eyes wide, a grin plastered on her face as she watched, clearly enjoying the show. 

Agatha could barely focus on the performance. Every part of her was screaming to leave, to do anything to escape the tension coiling in her stomach. But then, the stripper did something that made Agatha freeze.

The woman stepped off the little center stage, her eyes never leaving Agatha, and began to walk toward her. Agatha's breath caught in her throat, and she felt a sudden, intense urge to shrink into herself. The woman’s steps were calculated, confident, and the rhythmic sway of her hips drew every eye in the room toward her.

As she approached, Agatha’s palms began to sweat. She didn’t want this. She knew, though, that she couldn’t avoid it. The woman moved closer, and Agatha instinctively straightened up, shifting uncomfortably on her seat. She didn’t even know what to say.

When the stripper reached them, she stopped just a few feet away, the air around her thick with the scent of perfume and sweat. The woman looked at her with a knowing smile, as if she could sense Agatha’s unease. But before Agatha could form a single word, Rio, ever the instigator, leaned in.

“Relax, darling,” Rio said with that smirk Agatha had come to dread. “She’s not going to bite.”

The stripper gave a slight chuckle and turned back to Agatha, her hands moving to adjust her outfit, each touch seeming to heighten the tension in the air.

And then, without a word, the stripper began to dance. Her movements were slow, sensual, and deliberate as she lowered herself in front of Agatha, one hand resting on her knee, the other gliding up her leg. The air seemed to thicken around them as the woman’s body shifted, the soft, seductive music filling the space between them.

Agatha’s heart hammered in her chest, and she swallowed hard, feeling the heat of the woman’s body so close to hers. But it wasn’t the woman herself that had Agatha’s blood running cold. No, it was the way Rio’s gaze moved from the stripper to Agatha, that damned smirk still playing on her lips. 

Sensing Agatha's doubt the girl moved to Rio who was sitting next to her.

Rio reached out, her hands moving to the stripper’s hips, guiding her as if they were already familiar with each other. The two of them moved as one, Rio’s hands gliding expertly over the woman’s body, guiding her with precision.

Agatha could feel a tightness in her chest. The way Rio’s hands slid over the woman’s skin, the way their bodies meshed together on that small suit, made her insides twist in a way she didn’t understand.

She pushed her thoughts down, forcing herself to focus on the show instead. She didn’t want to look, didn’t want to see how much Rio was enjoying herself. But, despite every rational thought in her mind, she couldn’t tear her gaze away.

Rio and the stripper moved together, the rhythm between them effortless and fluid. Agatha’s pulse raced as she watched, her breath catching at the intimacy of the moment. It was too much, too overwhelming, and before she could stop herself, she looked at Rio. Just for a second. Her heart thudded as she caught Rio’s eyes, that smirk still in place.

Agatha quickly turned away, her face flushed with something she refused to acknowledge.

The show continued for what felt like an eternity, every movement from the stripper and Rio adding to the weight in Agatha's chest. She tried to keep her focus elsewhere—on the drinks in front of her, on the glistening lights of the club, on the chaos swirling around her—but all she could see were Rio’s hands on the stripper, guiding her through the dance with a familiarity that made Agatha feel like she was suffocating. Her pulse was erratic, her mind a jumbled mess, and every second of the performance made her more aware of how utterly out of place she felt.

Finally, the music started to fade, the stripper’s performance coming to a close. The woman got off of Nats lap. When did that happen? Agatha hadn't realized that. The woman gave one last slow, seductive spin, winking at her as she made her way off the small room. The lights flickered back to their usual dim ambiance, and her friends erupted into applause. Agatha’s chest was still tight, her breath shallow, and she knew she couldn’t stay there a moment longer.

“I need to use the bathroom,” she muttered to no one in particular, bolting from her seat before anyone could stop her. Her legs felt unsteady as she slipped out of the booth, weaving through the crowded club. She pushed past bodies that barely acknowledged her presence, the thrum of music pressing against her ears.

The moment she stepped into the relative quiet of the bathroom, she stopped. Exhaling sharply, she braced herself against the sink, trying to steady the storm churning inside her.

What was that?

Her reflection in the mirror caught her eye as she walked past the bathroom door, and for a split second, she didn’t even recognize the person staring back at her. The tight leather, the makeup—it was all too much. She felt like an imposter, someone who had walked into a world that wasn’t hers, only to find herself tangled in emotions she couldn’t untangle.

She shook her head and turned away, her thoughts racing. “Get it together,” she muttered to herself. “It’s just a night out. Nothing more.”

But it didn’t feel like just another night out. Not anymore.

As she looked around, she spotted Rio again, this time on the dance floor, talking to a guy. Her stomach dropped.She could feel that gnawing sensation from before creeping back,  irritation at herself for getting caught up in this whole damn mess.

“Vidal,” Agatha called out, her voice sharper than intended.

Agatha’s gaze flicked to the man still standing beside Rio, clearly waiting for her attention. “I’m sorry to interrupt… whatever this is,” she added, voice laced with disdain. Then, without hesitation, she turned to him. “You can go now.”

The man scoffed, his expression shifting from mild surprise to irritation. “Excuse me?”

Rio let out a quiet chuckle, swirling the drink in her hand. “Yeah, sweetheart,” she murmured, her eyes glinting with mischief. “She excused you.”

The man muttered something under his breath, shaking his head before stalking off. Agatha ignored him, already focused on Rio, who was now watching her with a look that made her feel entirely too seen.

“Do you need something?” Rio asked, her voice smooth and effortless, as if she already knew the answer.

Agatha’s heart thudded against her ribs, but she shoved it down. “Where are Natasha and Mariah?”

Rio’s laughter cut through the music, low and rich, curling around Agatha in a way that made her skin prickle. “Probably fucking somewhere,” she said with a shrug, taking a sip from her drink before flicking her gaze back to where the man had been standing a moment ago, as if vaguely disappointed that he’d left so easily.

Rio raised an eyebrow, looking at Agatha with that same knowing smirk. “Is she gay? You’re seriously asking me that?” she replied, her voice dripping with amusement. She gave a slow, exaggerated once-over of Agatha’s face, as though processing the question fully. 

Agatha hesitated. “…I mean, I just didn’t—”

Rio arched her brow, looking at her like she’d just asked if water was wet as she exhaled sharply, shaking her head in exaggerated disbelief. “Oh, wait. You’re actually serious.” She gave Agatha a slow, deliberate once-over, as if she needed to assess just how clueless she was.

Heat prickled at Agatha’s skin. “I—uh, yeah,” she muttered.

Rio leaned against the railing, clearly savoring Agatha’s discomfort. “Incredible,” she huffed, before taking another sip of her drink. “But yeah, Mariah is into women. Painfully obvious if you’ve been paying attention.”

“Okay, okay, I get it.” Agatha was absolutely mortified but trying to recover. “I still need to find Natasha.”

Rio tilted her head slightly, eyes glimmering with something unreadable. “Why don’t you just enjoy the night, Agatha?” She smirked. “You’re doing fine.”

Frustration sparked in Agatha’s chest. She wasn’t about to let Rio be smug and vague, especially when she was already so damn confused about everything else. “I’m not here to enjoy anything,” she snapped. “I just want to find her so we can go home. Please, help me.”

But then Rio sighed, shifting closer, her voice dipping just enough to make Agatha’s pulse stutter. “Fine, fine,” she relented, though amusement still curled at the edges of her words. “You’ve got that look in your eyes like you’re about to throw a tantrum, and trust me, no one needs to see that.”

She didn’t have time to think about it now, though. All that mattered was getting Nat and getting the hell out of this crazy club before she did something she'd regret.

Up here, the flashing lights made everything feel even more surreal, casting the crowd in alternating hues of electric blue and crimson that only added to the disorienting atmosphere. Laughter and conversation blurred into the music, creating a dizzying, intoxicating hum. Rio, as always, moved like she belonged—confident, unbothered. The walls of the kitchen seemed to close in around her, the air thick and suffocating. What would they think of her? What would they say? Mariah had always been so open, so unapologetically herself, but Agatha wasn’t like that. She couldn’t be. And Nat… Nat would never let her live it down. She’d make jokes, tease her mercilessly, and Agatha wouldn’t be able to handle it. She wouldn’t be able to handle any of it.

“No, no, no,” she whispered to herself, her voice trembling. “She wouldn’t tell them. She wouldn’t.”

But the doubt was already there, gnawing at her. Rio had looked so wrecked when Agatha left, so hurt. What if she had gone straight to Nat and Mariah for comfort? What if they were all talking about her right now, laughing at her, judging her?

Agatha’s legs gave out, and she slid to the floor, her back pressed against the cabinets. She buried her face in her hands, trying to steady her breathing, but it was no use. The panic was too much, too overwhelming. She felt like she was drowning, like the weight of her own fear was crushing her.

But she couldn’t stay here. She couldn’t fall apart. Not now. Not with Nicky’s party just hours away. She had promised him it would be perfect, and she wasn’t about to let him down because of her own mess.

Agatha took a deep, shuddering breath, forcing herself to focus. She counted to five, then exhaled slowly, repeating the process until her breathing evened out. Her hands still trembled, but she clenched them into fists, pressing her nails into her palms to ground herself.

She pushed herself to her feet, her legs shaky but holding.

She opened the fridge and stared blankly at its contents. There wasn’t much. A half-empty carton of eggs, a few slices of bread, some wilted lettuce. She grabbed the eggs and bread, deciding toast and scrambled eggs would have to do. 

Agatha picked at her eggs, her stomach twisting with every bite. The food tasted like ash in her mouth, but she forced herself to eat, knowing she needed the energy for the day ahead.

Agatha was halfway through forcing down a piece of dry toast when she heard the front door open. The handle rattled, followed by a long pause, then a muffled curse. A thud. More cursing. Finally, the door swung open, and someone stumbled inside, the sound of boots clumsily hitting the floor filling the quiet house.

Agatha didn’t even need to look.

Nat.

She took her time chewing, listening as Nat shuffled down the hall, bumping into at least two things along the way before finally making it to the kitchen. When Nat appeared in the doorway, Agatha let her gaze drag over her, unimpressed.

Her hair was a complete disaster, tangled in a way that suggested both bad decisions and a lack of access to a hairbrush. Her dress was wrinkled beyond saving, one strap hanging dangerously off her shoulder. And draped over her shoulders like a trophy Mariah’s leather jacket.

Agatha recognized the jacket instantly. Her stomach twisted.

Nat yawned, stretching like a cat that had spent the night rolling around in bad ideas. “Oh, hey. You’re alive.”

Agatha just took another bite of toast. “Unfortunately.”

Nat groaned dramatically, dropping into the chair across from her with all the grace of a corpse flopping into an open grave. She smashed her forehead against the table. “God, my head is killing me.”

“Shocking,” Agatha deadpanned.

Nat ignored her, pushing her tangled hair back, mascara smudged halfway to her temples. “Last night was insane.”

Agatha swallowed the dry lump of toast in her mouth, throat suddenly tight. "Yeah?"

Nat lifted her head just enough to squint at her. "Uh, yeah? You tell me. One second, you’re there, the next…poof.Vanished into thin air."

Agatha just sipped her coffee.

Nat narrowed her eyes. “You didn’t even answer my texts.”

“I did text you.”

“Yeah—‘I left.’” Nat held up air quotes, her voice dripping with mockery. “Very informative.”

She leaned back, stretching lazily. “At least you didn’t spend the night alone, right?”

Agatha nearly choked on her coffee. “What’s that supposed to mean?”

“I don’t know.” Nat gave her a look. “You vanished. No explanation, no nothing. It was a classic horror movie move… poof… and the main character is just gone.” She rubbed her forehead, groaning. “Mariah thought maybe you met someone and finally decided it was time to get laid for once, but I guess she was wrong. I kinda thought you did too, hell, I hoped you did.”

She yawned, then added casually, “I know Rio would’ve thought the same. You know… if she was with us.”

Agatha froze. “…She wasn’t with you?”

“Nope.” Nat sighed. “She disappeared, too, so…”

Agatha’s grip on her mug tightened slightly.

“Oh?” she said, carefully neutral.

“Yeah. No idea where she went. One second she was there, the next she wasn't. Kind of like you.”

Nat lifted her head now, watching Agatha with a look that was just a little too knowing.

Agatha forced a shrug. “Maybe she went home.”

“Maybe.” Nat tilted her head, squinting at her like a detective in a bad cop drama.

A beat passed. Then she sighed and stretched, draping herself over the chair like a woman who had barely survived a war. “Anyway, I was too drunk to care at the time, and, well…” She smirked, tugging at the edges of the leather jacket. “One thing led to another.”

Agatha pinched the bridge of her nose. “So you’re hooking up with one of my only friends here. Excellent job.”

“Correction,” Nat said, holding up a finger. “I hooked up with Mariah. Past tense. It’s already happened. No take-backs.”

Agatha peeked at her through her fingers. “Please tell me you’re joking.”

“Do I look like I’m joking?” Nat gestured to her disheveled state. “Because I feel like the evidence speaks for itself.”

Agatha groaned, dragging a hand down her face. “This is a nightmare.”

“No, this is progress,” Nat corrected. “The flirting worked. You should be proud of me.”

“Proud?” Agatha repeated, incredulous. “Nat, she’s my colleague. I have to see her at work. Do you have any idea how awkward that’s going to be?”

Nat shrugged, completely unbothered. “Not my problem.”

“It is your problem!” Agatha snapped. “You’re the one who—” She stopped herself, inhaling sharply. “Never mind. I don’t even want to know.”

Nat smirked. “Oh, come on. Don’t be such a prude. It’s not like I’m going to show up at the hospital and start making out with her in the break room.”

Agatha glared. “You better not.”

“No promises,” Nat said with a wink. She grinned, clearly pleased with herself. “Mariah’s a menace, by the way. I mean, I knew that, obviously, but my God. She’s got, like, bossy energy, you know? The kind that makes you reconsider your entire life. I think she might have hypnotized me.”

Agatha stared. “Yeah, that sounds horrifying.”

Nat waggled her eyebrows. “Oh, it was.”

Agatha just picked up her coffee and took a slow, deliberate sip. But her mind was stuck on one thing.

Rio disappeared, too.

Had Rio left because of her? Had she said anything? Told them anything? Had she found somebody else to take home?

She wasn’t sure if she wanted to know the answer.

Agatha cleared her throat, forcing her focus back. “So, what happened after I left? Please leave out the nasty details, I don’t want to hear them.”

Nat’s face lit up. “Oh, it was wild, and you’re boring. Anyway, I got into a drinking contest with some guy, which I obviously won. Mariah started a conga line, and I may or may not have stolen a bottle of tequila from the bar.”

Agatha blinked. “You’re kidding.”

“Nope,” Nat said, popping the ‘p.’ “It’s in my purse if you want a shot.”

“I’m good,” Agatha said dryly. “But thanks.”

Nat grinned. “Your loss.”

She drummed her fingers on the table, watching Agatha a little too closely. “So…what about you? You seemed… tense last night.”

Agatha shot up from her chair. “I need to clean.”

Nat frowned. “Uh, okay?”

“Nicky’s birthday is today,” Agatha reminded her sharply. “Remember Nicky? My son? The whole reason you’re here right now?”

Nat groaned. “I made it in time, didn’t I?”

“Barely.” Agatha wrinkled her nose. “And for the love of God, go take a shower. And use some makeup to cover those hickeys.”

Nat snorted. “These are my trophies. I’m not covering shit.”

Agatha shook her head, unable to suppress a small smile despite herself. “You’re impossible, you know that?”

“And yet, you keep me around,” Nat said, stretching. “Now, if you’ll excuse me, I’m going to take a shower and wash off last night’s good decisions.”

“Good luck with that,” Agatha muttered.

Nat winked. “Thanks. I’ll need it.”

As she disappeared down the hall, Agatha let out a long sigh, rubbing her temple.

She still didn’t know if Rio had said anything.

But at least, for now, Nat seemed clueless.

She just had to get through the day without spiraling.

The kitchen was a mess. Dirty dishes piled in the sink, crumbs scattered across the counter, the trash overflowing with the eggs she had just thrown away. It was as good a place to start as any.

Agatha grabbed a sponge and turned on the faucet, the sound of running water filling the silence. She scrubbed at the dishes with a ferocity that surprised even herself, her movements sharp and deliberate. The physical act of cleaning helped, giving her something to focus on, something to channel her restless energy into. 

By the time the kitchen was spotless, her hands were raw and red, but she felt a little more in control.  She moved on to the living room, straightening pillows, vacuuming the carpet, and wiping down surfaces. The repetitive motions were soothing, almost meditative, and for a while, she managed to push her worries to the back of her mind. 

Nat wandered into the living room, freshly showered, her damp hair piled messily on top of her head. She had traded last night’s wrinkled dress for a pair of sweatpants and one of Agatha’s hoodies, the one she had explicitly told her not to steal.

She flopped onto the couch with a dramatic sigh. “Okay, I’m clean. I’m alive. And I’m officially awake enough to pretend I’m useful. What do you need me to do?”

Agatha, still wiping down the coffee table with more force than necessary, barely looked up. “You can start by receiving the deliveries. Decorations should be here any minute, and the food and cake won’t be far behind.”

Nat groaned. “Ugh, manual labor?”

“Yes, because opening a door and taking boxes is so physically demanding.”

Nat stretched her legs across the couch, making herself comfortable. “You know, I could just say I have a hangover and be completely useless all day. But because I love you, I’m willing to suffer through the immense hardship of standing up and grabbing packages.”

Agatha rolled her eyes but smirked despite herself. “Truly, your sacrifice is admirable.”

Nat pointed at her. “Damn right it is.”

She glanced at the clock. “So, we’ve got… what? Three hours ‘til Nicky gets here, and five before the rest of the guests start showing up?”

“Yep.”

Nat exhaled, tilting her head back. “Okay. I can handle this. I can be responsible. I can—” She cut herself off, suddenly perking up. “Wait. Is there a bouncy house? Because I feel like, as the fun aunt, I should get first dibs.”

Agatha shook her head. “No bouncy house.”

Nat gasped, clutching her chest. “What kind of monster deprives a child of a bouncy house on their birthday?”

“One with limited space and a realistic budget,” Agatha said dryly.

Nat clicked her tongue. “Tragic. Truly tragic. Nicky deserves better.”

Agatha threw a pillow at her. “Shut up and go wait for the packages.”

Nat caught it with a grin, then reluctantly pulled herself off the couch. “Fine, fine. But I’m stealing a cupcake as payment for my labor.”

Agatha huffed a laugh as Nat wandered toward the door, already pulling out her phone. For the first time since last night, the weight on her chest felt just a little lighter.

By some miracle—or sheer force of will—everything was ready in time.

The living room had transformed from its usual cozy but chaotic state into something almost Pinterest-worthy. Blue and green streamers hung from the ceiling, twisting together like vines, and a big Happy Birthday, Nicky! banner stretched across the wall. Cartoon dinosaur cutouts, because Nicky was in his dinosaur phase, were taped to every surface, giving the place an oddly prehistoric feel. A giant T-Rex balloon loomed in the corner, looking vaguely threatening, and a smaller herd of balloon dinosaurs was scattered around the room like a migration had just passed through.

The food was set up on the dining table, with neatly arranged trays of snacks, sandwiches, and, because Agatha knew her son, the emergency backup nuggets. The birthday cake, a carefully decorated masterpiece featuring a very enthusiastic-looking stegosaurus, sat proudly in the center.

Nat surveyed the finished setup, nodding in approval. “I gotta say, Aggie, I was expecting way more of a trainwreck.”

Agatha, standing in the middle of it all, arms crossed, sighed. “Thanks for the faith.”

“I mean it! This looks, like, competent.” Nat gestured around. “Kid’s gonna lose his little mind.”

Agatha exhaled, letting herself relax for the first time all morning. “Let’s hope.”

Then Nat squinted at her. “Okay, so you do realize you still look like a haunted Victorian ghost, right?”

Agatha blinked. “Excuse me?”

“You’ve been running around like a lunatic all morning, and now you look like one.” Nat waved a hand at her. “Hair? Mess. Clothes? Somehow wrinkled despite being clean. Face? That’s just your face, but it could use a little help.”

Agatha groaned. “I don’t have time to—”

“You do have time,” Nat cut in. “Nicky’s not here yet, and I refuse to let you greet your ex-husband looking like you just crawled out of a crypt.”

Agatha stiffened at the mention of Daniel. “Right. He’s coming.”

“Yeah, and I need to be mentally prepared for that,” Nat said, cracking her knuckles. “Might be a good time to revisit my murder alibi collection.”

Agatha rolled her eyes but smirked. “I’m going to go change before you actually get yourself arrested.”

“Good call,” Nat said, already pulling up something on her phone. “But just so you know, if he so much as breathes wrong, I will be launching him into the sun.

—----

Agatha, now in her room, quickly swapped out her sweatpants for a simple but flattering dress, a deep blue that brought out her eyes. She brushed through her hair, letting it fall naturally around her shoulders, and even dabbed on a bit of makeup. Nothing too much, just enough to make it look like she hadn’t been stress cleaning and overthinking for hours.

When she returned to the living room, Nat let out a low whistle. “Damn, okay, Miss Effort.”

Agatha gave her a look. “I’m trying to look like a functional adult, not impress anyone.”

Nat smirked. “Sure. And I totally didn’t see you checking yourself out in the hallway mirror just now.”

Agatha ignored that. “What time is it?”

Nat checked her phone. “Daniel should be here soon.” She cracked her neck. “Do I need to be on my best behavior, or can I call him a bastard to his face?”

“Nat.” Agatha warned, giving her a sharp look.

“What?” Nat spread her hands innocently. “I’m just asking. I mean, the guy is the worst.”

Agatha sighed. “I know, but this isn’t about him. It’s about Nicky. I don’t want today turning into a thing.”

Nat groaned. “Fine. I’ll behave. Mostly. ”

Agatha gave her a pointed look.

“Okay, okay,” Nat huffed. “No violence. No dramatic insults. I won’t even bring up the fact that his entire existence is a crime against humanity.”

“Nat.”

“I said I’ll behave!” Nat raised her hands in mock surrender.

Agatha shook her head, but she was laughing. “This is going to be a long afternoon.”

“Yep,” Nat said, stretching her arms behind her head with a wicked grin. “But at least it’ll be entertaining .”

Just then, the sound of the doorbell broke through their banter. Both women froze, and for a moment, it felt like the calm before a storm.

“That’s him,” Agatha said, heart racing a little.

“Showtime,” Nat said, getting up from the couch with a dramatic flair, as if stepping into a role on stage.

Agatha made her way to the door, her breath catching in her chest. She opened it, and there he was. Daniel.

The first thing Agatha noticed was how normal he looked. His hair was neatly styled, and he was dressed in a perfectly ironed shirt and a pair of expensive jeans, the kind that screamed “I’m too busy for basic decency but I still want to look like I could care.” The casualness of his presence always grated on Agatha’s nerves.

“Hey,” Daniel said, flashing a smile that felt a little too rehearsed.

“Hi,” Agatha said, stepping aside so he could come in. “Where's my son?"

Before Daniel could respond, a small voice rang out from behind him.

“Mom!” Nicky’s voice cut through the air, and moments later, he appeared, eyes lighting up as soon as he saw Nat standing behind Agatha.

“NAT!” Nicky squealed, excitement bubbling out of him. Without a second thought, he ran straight toward her, arms flung wide.

Nat didn’t miss a beat. She grinned wickedly and scooped him up into the air with all the enthusiasm of someone who hadn't seen their favorite little person in ages. "My favorite little human!" she declared, tossing him into the air just enough for him to giggle like a maniac.

“Again! Again!” Nicky laughed, and Nat obeyed, throwing him up a second time, making him squeal even louder.

Agatha, watching the scene, couldn’t help but smile despite herself. Nicky was absolutely thrilled, and it was clear that Nat was very good at keeping him entertained. 

Meanwhile, Daniel, who had stepped back to give them space, looked not pleased. The stiffness in his posture was evident, but he kept it to himself. He didn’t even try to hide the annoyance that flickered across his face as he watched Nicky and Nat bond so effortlessly.

“Oh, so now you’re the fun aunt, huh?” he said, trying to sound casual, but his tone held a certain edge that Agatha knew all too well. He had always hated how easy Nat could connect with Nicky.

Nat, still holding Nicky, gave Daniel a long, pointed look before grinning widely. “What can I say? I’m the cool one,” she said, her voice dripping with playful sarcasm as she bounced Nicky up and down.

Daniel’s lips tightened, clearly irked, but he said nothing. Instead, he adjusted his posture and turned his attention back to Agatha. “Everything’s set for the lunch later?” he asked, as if this whole situation was entirely normal.

Agatha nodded, trying her best to act like everything was just fine. “Yeah, everything’s good. The cake and food should be here soon, and the decorations are all set up.”

“Good,” Daniel replied curtly, his gaze lingering on Nicky and Nat, who were still engaged in their little back-and-forth of laughter and playful antics. “I don’t want things to get out of hand. Last time—”

“Oh, please,” Nat cut in with a grin, still holding Nicky like he was the most precious thing in the world. “If anyone’s going to ‘get out of hand,’ it’s probably you. I’m just here for the cake.”

Agatha chuckled at the absurdity of it all. It was always the same with Daniel, so self-important, so insistent on the idea that he had everything figured out. And Nat? Well, Nat was here to make sure it all stayed interesting.

“Maybe you should take some notes,” Nat added to Daniel with a sly smirk. 

Daniel's face turned a shade of red that was too close to anger for Agatha’s liking, but she decided it was time to steer things in a more peaceful direction.

“Okay, guys. Let’s just… not make this a thing today, alright? We’ve got a whole afternoon ahead of us,” she said, trying to force some calm into the situation.

Nat, clearly relishing the tension, winked at Daniel. “Don’t worry, Daniel. I’ll make sure you get some attention too. Maybe you’ll even have a moment to show off how much you care,” she teased, making Agatha bite back a smile.

Daniel’s jaw clenched, but he didn’t say anything. He just shot one last look at Agatha before turning his attention back to Nicky and Nat, who had managed to break free from their playful exchange and now stood at the doorway of the living room, ready to begin the day.

Agatha smiled down at Nicky, who was still buzzing with excitement, his small hands tugging at the edge of Nat's leather jacket as if trying to climb back into her arms.

"Alright, buddy," she said, crouching down to his level. "You can’t run around in your pajamas all day, can you?"

Nicky’s face scrunched up in confusion. "But I like my pajamas..."

"I know, buddy, but today’s a special day," Nat said with an exaggerated wink. "You gotta look sharp for your big party. Now, go get dressed and make sure you pick something cool, alright? The coolest clothes you've got."

Nicky’s eyes lit up at the idea. "Okay!" he said, already darting off toward his room without another word.

Nat, standing behind Agatha, eyed Daniel with an unreadable expression. Then she smiled sweetly. “So, Daniel. How’s the whole living in your perfect little world with no consequences thing going?”

Daniel blinked, caught off guard. Agatha winced. Of course, Nat wouldn’t hold back.

“I… uh, good, I guess?” Daniel said, clearly not knowing what to make of Nat’s bluntness.

“Good to hear,” Nat said, a little too cheerfully. “Glad to see the moral bankruptcy isn’t taking too much of a toll on you.”

Daniel exhaled slowly, as if he were really trying to be the bigger person. "You know, Natasha, it’s always a pleasure."

"Aw, Danny, I bet you say that to all the women who can’t stand you," Nat cooed, tilting her head.

Agatha snorted, shaking her head. "Alright, children, play nice."

Nat raised her hands in mock innocence. "I am playing nice. I haven’t even mentioned the part where he—"

"Nat," Agatha cut in sharply, giving her a pointed look.

Nat huffed but crossed her arms, clearly restraining herself. Daniel shifted uncomfortably, his jaw tight.

“I’m just here for Nicky,” he said finally, running a hand through his hair.

Agatha raised an eyebrow. "Oh, trust me, we know. Otherwise, I doubt you’d ever set foot in this house again."

Daniel flinched, just barely, but it was enough to satisfy her.

"Alright," he said, exhaling as if he were the victim here. "I get it. I’m the bad guy. Always have been, always will be."

Nat smiled. "Wow, look at that, Agatha. He’s finally developing some self awareness. Maybe there is hope for him after all."

"Baby steps," Agatha murmured.

Daniel’s eyes darted between them, clearly debating whether it was worth engaging. He sighed. "Are we done? Or do you two want to get a few more punches in before lunch?"

Nat smirked. "I mean, I could go on, but Nicky might come back, and I wouldn’t want to damage his perception of his very responsible father."

Daniel shot her a flat look.

Agatha exhaled dramatically. "Fine. Truce. For now."

"Yeah, yeah," Nat said, waving a hand. "But if you do start acting like a condescending prick at lunch, I reserve the right to stab you with a butter knife."

Daniel sighed again, as if resigning himself to his fate. "I’ll be on my best behavior."

"You better," Agatha said, setting her coffee down. "Because I will take Nicky’s side in any argument, and we both know that kid can hold a grudge like no other."

Daniel looked genuinely nervous at that. "Noted."

Nat grinned, satisfied. "Good. Now, let’s go pretend we’re normal, functional adults until cake time."

—-- 

Lunch was a tense but relatively civil affair, mostly because Nicky was too excited about his birthday to notice the subtle barbs being exchanged over the table. Daniel, to his credit, kept his mouth shut and focused on Nicky, while Nat made a point of cutting her steak just a little too aggressively every time he spoke. Agatha, exhausted from both keeping the peace and making sure Nat didn’t actually stab anyone with a butter knife, focused on finishing her food in record time. The second they were done, she all but leapt from her seat under the pretense of checking on the decorations, relieved that the real event was about to start.

Just as she set out the last of the party favors, the doorbell rang.

"Showtime," Nat muttered, stretching her arms like she was preparing for battle.

Agatha rolled her eyes and went to open the door, only to be immediately bombarded by a chorus of greetings as the first wave of guests arrived, arms full of presents and energy levels far too high for her current state of mind.

The doorbell kept ringing through the next few minutes. 

The door swung open to reveal Wanda, effortlessly put together despite wrangling two very excitable twins, and Vision, carrying a comically oversized gift bag.

“Agatha!” Wanda greeted warmly, shifting slightly as Billy and Tommy shot past her like twin rockets.

"Nicky!" Billy shouted.

"Where is he?!" Tommy added.

Before Agatha could even answer, Nicky came barreling in from the living room. The moment he spotted his friends, he let out an excited yell, and the three of them collided in a chaotic tangle of limbs and laughter, nearly knocking each other over.

Agatha smirked. "Well, I guess we know who the real stars of the party are."

“They’ve been talking about this all week,” Wanda sighed, watching the kids immediately start scheming whatever disaster they were about to unleash. “I hope you don’t mind if they destroy your house.”

“It was a risk I accepted the moment I invited them,” Agatha said dryly.

As Vision set the massive gift bag down by the table, Agatha gestured toward Nat, who had been watching the chaos unfold with an amused smirk.

“Wanda, Vision, this is Natasha,” Agatha said, waving lazily between them. “She’s, unfortunately, a permanent fixture in my life.”

“Rude,” Nat muttered before grinning and shaking Wanda’s hand. “Nice to meet you. I’ve heard a lot about you.”

“Oh?” Wanda arched a brow. “All good things, I hope.”

Nat shot Agatha a look. “Hmm… define ‘good.’”

Vision, ever polite, extended his hand. “It’s a pleasure, Natasha.”

“Likewise,” Nat said, shaking his hand. She eyed the oversized gift bag. “Did you guys bring an entire toy store?”

“Almost,” Wanda said, sighing. “The boys couldn’t agree on just one thing, so…”

Nat smirked. “Sounds about right.” Then, turning to Agatha, she added, “You actually have normal friends. I’m shocked.”

The party was in full swing, and Nicky was having the time of his life. Between running around with all of his friends, eating way too much cake, and unwrapping presents like a child possessed, he was practically glowing with excitement. Every gift was met with an over the top reaction, gasps, squeals, and a dramatic “THIS IS THE BEST DAY EVER!” that had Wanda hiding a laugh behind her hand.

Vision, ever the patient observer, helped keep the gift pile organized while the twins egged Nicky on to tear through them faster. By the time he got to Wanda and Vision’s oversized gift bag, there was already a mountain of discarded wrapping paper on the floor.

When he finally pulled out the contents, a high-tech LEGO set, a superhero costume, and a book about space, his face lit up like a Christmas tree. “THIS IS SO COOL!” he yelled, immediately throwing himself at Wanda and Vision in a grateful hug.

“We figured you’d like it,” Wanda said, ruffling his hair.

“I LOVE IT.”

Nat, watching the whole thing with an amused smirk, nudged Agatha. “Kid’s got a good racket going here. Think I could get people to buy me stuff if I started screaming about how it’s the best day ever?”

Agatha sighed. “You’d be lucky to get a sympathy drink.”

“Rude,” Nat muttered, stealing a bite of cake from Agatha’s plate anyway.

Meanwhile, Agatha was doing an excellent job of pretending Daniel didn’t exist. She barely acknowledged him, only making the absolute necessary polite small talk when Nicky was around. Other than that, she kept herself busy, refilling drinks, keeping an eye on the kids, making sure Nat didn’t get too drunk on birthday punch (because, somehow, she absolutely would).

Wanda, however, noticed. She slid up beside Agatha while Daniel was awkwardly standing alone near the snack table. “So, avoiding your ex like the plague, huh?”

Agatha didn’t even pretend to deny it. “Obviously.”

“I mean, fair,” Nat chimed in, appearing at Agatha’s other side like a devil on her shoulder. “Look at him. Just existing over there. Ugh.” She shuddered dramatically.

Wanda smirked. “God, I can’t stand men like him.”

Nat gasped. “Wanda. Are we about to bond over hating the same man?”

“I think we are,” Wanda said, pretending to wipe away a tear.

Agatha sighed, rubbing her temples. “I regret this already.”

“Too late,” Nat said cheerfully, slinging an arm around Wanda. “Welcome to the ‘Daniel Sucks’ fan club. Meetings are every Wednesday. We bring wine.”

“I’ll bring the snacks,” Wanda said, nodding solemnly.

“Oh, I like her,” Nat declared.

Agatha just groaned, staring longingly at the cake like it could save her.

As the sun dipped below the horizon, the party slowly wound down. The kids, fueled by sugar and excitement, were starting to crash, and the adults had reached that polite, lingering phase where they pretended they weren’t ready to leave but were very much thinking about their couches.

Daniel, thankfully, had taken the hint early and left, though not before reminding Agatha, twice, that he’d be in town for the next two days to spend time with Nicky. She had nodded stiffly, keeping her answers short, and had all but shoved him out the door before he could say anything else.

Now, with the house finally quiet and most of the mess cleaned up, Nicky was curled up on the couch, rubbing his eyes. Agatha crouched down beside him. “Alright, kiddo, bedtime.”

Instead of reaching for her, Nicky turned to Nat. “Can you put me to bed?” he mumbled sleepily.

Nat’s eyes widened slightly before she grinned. “Me? Wow. Big honor.” She scooped him up effortlessly, carrying him toward his room. “Alright, let’s get you tucked in, birthday boy.”

Agatha watched them disappear down the hall, feeling an odd warmth settle in her chest. Nat had always been good with Nicky, but there was something about seeing her in full “cool aunt” mode that made Agatha… soft. Not that she’d ever admit it.

With the house finally empty, Agatha sighed and slumped onto the couch. Her eyes flickered toward her phone facedown on the coffee table. She had been avoiding it all day, dreading whatever awaited her.

Taking a deep breath, she reached for it, hesitating for just a second before flipping it over. With a flick of her thumb, she pressed the power button. 

The screen stayed dark for a second, just long enough to make her think maybe, just maybe, she could still back out of this. Then, with an ominous little buzz, the phone came to life.

The notifications flooded in all at once. Messages. Missed calls. A string of texts stacking on top of each other, the preview screen flashing names she wasn’t ready to see.

Agatha stared at the flood of notifications, her thumb hovering over the screen. Nope. Absolutely not. She wasn’t dealing with this right now.

Without even glancing at the messages, Agatha swiped them away and tapped on Wanda’s contact instead. The phone rang twice before Wanda picked up.

“Well, well,” Wanda teased, her voice dripping with amusement. “She lives.”

Agatha rolled her eyes, sinking further into the couch. “Barely. Just calling to say thanks again for today. Nicky had the best time.”

“Oh, please. We had just as much fun,” Wanda said. “The boys are already asking when they can come back.”

Agatha smirked. “As long as they promise not to turn my living room into a wrestling ring again, they’re welcome anytime.”

“No promises,” Wanda said with a laugh.

They fell into easy conversation, trading complaints about the sugar-fueled chaos of the afternoon. For a moment, Agatha almost forgot about the mess of last night. Almost.

Then, casually, too casually, Wanda added, “By the way, I’m really happy for you.”

Agatha frowned. “Uh… thanks?”

“I mean, you’ve been so tense lately. It’s good to see you finally letting loose a little.”

Agatha’s grip on the phone tightened. “Wanda…”

“And honestly, you were overdue,” Wanda continued, her tone far too smug. “So really, congrats.”

Agatha’s stomach twisted. There was something in Wanda’s voice, too knowing, too pleased.

She shifted on the couch, suddenly feeling like she’d walked into a trap. “Uh-huh,” she said slowly. “And… what exactly am I being congratulated for?”

Wanda let out a soft hum, like she was savoring the moment. “Oh, you know,” she said lightly. “Finally getting some.”

Agatha froze.

Her brain stalled, her breath catching in her throat. “I—what?”

Wanda chuckled. “Oh, don’t be shy. It’s about time, really. I was starting to think you’d taken a vow of celibacy.”

Agatha opened her mouth, then closed it.

Her mind raced. What did Wanda know? Was she guessing? Was she messing with her?

Agatha swallowed, pulse pounding in her ears. “Wanda,” she said carefully, “where exactly did you hear that?”

Wanda’s laughter was warm, teasing.

“Oh,” she said, “I have my sources.”

Chapter 20

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Agatha’s heart started hammering in her chest. Her grip on the phone tightened as panic crept in, sharp and sudden.

She knows.

Her mind raced, replaying every second of the night before. Had Rio said something? Had someone seen them? 

Agatha sat up straighter on the couch, fingers gripping the phone so tightly her knuckles went white. She forced out a laugh, strained and brittle. “I… I don’t know what you’re talking about.”

Wanda made a low, amused sound on the other end. “Mmhm.”

“I didn’t—” Agatha’s voice caught, panic bubbling under the surface. “I mean, I wouldn’t—”

“You so would.”

Agatha’s heart slammed against her ribs. “Wanda, I did not—”

“Relax,” Wanda cut in, clearly enjoying herself. “I’m not interrogating you, Agatha. I just noticed a little something during Nickys party.”

Agatha blinked, mind spinning.

“What... what little something?” she asked, her voice pitching a little too high.

Wanda made a thoughtful noise, like she was savoring dragging this out. “Well, it could’ve been the way you were avoiding eye contact all afternoon… or how you practically sprinted away whenever someone mentioned last night.”

Agatha’s pulse thudded in her ears. Another pause. Then Wanda’s voice came through sweet and sharp.

“But,” Wanda drawled, “if I had to guess… I’d say it was the hickey on your neck that gave it away, darling.”

Agatha’s stomach plummeted.

Agatha’s stomach dropped. Her free hand shot to her neck on instinct, fingers brushing against the soft skin just beneath her collarbone, the exact spot Rio’s mouth had lingered.

Oh, fuck.

Agatha opened her mouth, but nothing came out.

Wanda’s soft laugh filled the silence. “I knew it,” she sing songed.

Agatha's mind short-circuited between full on panic and the urge to throw her phone out the nearest window.

Goddamn it. 

Wanda laughed outright at her silence. “So? Are you gonna tell me who the lucky one is, or do I have to bribe Nat for the gossip?”

Agatha's mind short circuited between full on panic and the urge to throw her phone out the nearest window.

“Wanda,” she hissed, trying to salvage some dignity. “It’s—it's not what you think.”

“Oh?” Wanda teased. Right. Because you accidentally got bitten on the neck? Happens all the time.”

Agatha clenched her jaw, heat prickling at the back of her neck, cursing herself for not checking the mirror more closely.

Wanda’s voice softened, teasing but warm. “I’m happy for you, Agatha. Really. It’s about time someone knocked that chip off your shoulder, at least for one night.”

Agatha’s throat tightened.

If only Wanda knew who was responsible for the maroon mark she saw near her collarbone… 

Agatha barely heard whatever Wanda was saying next. Her mind was too busy rewinding, rewinding to every damn interaction she’d had today.

If Wanda saw it, probably everyone had. 

And then it hit her.

Nat saw it.

Nat had to have seen it. And she had let her walk all day with the damn mark on her neck.

That fucking bitch.

Agatha’s eye twitched, her grip on the phone tightening. Oh, she was going to kill her. Slowly. Painfully. Maybe she’d start by poisoning her coffee, nothing lethal, just enough to make her suffer. Then she’d move on to more creative punishments.

And Rio.

The audacity. The absolute gall of that woman. Marking her like she was some possession. As if Agatha wouldn't notice. As if she wouldn’t wake up, see the evidence, and lose her entire goddamn mind.

She was going to kill both of them.

But first—

“Alright, I’ve had enough of your shit,” Agatha cut Wanda off, voice dry as sandpaper. “Enjoy your little fantasy, Maximoff, but I am hanging up now.”

Wanda was still laughing when Agatha stabbed at the red icon on her screen.

With a slow, deep inhale, she let her phone drop onto the couch beside her.

And then she started brainstorming.

Snarky responses. She needed a shield, something to throw at Wanda next time she opened her mouth with that smug tone. Something witty, something cutting—

But before she could settle on a solid comeback, rage overtook logic when she came back to Nat. She knew.

That sneaky, smug, traitorous little—

Agatha shot up from the couch, hands clenched into fists. Then, in a voice loud enough to shake the walls, she roared:

“NATASHA ROMANOFF, GET YOUR ASS IN HERE!”

Nat strolled in with the casual confidence of someone who knew they were in trouble but had absolutely no intention of apologizing for it. She leaned against the doorway, arms crossed, lips curled into the smuggest smirk Agatha had ever seen.

“What’s up, sunshine?”

Agatha, still fuming, narrowed her eyes. “You know exactly what’s up, you absolute menace.”

Nat blinked, all wide eyed innocence. “I really don’t.”

Agatha pointed an accusatory finger at her neck. “Oh, really? Then explain why Wanda just congratulated me for getting laid.”

Nat gasped dramatically, pressing a hand to her chest. “Wanda knows? Wow. Word travels fast.”

“Oh, don’t you start.” Agatha marched up to her, stabbing her finger into Nat’s shoulder. “You knew. You saw it, and you didn’t say a damn thing. You let me walk around all day with—”

“With receipts?” Nat finished for her, grinning.

Agatha let out a strangled noise that was somewhere between a growl and a scream. “I swear to God—”

Nat cut her off by poking her cheek. “Look at you, getting all worked up over a little love bite. It’s adorable.”

Agatha swatted her hand away. “Do you have a death wish?”

Nat grinned. “Not particularly, but if I did, I’d want you to be the one to take me out.”

Agatha groaned, dragging her hands down her face. “I should kill you. I should—”

“—Be thanking me?” Nat suggested. “Because I totally covered for you, by the way. Wanda asked if I knew anything, and I played dumb.” She paused “well technically I don't know anything because you refuse to tell me who it was but the evidence speak for it self”

“You are dumb.”

“Wow. Hurtful.”

Agatha huffed, arms crossed tightly. “You’re enjoying this way too much.”

Nat shrugged, grinning. “Listen, I’m just happy you’re out there.” Her voice softened, just a little. “you deserved a moment to finally let loose. After everything…” 

Agatha’s lips pressed into a thin line, caught between irritation and something heavier, something she wasn’t ready to acknowledge.

Nat, as always, was too perceptive.

She nudged Agatha’s arm lightly. “So? You gonna tell me who it was?”

Agatha scoffed. “Absolutely not.”

Nat sighed dramatically. “Fine. Be mysterious. But if you start getting cryptic poetry texts from you at three in the morning, I will know.”

Agatha rolled her eyes and shoved Nat toward the door. “Out.”

Nat laughed as she went, tossing one last grin over her shoulder. “Hey, just a little advice, next time check a mirror before facing the public.”

Agatha picked up a throw pillow and launched it at her head.

With Nat finally gone, Agatha exhaled and collapsed onto the couch. Her phone sat on the table, still waiting, still taunting her. She had been putting it off long enough.

Alright. Just rip the band-aid off.

She grabbed it, unlocking the screen with a swipe of her thumb. The notifications blinked back at her, texts from Wanda, a few from some other acquaintances, an email about some book event she definitely wasn’t attending.

But nothing from her.

Her grip on the phone tightened.

Nothing from Rio.

Agatha stared at the screen, waiting, as if something might magically appear just because she willed it hard enough.

Nothing.

Her jaw clenched.

The realization settled like a stone in her gut. She scrolled, refreshed her messages, even checked her missed calls, as if maybe, somehow, she’d just overlooked it. Maybe there was a single text hidden between all the others, half-hearted, so that happened waiting for her.

But no.

Not a damn thing.

Her jaw clenched.

Oh. Oh, so that’s how we’re playing this?

She wasn’t sure what she had expected. She had spent the entire day dreading the moment she’d turn on her phone, bracing herself for whatever fresh chaos Rio would throw at her. A smug, knowing text. A cryptic message. A simple, Did you dream about me?, the kind of thing that would’ve sent her spiraling.

And yet, now that it wasn’t there… she felt something almost worse.

Now that it wasn’t here, she was mad.

She was the one who ran. The one who left without a word, without so much as a glance back. She had been the one to decide there was nothing left to say.

So why did it piss her off that Rio was acting like she agreed?

It wasn’t even about the kiss.

…Except that was a lie, wasn’t it?

Because that was the moment burned into her skull. The way Rio had kissed her, the way she had looked at her afterward, with something dark and knowing in her eyes, something that told Agatha that Rio had seen everything. Every hesitation, every shaky inhale, every damn thing she didn’t want her to see.

And Agatha had run.

She hadn’t thought, hadn’t processed, just bolted before Rio could say anything, before she could smirk and make some biting little comment about how Agatha had wanted it. Because she had, and that was the worst part.

She wanted Rio to have texted.

Not because she wanted to talk. Not because she had anything to say. But because, what? Rio got to decide they weren’t speaking? Rio got to just move on like nothing happened?

Agatha let out a breath, tossing the phone onto the couch beside her like it had personally offended her.

This was stupid.

Agatha had gotten exactly what she wanted all along.

Rio wasn’t texting her. She was leaving her alone.

No sly messages, no teasing, no dragging her into some exhausting push and pull.

It was what Agatha had wanted. What she had told herself she needed.

So why did it feel like losing?

She ran a hand down her face, exhaling sharply. This was pathetic. She should be relieved. 

She was relieved. 

This was the best possible outcome. It meant she could pretend last night never happened, could file it away under reckless, stupid mistakes and move on like she always did.

And yet, that gnawing irritation wouldn’t leave her alone. Because, no matter how much she wanted to deny it, a small, irrational part of her wanted Rio to have texted. To have acknowledged it, something.

Because now it felt like Rio had decided it didn’t matter. Like she was the one brushing it off, moving on without a second thought.

And that, somehow, was even worse.

—---------------------

Sunday was a blur of movement and noise; exactly what Agatha needed.

She, Nat, and Nicky spent the afternoon at the ice rink, where Nicky wobbled around on skates with a mix of excitement and frustration while Nat, ever the show-off, glided effortlessly across the ice. Agatha stuck to the sidelines, coaching Nicky through his attempts while Nat took every opportunity to spin and skate backward just to be annoying.

After that, they grabbed hot chocolate to warm up before heading to the cinema. Nicky insisted on getting the biggest popcorn available, which resulted in half of it ending up on the floor before the previews even finished. Nat kept up a running sarcastic commentary on the movie, whispering dramatic gasps at predictable plot twists while Nicky giggled beside her. Agatha let herself get lost in it, the warmth, the noise, the simplicity of it all.

For a whole day, she didn’t think about Rio.

But Monday was coming. And with it, the inevitable.

Nat was staying with Nicky all week, which meant Agatha had no excuse. She had to go back to work.

And she had to see her.

—-----------

Monday arrived far too soon.

Agatha stared at the ceiling of her bedroom, the early morning light filtering through her blinds, and seriously considered calling in sick. Her throat wasn’t sore, her head didn’t hurt, and she wasn’t even remotely ill, but surely, there had to be some kind of medical exception for this.

She could call in sick. 

Just roll over, grab her phone, and fire off a quick email. It would be easy.

Except she didn’t call in sick. 

Ever .

What was happening to her?

She was Agatha Harkness, for God’s sake. One of the top OB-GYNs in the country, maybe the world, depending on who you asked. She had trained under the best, delivered hundreds of babies, and performed some of the most complicated surgeries imaginable. She had been in life-or-death situations more times than she could count.

And yet, here she was, lying in bed like a coward because she had kissed one of her colleagues.

Stupid.

She wasn’t some flustered teen sneaking glances at a crush across the high school floor. She was a grown woman, a damn good doctor, and she had worked too hard for too long to let something as ridiculous as this shake her.

So why did it feel like she was standing at the edge of a cliff?

Agatha groaned, pressing the heels of her hands into her eyes. She was mad. Furious, even. At Rio. At herself. At the entire ridiculous situation.

She wanted to march into work, track Rio down, and…..what? Demand an explanation? Pretend it never happened? Kiss her again just to make a point? 

She exhaled sharply and sat up. 

No. She was being ridiculous. She needed to get a grip.

She had a job to do.

And she sure as hell wasn’t going to let Rio Vidal (or herself) get in the way of that. 

She should be able to walk into that hospital like nothing had happened. Like it was just another Monday. But instead, there was this… gnawing, twisting thing in her stomach. 

With a sharp exhale, she shoved the blankets off and forced herself out of bed. She had a job to do.

And if she had to see Rio?

Well, she would just have to act like she didn’t care. Cuz it was true. She didn't. 

She moved on autopilot through her morning routine, determined not to let anything, not even the mess in her head, ruin her day. She kissed Nicky on the forehead, ruffled his hair, and ignored the way he grumbled about it.

"Be good for Nat, alright?" she said.

"I’m always good," Nicky declared, already focused on his cereal.

Nat snorted. "Debatable."

Agatha smirked. "See you later, troublemaker."

"Have fun at work!" Nat called after her with an exaggerated wink.

Agatha flipped her off on her way out the door.

The drive to the hospital was uneventful, but her grip on the steering wheel was tight the whole way. She was fine. She was completely, absolutely fine.

Then, just as she pulled into the parking lot, her phone buzzed.

She glanced at the screen. Dr. Calderu.

“Agatha; How are you?? I need to see you at my office before rounds”

Agatha's stomach twisted. Lilia wasn’t the kind of person to waste time with unnecessary meetings. Whatever this was, it was important. And important in a hospital usually meant bad.

With a sigh, she grabbed her coat and strode inside the hospital, heading straight for Lilia’s office. When she arrived, the door was ajar, and to her shock, there was already someone sitting in the office. For a moment she stopped breathing.

Because sitting there, legs crossed, poised like she belonged in the pages of a high-fashion magazine,,was Rio, wearing a dress.

A deep green one that hugged her in ways that should have been illegal. 

She was sitting in one of the chairs, legs crossed in a way that made it look like she belonged in a high end magazine. The dress was blue, hugging her body in ways Agatha was too mad to appreciate, and was borderline criminal in the best possible way. And, of course, there were the heels. High, sharp heels. 

She looked up as Agatha entered, her gaze cool and indifferent, but there was a slight twitch at the corner of her mouth, as if she were just waiting for Agatha to react.

Agatha froze.

Rio glanced up at her, her expression unreadable before one perfectly arched brow lifted ever so slightly. "Ah. You"

Agatha saw red; her stomach twisted. She took a breath and let it out slowly, but it didn’t help.

"What the hell is this?" Agatha demanded, her voice sharper than she intended. "Is this some kind of intervention? Am I being audited?"

Rio raised a brow, clearly amused by Agatha’s frustration. "Relax, Harkness I know the same as you know I presume," her smirk not meeting her eyes .

Agatha’s heart pounded, her frustration building. "Relax? You’re sitting here—" She gestured vaguely at Rio, who was practically lounging in her chair. "dressed like you’re about to do anything but show up at a runway show, and you’re telling me to relax?"

Rio blinked slowly, as though she didn’t have a care in the world. "I like looking good."

Agatha was about to lose it.

"Why are you here?" she snapped. "What is going on? I got a text from Lilia, and now I walk into this ridiculousness?"

"Someone's in a mood" Rio said slowly without looking at her. 

Oh, Agatha wanted to kill her.

Just then, the door to Lilia’s office creaked open, and she walked in, glancing between the two of them. Her eyes lingered on Agatha for a second, but she didn’t comment on the tension.

"Agatha," Lilia greeted her coolly. "Glad you could join us."

Agatha gritted her teeth. This was it. She was about to explode. 

Lilia, for her part, looked perfectly at ease, but she was clearly ready to get to the point. "We need to talk," she said.

About what, Agatha wanted to scream, but she was too busy wondering why she was feeling so completely out of control.

Agatha clenched her jaw and turned to Lilia. "What is happening?"

Lilia leaned back in her chair. "Well, if you’d stop bickering for five seconds, I could tell you."

Agatha crossed her arms. "Fine. Enlighten me."

Rio hummed under her breath, glancing at her nails. "Yes, please, enlighten us, Dr. Calderu. Some of us have rounds to get to."
