Agatha snapped her gaze back to Rio. "Oh, I’m sorry, am I inconveniencing you?"

Rio’s lips twitched. "A little, yes."

Oh, that was it.

Agatha’s hands twitched at her sides, resisting the urge to throw something. She wasn’t sure what was more infuriating, Rio’s complete indifference to their situation or the fact that she somehow managed to look effortlessly flawless while doing it.

Lilia didn’t even blink. "Enough you two. We need to talk about the trauma certification"

Agatha blinked. "Uh… what? That’s it?" She half expected Lilia to hand her a gold star and a congratulatory handshake. She’d been working her ass off on this certification, and she was pretty sure she’d nailed it. “ So tell us chief… Did we pass the trauma certification with flying colors? Because I’m expecting a nice little thank you for keeping the residents from imploding on each other, you know. I think we did an amazing job and- “

"No," Lilia interrupted, holding her hand up. "You and Dr. Vidal didn’t pass it with flying colors. You didn't do an amazing job. You failed half of them. Half of the other ones didn’t even finish the certification because the little stunt you two pulled in the rain"

Lilia sighed heavily. "You terrorized them. And now I’ve got complaints stacked up. You need to apologize. And not just some email or half-hearted note; face them."

Agatha's eyes widened. "Wait. So, we’re not getting congratulated for our rigorous standards?"

Lilia looked like she wanted to strangle both of them. "You’re getting nothing but an apology and a reminder that we’re in a hospital, not a survivalist boot camp. You’re lucky you’re not getting suspended."

"Suspended?" Agatha scoffed, throwing her hands up. "For teaching them the real pressures of being a surgeon? Please. They should be thanking us for showing them what it takes."

Rio crossed her arms with a smug look.  "Exactly. What’s the problem? A little rain never hurt anyone. If they can’t handle a little water and mud, maybe they should be looking for another line of work."

"No," Lilia interrupted, holding up a hand. "You were not right. Two of them ended up with pneumonia."

Rio’s eyes widened in disbelief. "Pneumonia?! How did they catch pneumonia from standing in the rain? What are they, delicate flowers? "

"I told you it was a terrible idea," Agatha muttered, throwing a pointed glare at Rio. "But no, you had to make it dramatic—‘Let’s do trauma certification in a thunderstorm, Agatha. It’s for their character.’"

Rio just shrugged with her signature smugness. "They were fine."

"Fine?!" Lilia exploded. "This is not fine! We could get a lawsuit!"

Rio raised a single eyebrow. "The rest of them finished, right? They’re tougher than the rest of the whiners."

Lilia shot them both an incredulous look. "Enough the two of you. Not only did you fail them but some of them have even complained about the way you terrorized them during the entire process. There’s talk about filing formal complaints."

"Complaints?!" Agatha almost choked on her own frustration. "Complaints because we made them push through tough training? How is that a complaint?! When I was in residency i was put though worst"

Rio snorted. "They should have been able to handle a little rain. Honestly, if they can’t deal with a wet jacket and a little hypothermia, maybe they shouldn’t be in the OR."

Lilia narrowed her eyes. "I’m serious, both of you. These residents are scared to even look at the two of you"

Agatha threw her hands up in the air. "What do you mean, ‘what am I going to do about it’? You want me to wrap them in cotton balls and give them a bottle of chamomile tea? Maybe a spa day to help them recover from the trauma of getting a little wet?"

Rio folded her arms, looking amused. "Honestly, I’m starting to think they should just be grateful we didn’t make them carry the dummies uphill. You know, real trauma training. Some of them—" she paused, glancing at Agatha with a half-smile, "—just need to toughen up."

"Yeah, exactly," Agatha agreed, practically waving her arms around. 

Lilia blinked twice, clearly not on the same page. "If you two keep talking like this, I will personally—"

"We’re just saying," Agatha interrupted with an exaggerated shrug. "If they want to be surgeons, they need to learn how to handle a little discomfort. It’s part of the job!"

Rio nodded sagely. "Honestly, I don’t know how anyone survives in this field without a couple of minor injuries and mental breakdowns. It builds character."

Agatha shook her head, sighing heavily. "Right. And if they can’t handle a little water and a few pushes from their attendings, they might want to rethink their career paths.."

Lilia looked between the two of them, still unimpressed. "Both of you are ridiculous, but there’s no getting around it. You need to work on your approach, because this—" she waved her hand vaguely, "—this isn’t going to fly again. Got it?"

Agatha and Rio exchanged a look. "Understood," Agatha said in a completely sarcastic tone. "We’ll be sure to ease up on the rain and trauma drills in the future. Maybe a group hug and a meditation session instead."

Lilia didn’t laugh, but Rio did, a little too loud for Agatha’s liking.

Lilia sighed deeply, rubbing her temples. "You’re both impossible. But you will apologize, or I swear I’ll make the next few months for you so brutal you’ll be begging for the rain."

Agatha let out a sharp sigh. "This is ridiculous."

Rio raised an eyebrow. "We’re sorry, Lilia. So sorry. Happy?"

Lilia shot them both a venomous look. "Not until I hear it from your lips. Apologize to the residents in person. And make it believable."

With a groan, Agatha and Rio walked out of the office. As soon as the door closed behind them, Agatha whirled on Rio. 

"This is your fault. You pushed for that stupid rain test. You’re the reason I’m apologizing to a bunch of crybabies who can’t even handle a little cold air."

Rio raised her hands innocently. "Me? I was just trying to help them build character. Tough love as you say."

"Yeah? Well, they’ve got character. Pneumonia, too." Agatha shot her a death glare. 

Rio grinned mischievously. "You know, I’m actually starting to enjoy this. Watching you go all ‘Oh no, my pride’ is actually a lot of fun."

Agatha shook her head, exasperated. "I am not this person. I’m one of the top OB-GYNs in the county, if not the world, and now I’m here, apologizing to a bunch of whiners because of you."

Rio laughed. "Well, if you don’t like it, maybe we can have another ‘special certification’ to help you unwind." Her voice dripped with sarcasm.

"Stop it!" Agatha snapped, turning to storm down the hall, but Rio easily matched her pace.

"You know, Agatha, if you’re really mad about this, you could always write it in a nice, passive-aggressive email. Just start every sentence with ‘I was forced to apologize to you by my boss…’," Rio teased.

"I swear to God, one more word out of your mouth and I’ll strangle you with my stethoscope," Agatha muttered

Rio chuckled darkly. "It’s hilarious, Agatha. I don't like this but I’m fine with it, you on the other hand, might explode with all your righteous indignation."

Agatha shot her a glare. "I am not going to apologize for teaching them how to survive under pressure. It’s a skill. But here I am, caving in to this ridiculous demand from Lilia, who clearly thinks we’re running a daycare."

"Well, you did kind of turn it into one," Rio said with a grin that could only be described as infuriating. "I mean, what’s her plan anyways? Hand them a juice box and tell them they did a great job for trying?"

Agatha clenched her teeth, trying not to snap. "Don’t even start with me. You’re the one who insisted on making them stand out in the rain like it was some kind of movie scene." Agatha growled. "I am not apologizing for your idiotic idea. You could have at least backed me up when I said this was a bad idea."

"Oh, come on," Rio said, clearly enjoying this, "it wasn’t that bad. Sure, they got pneumonia, but that’s basically a badge of honor in some circles, right?"

"Stop it!" Agatha hissed, but the grin on Rio’s face only made her angrier. "You know what? Fine. I’ll apologize. I’ll say ‘sorry’ to a bunch of whiny little residents who can’t take a little rain. How’s that for you, huh?"

Rio leaned in, her voice low and teasing. "I can just imagine you standing in front of them, saying, ‘Sorry for traumatizing you with the rain and having you work through it like professionals.’ It’s a masterpiece really."

Agatha shot her a look that could have melted steel. "I am doing this because Lilia said so and I actually appreciate my job and don’t think for a second I won’t make sure everyone knows this was all you."

"Sure, sure, blame it all on me," Rio said, clearly not even phased. "That’s what you do best, right?"

"Stop it," Agatha almost shouted, but she quickly lowered her voice, glancing around to make sure no one had overheard. "This isn’t a joke."

Rio held up her hands in mock surrender, but something was different this time. Agatha noticed it immediately. The usual infuriating smirk was absent. Rio’s expression was calm, almost neutral, and her tone lacked the playful edge Agatha had come to expect. It was unsettling, like the absence of a familiar sound in a room you’ve known your whole life.

And with that, Rio was gone, disappearing down the hallway, leaving Agatha standing there, staring after her in frustration.

Agatha’s mind raced as she replayed the interaction. Rio hadn’t teased her. Not really. There had been no sly remarks, no lingering glances, no smug satisfaction. It was as if the incident   had never happened.

Agatha stood in the hallway, her chest rising and falling with the effort of keeping her composure. The absence of Rio’s usual smirk, the lack of her biting sarcasm—it was jarring. Agatha had expected a fight, a snarky comment, something . But instead, Rio had just… walked away. 

The thought burned hotter than any argument ever could.

—----

The rest of the day passed in a blur of appointments, surgeries, and paperwork. Agatha threw herself into her work, using it as a distraction from the storm brewing in her mind. But no matter how hard she tried to focus, her thoughts kept circling back to Rio. To the way she had looked at her in the hallway. To the way she had just… walked away. She needed to do something about it. 

She stormed down the hallway, her heels clicking against the tile with the force of her irritation. This was karma, she was sure of it. Some cruel, cosmic joke at her expense. She’d spent the last eight hours seething over Rio, wanting to see her stumble, wanting to watch her squirm—and instead, here she was, being forced to eat her words in front of a room full of whiny, pneumonia-prone residents. It was humiliating. Infuriating. She had survived worse, but this? This was a new form of torture.

And she wasn’t about to let Rio enjoy it.

If she had to apologize, she was going to do it on her terms, without Rio’s smug face hovering in the background. Let Rio miss it and look like the unprofessional one. That would be her revenge. Small, petty, but satisfying.

Agatha turned the corner sharply, and slammed right into Wanda.

“Jesus, Harkness,” Wanda huffed, steadying herself before Agatha could knock her flat. “Where’s the fire?”

Agatha stepped back, barely acknowledging her. “I have to go apologize.”

That made Wanda pause. Her brows lifted, her lips twitching. “I’m sorry, what?”

Agatha sighed through her teeth, already regretting saying anything. “You heard me.”

“Oh, I did,” Wanda said, her grin stretching wider. “I just never thought I’d live to see the day. Agatha Harkness, apologizing?” She shook her head, her amusement practically radiating off of her. “This, I have to see.”

Agatha groaned. “Absolutely not.”

But Wanda was already falling into step beside her, far too entertained to be deterred. “Oh, come on, don’t be like that. You can’t drop something this good and expect me to just walk away. Who’s the lucky soul on the receiving end of this historic event?”

Agatha gritted her teeth. “A room full of crybabies who think rain is a trauma.”

“Oh, this keeps getting better.” Wanda was practically beaming. “I would pay to witness this.”

“Fantastic,” Agatha deadpanned. “Get your checkbook ready.”

Wanda smirked, unbothered by Agatha’s hostility. “Oh, don’t worry, I don’t mind taking a front-row seat for free.”

Agatha shot her a glare, but Wanda only grinned wider, happily tagging along as they made their way to the conference room. 

Minutes later Agatha stood at the front of the conference room, arms crossed, her expression resting somewhere between unimpressed and homicidal. The group of residents before her looked like a bunch of scolded children.

“Alright,” Agatha began, her tone as warm and inviting as a slab of ice. “I’ve been strongly encouraged, and by that, I mean blackmailed, into apologizing for the trauma I apparently inflicted upon you during the certification exercise.” She paused, letting her gaze sweep over them, her lips pressing into a thin, deeply unamused line. “So. Here it is. I’m sorry.”

Silence. A few residents exchanged nervous glances. One actually gulped.

She exhaled dramatically, as if this was the single most exhausting task she had undertaken in her entire career. “I’m sorry,” she continued, tone dripping with exaggerated patience, “that some of you have yet to experience water in your lives.  I’m sorry that standing in wet clothes for a few hours was apparently too much for you to bear. I’m sorry that, instead of rising to the challenge, some of you decided to… what was it? Oh, right. Catch pneumonia.”

A tentative hand went up. “Uh, Dr. Harkness, are you saying you’re not actually—”

“Oh, no, I am deeply sorry,” Agatha interrupted, placing a hand over her chest in mock sincerity. “I am devastated that your fragile constitutions couldn’t handle moisture. You poor, delicate creatures. How will you ever survive the horrors of, I don’t know, washing your hands?”

Someone stifled a laugh. Others looked like they wanted to crawl under the table.

 “Careful, Harkness,” Wanda whispered. “You wouldn’t want to emotionally damage them.”

Agatha turned to her with the slow precision of someone considering murder. “Oh, you mean the way nature emotionally damaged them by daring to rain?” She looked back at the residents and sighed dramatically. “Fine. Let me be clear. I’m also sorry that I assumed you were all capable of enduring mild discomfort without falling apart.”

One of the residents, a young woman who looked like she had been through worse, spoke up. “So… what exactly are we supposed to take away from this?”

Agatha’s lips twitched. “Take away that you might want to grow a spine before you’re alone in an OR at 3 a.m. with a patient coding and no one to hold your hand”

Wanda finally pushed off the wall, stepping forward with the air of someone about to smooth things over. “What Dr. Harkness means…in her own… distinctive way is that we believe in you. We pushed you because we know you can handle it.” 

A few residents nodded, some looking chastened, others relieved. Agatha huffed. “Any questions?”

No one moved.

“Good.” She turned on her heel. “Now, if you’ll excuse me, I have actual work to do.”

As she strode out, Wanda caught up with her in the hallway, smirking. “Well,” she said, voice full of amusement, “that was… inspiring.”

Agatha shot her a look. “Do not start.”

Wanda held up her hands in mock innocence. “Hey, I’m just saying, that was the most Agatha Harkness apology I’ve ever heard. Lilia is going to love it.”

Agatha rolled her eyes, but somewhere deep, deep down, beneath all the irritation, there was a flicker of satisfaction.

She hadn’t backed down. She hadn’t caved.

And if the residents learned something? Well, that was their problem.

Agatha had barely made it down the hall when she heard quick footsteps behind her. She gritted her teeth, already done with this conversation before it even began.

“Dr. Harkness!”

She exhaled through her nose. Of course.

Agatha turned sharply, expecting some fragile little thing on the verge of tears, but instead, she found herself staring at her .

The brunette from the trauma certification.

Kate… something .

Unlike the rest of her whining classmates, she hadn’t completely embarrassed herself that day. Agatha vaguely remembered her keeping up, at least better than the others. Which, granted, wasn’t a high bar, but it was enough to keep Agatha from immediately dismissing her.

Kate shifted under her gaze, clearly bracing herself for whatever brutality was about to come out of Agatha’s mouth.

“Well?” Agatha crossed her arms. “Do you actually need something, or are you just here to waste my time?”

Kate swallowed, then straightened her shoulders like she was committing to this moment. “I want you to mentor me.”

Agatha blinked. “You what?”

“Mentor me,” Kate repeated, less hesitant now. “I want to be an OBGYN, and you’re the best.”

Agatha stared at her, unimpressed. “Flattery won’t get you anywhere with me.”

Kate nodded. “I figured.”

There was a pause, and Agatha narrowed her eyes.

“You’re serious.”

Kate nodded again.

Agatha tilted her head slightly, considering her. She was young, obviously. Too green to fully understand what she was asking. But there was something there, a stubbornness, maybe even a little recklessness.

Still, Agatha wasn’t exactly in the business of hand-holding.

She sighed, already regretting entertaining this conversation at all. “First of all, what’s your name?”

Kate blinked. “Kate.”

Agatha raised an eyebrow.

“…Bishop,” Kate added quickly.

Agatha hummed. “Right. Bishop.” She let the name roll around in her head for a moment, then shrugged. “No.”

Kate frowned. “No?”

“No,” Agatha repeated. “Mentorship requires patience, which I don’t have. You want someone to hold your hand while you stumble through this program? Find someone else.”

Kate opened her mouth, but Agatha was already turning on her heel.

“I’m not looking for someone to hold my hand,” Kate called after her. “I just need someone who’ll make me better.”

Agatha almost kept walking.

She was over this conversation, over this day, over these sniveling little residents and their ridiculous requests.

“No,” she said again, sharper this time, not even turning back. “You don’t get to waltz up to me, ask for my time, and expect me to care.”

Kate didn’t move, didn’t flinch. “I don’t expect you to care. I expect you to teach.”

 

That made Agatha pause. Just for a second.

She exhaled through her nose, eyes flicking up toward the ceiling as if it held the patience she clearly lacked.

She should say no.

 

She should tell this overconfident intern to get lost and go find someone with more compassion and less contempt.

But then…

 

Then she thought about Rio.

About Lilia watching them both. Judging them.

And what better way to get ahead than to do something Rio wouldn’t?

Agatha had no interest in mentorship, but she did have an interest in proving she was more than just a brilliant surgeon, she was an asset. And if taking on an eager little intern put her one step ahead of Rio in Lilia’s eyes?

Well…. She could suffer through it.

Agatha turned, fixing Kate with a stare. “Fine. You want me to mentor you? Congratulations, Bishop. You’re on my rotation starting now.”

Kate’s brows shot up, clearly surprised it had actually worked. “Wait seriously?”

“Don’t make me regret it.”

Kate straightened. “I won’t.”

“Good.” Agatha narrowed her eyes. “Because if you screw up, I will not be gentle about it.”

Kate smirked. “I figured.”

Agatha huffed, already regretting this decision, and turned on her heel. “Hope you like hell, Bishop. Because you just signed up for it.”

Kate didn’t argue, and that, at least, earned her a few points in Agatha’s book.

As Kate stood there, looking all smug like she’d just won the lottery, Agatha’s gaze finally dropped to her scrubs.

Purple.

Bright, obnoxious purple.

Agatha immediately grimaced. Just like that, whatever microscopic sliver of respect she might have almost gained for this kid vanished into thin air.

“Never mind,” she said flatly, waving a dismissive hand. “I take it back. You’re off my rotation.”

Kate blinked. “Wait—what? Why?”

Agatha gestured vaguely at her like it should be obvious . “ That. ”

Kate glanced down at herself, frowning. “My scrubs?”

“Yes. Your hideous purple scrubs.”

Kate looked back up, thoroughly confused. “What’s wrong with purple?”

Agatha scoffed. “Purple is my color.”

Kate actually had the audacity to laugh. “Are you serious?”

“Deadly.” Agatha crossed her arms. “You want to learn from me? First rule, burn those scrubs and never wear them again.”

Kate snorted. “So, just to be clear, my entire future as an OBGYN depends on not wearing purple?”

Agatha tilted her head. “Now you’re getting it.”

Kate grinned. “Wow. I was expecting you to be tough, but this is a whole new level of insane.”

Agatha smirked, finally turning away. “You have no idea, Bishop.”

—--------------------------

The next few days went by as they always did.

Daniel left for New York. Good riddance. Agatha didn’t have to think about her ex-husband again until Nicky’s next birthday, and that was a beautiful thing.

Then Nat left. Less beautiful.

She wasn’t about to admit, to anyone, that it affected her. But it did.

Nat had lingered in the doorway before leaving, squinting at Agatha like she knew something was off. “Promise me you’re not gonna go radio silent again.”

Agatha rolled her eyes. “I work, Natasha. That’s not ‘radio silent.’ “

Nat gave her an unimpressed look. “Yeah, well, I know you. You’ve pulled the ‘I’m too busy’ card before, and next thing I know, you’ve fallen off the face of the earth. So promise me you won’t be a complete hermit this time.”

“That’s called ‘being an adult with a job.’”

“You know what I mean.”

Unfortunately, she did. Nat had seen her disappear into herself before, weeks of dodging calls, texts, the whole hermit act. Agatha huffed, exasperated. 

“Fine,” Agatha sighed, pretending to be put out. “I promise.”

Nat raised an eyebrow, still skeptical. “You better.”

With that, Nat was gone, and Agatha was left to pretend like she didn’t care.

She had managed to keep herself occupied all week. Between torturing Kate in her work hours and spending time with Nat and Nicky in her off work hours, she hadn’t let herself think too much. There was no time to dwell. No time to let her mind wander to places it shouldn’t.But now, Saturday morning, Nat was gone as of a few hours ago, and Nicky was at Wanda’s house to spend some time with the twins for the entire weekend. 

And the thoughts Agatha had shoved into a dark corner of her mind all week? They were back .

She refused to sit in them.

Her phone buzzed with an email. A last-minute request for a surgeon to pick up a 24-hour shift.

Agatha didn’t hesitate. Yes.

Almost immediately after, she shot off a message to Kate.

“ If I’m doing a 24 hour shift on a weekend, you’re doing it with me. If you want to be taught, you have to suffer”

Kate’s response was almost instant.

“ This feels illegal, but okay”

Agatha smirked.

Good.

Agatha felt like the luckiest woman on the planet. She had successfully managed to avoid the thoughts that had been threatening to make her way back into her mind all week. And now she had gotten herself 24 hours free of her own thoughts, and to top it off, she was getting paid for the privilege. 

Agatha: 1, Universe: 0.

And then, as if the universe had been watching her with a wicked sense of humor, it decided to even the score.

Agatha froze in the doorway of the trauma pit, her brain short-circuiting for a moment. No. No, no, no, no, no.  

There, in the middle of the room, wearing scrubs that were way too tight to be legal, was the exact person Agatha had taken this shift to avoid in the first place. She had signed up for this shift in the hopes of burying her thoughts under a mountain of medical cases, only to have the universe deliver Rio Vidal in all her smug, scrubs wearing glory.

Agatha’s eyes twitched. Of course it’s her.

The universe had just handed her a migraine on a silver platter. 

The universe was a cunt.

Agatha sighed loudly, rubbing her temples. “Agatha: 1, Universe: 1,” she muttered to herself.

Chapter End Notes

Agatha, Agatha, Agatha... you made your bed, now lie in it....

Chapter 21

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Agatha had been so close to winning.

She had secured herself 24 hours of distraction; a whole shift of grueling surgeries, and mind numbing paperwork. She could almost taste the sweet relief of keeping herself busy, of avoiding everything. She had been winning.

And then the universe, in its never ending spite, decided to humble her.

Her eyes twitched.

It was like some cosmic joke. Every single time Agatha thought she had the upper hand since moving to Minnesota, the universe would take one look at her efforts and say, “absolutely not, bitch”

She should have known. She should have checked before signing up for this shift. But no, she had been so desperate for a distraction, so eager to shove her thoughts into the abyss, that she had walked right into the exact situation she was trying to avoid.

This was proof. Proof that God hated her.

Her palms began to sweat as she glanced around, her eyes landing on the one thing she was trying to escape.

Rio hadn’t noticed her yet, which meant Agatha still had time to turn around and walk in the opposite direction. Maybe she could fake an emergency. Maybe she could—

“Dr. Harkness!”

Agatha squeezed her eyes shut, inhaling slowly through her nose.

Of course. Of course she couldn’t.

She had no time for this. She had no time to deal with her emotions right now. Not with this shift, not with Rio, not with anything.

“Shit,” she muttered under her breath.

Rio looked up, her expression as unbothered as ever. “Morning, Harkness”

She turned just as Kate jogged up, holding out a cup of coffee like she was presenting some grand peace offering.

“Brought you coffee,” Kate said proudly, clearly not understanding the severity of the situation. 

Agatha snatched it without comment, too busy mentally cursing the entire universe, and Kate. She could already feel the headache forming.

She had one plan. One. And now, not only was Rio here, but she was stuck with the intern too.

God was testing her.

And then, as if this situation wasn’t already catastrophic, a voice drawled—

“Why are you here?”

Agatha raised an eyebrow and turned slowly to Rio, trying to maintain her composure. She wasn’t about to let Rio Vidal see how unhinged she felt.

“I’m on call. Same as you,” Agatha replied, her voice flat, like she was giving an explanation to a small child.

“Yeah, I figured,” Rio answered. “Not you, Harkness; her.” She pointed at Kate, an amused glint in her eyes.

Kate blinked, looking between them like she’d just walked into an alternate reality. “Me?”

“No, the other eager little intern who’s about to get her soul crushed.” Rio’s lips twitched. “You’re not on call, Romel is”

Kate grinned. “I am now.”

Rio raised an eyebrow, looking like she was trying to decide whether she was more impressed or amused. “You dragged an intern into a 24 hour shift with you?”

Agatha took a slow sip of her coffee, maintaining the last shred of composure she had left. “Call it a bonding exercise.”

Kate snorted, clearly relieved to have some humor in this otherwise chaotic situation. “Yeah, by ‘bonding exercise,’ she means ‘mild workplace hazing.’”

Agatha hummed, unbothered. “Tomato, to-mah-to.”

Rio tilted her head, raising an eyebrow. “Wait. Is she even getting paid for this?”

Kate blinked, processing the sudden revelation. “Wait. Am I getting paid for this?”

Agatha rolled her eyes. She should have known she’d have to handle all the questions. “Do you want to be a great surgeon or not?”

Kate hesitated, clearly calculating the situation. “Yes?”

“Then congratulations, you’re volunteering.”

Kate frowned. “That doesn’t sound legally sound.”

Agatha patted her shoulder like she was trying to soothe her, but it only added to the chaos. “Nothing about medicine is legally sound.”

Kate scowled, arms crossed like a petulant child.

Agatha didn’t even slow her stride. “Bishop, this is delegation. You’re learning an important skill.”

“Yeah? And what skill is that?”

“Knowing when to shut up and do as you’re told.”

Rio huffed. “Wow. Inspiring.”

Agatha smirked, shoving the door open. “Glad to be a role model.”

Kate stared at her with a look that bordered on desperation. Agatha gritted her teeth, downing the rest of her coffee in one long, furious gulp before tossing the empty cup into the nearest bin. “Come on, Bishop. I don’t have time for whatever nonsense this is.”

Kate quickly followed her down the hallway, but not before throwing Rio one last glance. It was the kind of look that said everything without saying a word.

And Agatha couldn’t help but feel a flicker of jealousy. Because it wasn’t just Kate who was stuck here, looking completely out of her element. It was her, too.

Her mind was still reeling from the last few minutes. She was on the edge of losing it, and the last thing she wanted was Rio's teasing presence making it all worse. But there she was. As if fate wasn’t trying hard enough to test her. She should have known better than to think she could outrun her feelings, especially not when she was stuck here, right in the middle of the storm.

Kate groaned behind her, but Agatha didn’t bother looking back. She had bigger things to focus on, things that didn’t involve babysitting an intern with shaky hands and a questionable sense of confidence.

The second she stepped into the hallway, the chaos of the hospital swallowed her whole. Nurses rushed past, monitors beeped in the distance, and the scent of antiseptic clung to the air. It was a familiar kind of madness, the kind that kept her moving, kept her from thinking too hard about anything else.

She liked it that way.

—----------------

For the first few hours of her shift, Agatha successfully avoided any interaction with Rio. She didn’t look at her, didn’t acknowledge her, didn’t even breathe in her direction. As far as she was concerned, Rio Vidal did not exist.

Unfortunately, her presence did.

It was everywhere.

It didn’t matter which part of the hospital Agatha found herself in; she always knew when Rio was nearby. A shift in the air, the faintest sound of footsteps, and just like that, Rio’s energy would slam into her like an unavoidable force. It was annoying, like a song stuck in her head, except instead of music, it was just awareness.

She was not in the mood for this.

Which was exactly why she had trapped herself in an empty room with Kate, teaching her how to suture. Because if there was anything more miserable than being in Rio’s presence, it was teaching a baby doctor how to stitch a tear without making it look like Frankenstein’s monster.

Kate, to her credit, was taking this very seriously.

Agatha, to her credit, was not yet homicidal.

It was a win for both of them.

“Okay, Bishop,” Agatha sighed, crossing her arms as she watched Kate fumble with the needle. “Let’s pretend for a second that I don’t hate you. How are you going to impress me?”

Kate furrowed her brow in concentration, clearly trying to focus despite the stress. “By doing a perfect subcuticular suture?”

Agatha gave her an unimpressed look. “If you were going to do it perfectly, you wouldn’t still be standing there looking like an anxious intern about to fuck it up.”

Kate scowled but said nothing. Probably because she was, indeed, an anxious intern about to fuck it up.

“Go on,” Agatha gestured toward the practice pad, “show me your perfect suture.”

Kate took a slow breath, clearly hyping herself up. Then, with the utmost focus, she began, her hands trembling ever so slightly as she worked.

Agatha watched silently for all of three seconds before sighing deeply.

“Bishop,” she said flatly, “what the fuck are you doing?”

Kate frowned. “Suturing?”

“That’s not suturing, that’s embroidery.” Agatha leaned in, examining Kate’s work like it personally offended her. “Christ. If I wanted decorative stitching, I’d ask Martha Stewart.”

Kate groaned. “It’s not that bad.”

Agatha shot her a look so sharp it could slice through steel. “It’s worse than bad. It’s an atrocity. An insult to anyone who’s ever had to wear a suture.”

“Okay, fine,” Kate muttered. “It’s bad.”

Agatha snatched the needle from her hand, barely able to hide her frustration. “Here, watch and actually learn.”

Kate watched as Agatha threaded the needle with ease, her hands moving with practiced fluidity, too fast for Kate’s sleep-deprived brain to follow. There was something almost hypnotic about the way Agatha worked. Efficient, precise, controlled. It was a stark contrast to the chaos of her own thoughts, something Kate envied.

“This,” Agatha muttered as she worked, “is how you don’t make a mess out of someone’s vagina.”

Kate choked, her face flushing crimson. “Please, please never say that sentence again.”

Agatha smirked. “Why? Feeling squeamish, Bishop?”

“No.” Kate scowled. “Just… weirdly personal.”

Agatha finished her stitch with a flourish, stepping back to admire her work. It was almost perfect, far better than what Kate had managed, and that was all that mattered right now.

“Well, if you don’t want to personally destroy someone’s perineum, maybe you should practice until you don’t suck at this.”

Kate grumbled something under her breath but grabbed the needle back, her determination now clear. She was serious about this.

Agatha crossed her arms, watching her carefully. It was easier to focus on this. On the work. On teaching. On anything other than the fact that no matter how hard she tried, she still felt Rio’s presence in every damn corner of this hospital.

Every time the door creaked open, every time footsteps echoed down the hallway, Agatha's attention would shift for just a moment, her brain tuning into Rio like a radio searching for a signal. She couldn’t avoid it. Even when she didn’t want to think about it, especially when she didn’t want to think about it, there she was.

Her head buzzed, her frustration growing as her thoughts tangled. She had come here to get away. To escape . But it felt like no matter how hard she tried, the gravitational pull of Rio Vidal was always just a little bit too strong.

The minutes went by, and there were no signs of Rio. She had just started to consider that maybe, maybe , this shift wouldn’t be a complete disaster when her pager went off.

Agatha’s eyes snapped to it, grateful for the distraction.

She ripped the pager from her belt, her heart rate speeding up as she scanned the message.

Emergency delivery. Ten minutes out. OR 3

Agatha exhaled sharply, already tossing her gloves into the bin. “Alright, Bishop, you’re done playing with the practice pad. I’ve got a real patient coming in.”

Kate perked up. “Great, I’ll—”

“No, you’ll go do my paperwork.”

Kate’s face fell as she stared at her in disbelief. “Wait, what?”

Agatha was already halfway to the door, her movements sharp and efficient. “You heard me. I need the charts from the last three patients logged. And if you do it correctly, I might let you scrub in next time.”

Kate groaned dramatically but didn’t argue. Agatha wasn’t in the mood for her whining, especially not when a real emergency was looming.

She turned the corner into the trauma bay just as the doors burst open. The team of paramedics wheeled in a woman mid-contraction, breathless, her face twisted in pain.

“Thirty two years old, thirty six weeks, severe preeclampsia,” one of them called. “BP’s through the roof, seizures in the ambulance, she needs an emergency section.”

Agatha nodded sharply. “Get her to OB now.”

Agatha’s mind clicked into place, every second moving like clockwork. “Get her to OB now,” she barked. The team moved with practiced precision, and just as Agatha was about to follow, she caught a glimpse of something, or rather, someone, out of the corner of her eye.

She turned.

And her stomach flipped.

Because standing across from her, already gloving up, was Rio.

Her hair was tucked under a scrub cap, the mask dangling loosely around her neck, eyes sharp and focused as she prepared for the surgery.

Agatha felt her jaw clench. Of course.

She braced herself for some kind of smug comment, a teasing remark, a knowing smirk, anything that would set her on edge, the kind of games Rio always liked to play. But instead, Rio just met her gaze with an even, composed look and nodded.

“I’ll assist you. Romel is stitching up some idiots who fell off their bikes,” Rio said, her tone calm, polite.

That was it.

No smirk. No teasing. No games.

Just calm, polite professionalism.

Agatha didn’t know what to do with that.

Agatha’s brow furrowed as she processed that. She couldn’t quite figure out what to make of it, and the fact that she couldn’t figure it out unsettled her. She stared at Rio for a beat too long before blinking and turning sharply on her heel. “Fine,” she muttered, willing her heart rate to steady.

They moved quickly. The patient was prepped for surgery, the anesthesiologist worked with precision, and soon enough, Agatha was making the first incision.

For a while, it didn’t even occur to her that Rio was standing next to her. They had scrubbed in together before, of course, but it had always been a chaotic rush, each of them maneuvering around the other, quick, effective, occasionally brushing against each other. But this time? This time, Rio wasn’t flirting. She wasn’t watching Agatha like she was some puzzle to be solved. She wasn’t even throwing her usual teasing remarks.

She was just… there. 

Assisting. 

Efficient. 

Methodical.

Professional. 

It shouldn’t have felt wrong, but it did.

Agatha couldn’t shake the disorientation it caused. Every now and then, her gaze flickered up from the patient, expecting some sort of look, some small acknowledgment from Rio, something, anything. But every time, she found nothing but quiet concentration in Rio’s eyes.

Her hands moved with practiced grace, never wavering, and Agatha, well, Agatha wasn’t used to this. She wasn’t used to feeling like she didn’t have Rio’s full attention. Her chest tightened, her mind spiraling in confusion as she focused on closing up, the skillful suturing of the incision almost mechanical in its simplicity.

By the time she was closing up, she was scowling.

The baby was fine. The mother was stable. The procedure had gone as smoothly as an emergency C-section could.

Everything was fine.

And yet…

Why did she feel so off?

Her head buzzed with an uncomfortable tension. She finished the suturing, stripped off her gloves, and turned, fully expecting Rio to say something. A compliment. A sarcastic remark. Anything. But no.

Rio just gave a short nod. “Good work, Dr. Harkness,” she said in that calm, neutral voice, her eyes briefly meeting Agatha’s before she turned and left the room.

No smirk. No taunt. No lingering gaze.

Just… left.

Agatha stared after her for a moment, blinking in disbelief.

Had she missed something?

Her heart pounded in her chest, and a strange mix of anger and frustration surged up. It was almost like Rio didn’t even care anymore. And that pissed her off.

She stormed out of the OR, her mind racing, frustration churning in her gut. The sharp, echoing clack of her shoes against the sterile hospital floors only heightened the feeling of betrayal, as though the very ground was betraying her. The whole situation felt like an affront.

She’d been so close.

She’d been managing to ignore it all, the tension, the mess they’d made of their relationship, the way Rio seemed to shift from flirtation to indifference in the span of a single day.

And now, after everything, she had to watch as Rio Vidal, the woman who had driven her crazy for weeks, had walked out of that room without so much as a sideways glance.

She should have been able to keep it together. She should have been able to stay focused on her work and nothing else.

But of course, not everything went her way. Because no matter how hard she tried to ignore Rio Vidal, the damn woman always seemed to find a way to worm her way back into Agatha’s thoughts, making it impossible to just move on.

Why the hell is she doing this to me?

Agatha’s chest constricted. Her blood boiled.

She stormed down the hall, trying desperately to put as much distance between herself and the OR as possible. The feeling of helplessness clawed at her chest like a beast that wouldn’t let go. 

And as she walked through the sterile, empty corridors of the hospital, all she could hear was the echo of her own frustration.

She had spent the last few weeks of her life learning exactly how to brace herself for Rio Vidal. Agatha had spent countless hours observing her, watching the way Rio operated with that easy charm, how she pushed boundaries, teased, and smiled like she knew things she had no business knowing. Agatha had grown used to that, the way Rio made her feel like she was being drawn into something she didn’t understand, something dangerous, something thrilling.

But now? This past week, Rio had switched gears completely. Polite nods, professional distance. The kind of behavior that made Agatha feel like she was standing in the middle of a well rehearsed performance, and she had no idea what the script was.

With an irritated yank, Agatha pulled off her mask as she walked through the hospital’s sterile hallways, barely noticing where she was going. Her mind was still reeling from the encounter in the OR, from Rio’s complete lack of anything .

She reached the nurses’ station, still scowling, hands shoved deep into her pockets like they could anchor her to reality. Kate was hunched over a pile of paperwork, looking every bit like she had been forced to transcribe the entire hospital’s medical history by hand. The sight would have been comical if Agatha wasn’t so pissed off.

Kate looked up at her approach, expression immediately wary. “Uh-oh. Who pissed you off?”

Agatha ignored the question entirely, dropping into the chair across from her with an exaggerated huff, slumping as though the weight of the entire hospital rested on her shoulders.

Kate raised an eyebrow, a slight smile tugging at the corner of her lips. “Bad surgery?”

“No,” Agatha snapped, her voice tight. She let out a frustrated sigh, then muttered, “It was fine.”

Kate frowned. “Then why do you look like someone ran over your cat?”

Agatha glared at her, fighting the urge to bite back a snarky response. “I don’t have a cat.”

Kate shrugged. “Okay, well, if you did, you look like someone ran it over.”

Agatha exhaled sharply, pinching the bridge of her nose. She wasn’t about to sit here and dissect whatever the hell had just happened with Rio. Especially not with Kate Bishop of all people, who had a habit of poking at things she shouldn’t, asking questions Agatha didn’t have answers to.

Kate, who was still staring at her like she could read her mind, and Agatha wasn’t sure if she found that more irritating or terrifying.

Rolling her eyes, Agatha finally snapped. “Shouldn’t you be working? You know, doing the paperwork I told you to do? You’re supposed to be making my life easier, Bishop, and so far, you’re doing an awful job of it.”

“I was working,” Kate said defensively, motioning to the half filled charts in front of her. “Then you showed up looking like you just lost a fight with God.”

Agatha didn’t dignify that with a response. Instead, she reached for her coffee only to find it empty.

She frowned. “Where’s my refill?”

Kate blinked, clearly confused. “I—what?”

“My coffee, Bishop.” Agatha waved dramatically the empty cup, giving Kate a pointed look. “Do I look caffeinated to you?”

Kate stared at her, then shook her head in disbelief. “You made me work this shift for free, and now you expect me to fetch your coffee?”

“Yes.”

Kate opened her mouth. Closed it. Pinched the bridge of her nose exactly like Agatha had just done moments ago.

Finally, she let out a long, slow sigh and stood. “You know what? Fine. But only because I want coffee too.”

Agatha smirked. “Whatever helps you sleep at night, Bishop.”

Kate muttered something under her breath as she walked away, and Agatha leaned back in her chair with a deep, tired breath. She was fine. Everything was fine. She didn’t need to worry about the fact that Rio had been so normal today, so detached, like their entire past was just something she could easily sweep under the rug.

No, she wasn’t going to think about it. She couldn’t. She had work to do. She was fine.

So fine that she had been sitting at the nurses' station for a full five minutes, staring blankly at a patient chart, without reading a single word. She was so damn tired of this.

It was infuriating.

Because her mind, the traitorous, idiotic thing that it was, wasn’t on the chart. Or the shift. Or the poor, overworked intern she was exploiting for free labor.

Her mind? Her mind was on Rio.

Because Rio had been normal. Too normal. And it was making Agatha feel like she had accidentally stepped into some alternate dimension where everything made sense, and she hated it. This wasn’t how it was supposed to be.

Everything had changed after the kiss.

The kiss she had initiated.

And then, she had run away from it.

Now Rio was acting like none of it had happened. Like Agatha hadn’t grabbed her by the collar and kissed her like she was trying to solve every problem in her life with one reckless, desperate move. Like Rio hadn’t kissed her back, and Agatha hadn’t felt something when their lips had met.

Agatha didn’t want things to go back to normal. No. That was a lie. She didn’t want this new normal. This weird, distant, unbothered Rio.

She didn’t know what she wanted.

Which was exactly the problem.

With a sharp breath, Agatha shook her head, trying to push it all aside. Focus. Work. She had work to do.

And then—because the universe was a vindictive bitch—Rio walked in.

Agatha stiffened before she could stop herself, her heart kicking into overdrive.

Rio didn’t seem to notice. Or if she did, she didn’t show it. She just walked up to the counter, grabbed a patient file, and flipped it open as if she weren’t currently ruining Agatha’s entire existence with her presence.

She didn’t even look at her.

It was infuriating.

Agatha was about to ignore her completely, pretend she wasn’t there, pretend she didn’t care, when Rio, without looking up from the file, spoke.

“You’ve been sitting there for five minutes.”

Agatha blinked, caught off guard. “Excuse me?”

Rio turned a page, her voice casual. “Five minutes. Staring at that chart. Haven’t flipped it once.”

Agatha scowled, irritation rising again. “Maybe I was thinking.”

Rio hummed, the sound almost too casual. “Sure. Let’s go with that.”

Agatha bristled. “I was thinking.”

Finally, Rio looked up at her, and for the first time since their last encounter, really looked at her. Not in that teasing, amused way she was used to.

It made Agatha feel like her skin didn’t fit right. Her heart stuttered in her chest, and her hands twitched with the urge to do something, anything, to break the tension that was suddenly unbearable between them.

She was about to snap, about to say something, anything, when Kate reappeared, dropping a fresh coffee cup in front of her.

“Here,” Kate announced, before plopping down in her chair. “Not that you deserve it.”

Agatha grabbed the cup without hesitation, taking a long sip, as though the hot liquid might burn away the unease crawling under her skin.

Rio watched her, her eyes flicking between Agatha and Kate, then asked, “You really have her running errands for you?” Her tone was amused, but it didn’t mask the curiosity lurking beneath.

Kate scoffed. “Right? That’s what I said.”

Agatha, unfazed, leaned back in her chair with a smirk. “She’s learning valuable skills.”

Kate snorted. “Yeah, like how to be exploited.”

Rio shook her head with a small, almost rueful smirk, then turned back to her file.

Agatha should’ve felt victorious. But instead, everything just felt… off . 

And with a muttered curse that was definitely not hospital-appropriate, Agatha slouched deeper into her chair, wishing she could escape whatever mess her emotions had gotten tangled up in.

—-----------

The next few hours were hell.

The kind of hell that made Agatha question all her life choices that led her here.

Every surgical procedure bled into the next, an unending cycle of high-stakes decisions, steady hands, and relentless pressure. There were no breaks, no time to breathe, no pause to process. Every second felt like it was biting into her bones, and the exhaustion was suffocating.

And, of course, Rio was there for all of it.

It wasn’t like they spoke much.There was barely time to. But she felt her. Everywhere. They moved like two parts of the same machine, cutting, suturing, making life or death decisions without hesitation. Together, they flowed through the surgeries, two professionals working in perfect sync, no hesitation, no second guessing. A beautiful, maddening choreography.

It should have been good. It should have been the ideal working relationship. The kind of bond that every surgeon dreamed of. But it wasn’t.

Instead, it was infuriating.

Because no matter how hard she tried to focus, no matter how much she told herself she did not care, Agatha couldn’t ignore the nagging feeling crawling up her spine.

The way her mind kept circling back to Rio, like an itch she couldn’t scratch.

Like a problem she couldn’t solve.

By the time the chaos finally settled, it was well past 2 a.m. and Agatha felt like she had been wrung out. Every muscle in her body ached with exhaustion, her scrubs stiff and sticky with god knows what from the countless surgeries she had performed. Her mind was a haze of fatigue, and her patience, what little she had left, was nonexistent. The caffeine had long worn off, and now she was left with nothing but the sickly remnants of a crash that made her feel like she was teetering on the edge of collapse.

And Rio. God, Rio’s presence was still gnawing at her. The quiet professionalism was grating. It was so calm, so controlled, and yet Agatha couldn’t shake the feeling that something was wrong. Something had changed. It was like she was still stuck in the aftermath of the kiss, of what had been, what could have been. And now Rio had retreated, back into the safe distance of a coworker, a colleague. She was polite, efficient, and utterly unreadable.

Agatha wasn’t sure if she wanted to throttle Rio or throw herself into the ocean and hope to drown in the sound of the waves. Everything felt so... confusing. It made her angry that she couldn’t get a grip on any of it. Between the exhaustion, the caffeine crash, and Rio’s infuriating presence, she was pretty sure this was how she was going to die. Collapsed in a heap on the pit floor, with Rio standing over her, probably smirking.

So, with a sharp exhale, she did what any sane person would do at this hour: she escaped.

She made her way to the on-call room, dragging her exhausted body like a corpse that was still somehow walking. Every step was a struggle. She got to her room and the realization hit. She hadn't stopped anywhere  to grab something, anything to eat.

And that’s when she saw it.

Sitting neatly on the table, as though placed there by some divine hand, was a Greek salad and an iced tea. Her favorite.

Agatha blinked, standing frozen in the doorway, the exhaustion momentarily forgotten. She stared at the food for a beat too long, skeptical. Who would have known that she liked this? She hadn’t even told Kate that she ate it on every shift, or everyday she was at the hospital. The thought made her stomach flip uncomfortably, and she couldn’t shake the suspicion that something wasn’t right. The feeling deepened when she grabbed her phone and shot a quick text to Kate.

Agatha: Thanks for the food.

A beat passed before Kate responded, and Agatha waited with bated breath.

Agatha: Didn’t realize you were observant enough to notice that.

Kate had won herself some points with the food. Agatha had always eaten the same thing when she worked at the hospital, a Greek salad, iced tea, no exceptions. 

A minute passed. Then—

Kate: What food?

Agatha frowned, a wave of confusion sweeping over her. She glanced down at the screen again, rereading Kate’s message, feeling something stirring in the pit of her stomach.

Agatha: The Greek salad. And the iced tea.

Kate: Dr. Harkness, I have no idea what you’re talking about.

Agatha stared at her screen, eyes narrowing. What the hell? She quickly scrolled back through their messages. No mention of food. No hint that Kate had done anything, let alone brought her dinner. Agatha sat there for a moment, the quiet hum of the hospital around her, trying to process.

And then, like a punch to the gut, it hit her.

Her heart dropped into her stomach.

It wasn’t Kate.

It couldn’t have been.

Her eyes snapped up, scanning the empty room around her with frantic urgency. The silence felt oppressive now. Every corner of the room, every shadow felt charged. She turned slowly, as if the food might suddenly vanish, or the world might stop making sense altogether.

She had already known, hadn’t she? The moment her gaze had flicked to the table, she had already known. She had felt it, a strange sensation, like someone had been watching, waiting for her to realize.

Agatha was on her feet before she even realized what she was doing.

The Greek salad, the betrayal salad, sat abandoned on the table as she stormed out of her room, her blood boiling hotter with every step.

This was bullshit.

This was textbook Rio Vidal bullshit.

And Agatha was not going to stand for it.

Her footsteps echoed furiously through the halls as she made her way straight to Rio’s room. She didn’t hesitate. Didn’t second guess herself. She just knocked.

No, pounded.

Like a maniac.

No answer.

Agatha’s eyes twitched.

She knocked again, harder this time. Nothing.

Oh, hell no.

Without another thought, she shoved the door open, ready to unleash hell- 

Only to find the room empty.

The bed was undone, the sheets a tangled mess, but Rio was nowhere to be seen.

Agatha’s irritation flared into something even uglier .

She had stormed over here, on a mission, only for Rio to be—what? Gone? Missing? Evaporated into thin air like the smug, infuriating bitch she was?

Unacceptable.

Agatha spun on her heel, marching straight to the pit.

No Rio.

Fine.

She made her way to the ORs, her exhaustion now replaced with sheer, unfiltered rage.

Still no Rio.

Agatha stopped in the middle of the hallway, taking a deep breath through her nose.

If murder were legal…

She yanked out her phone.

Agatha: Where the hell are you?

It took all of five seconds before a response came in.

Rio: Is there an emergency coming up? Romel and Kate are covering the pit. They are supposed to page us if anything comes in. 

Agatha saw red.

Agatha: No emergency

Agatha: Answer the fucking question.

Another pause. Then—

Rio: 18th floor.

Agatha frowned.

The 18th floor?

What the fuck was on the 18th floor?

Her grip tightened on her phone. She didn’t know what the hell Rio was playing at. But she was going to find out.

And if she had to kill her in the process?

Well.

That was just a bonus.

Agatha stepped onto the 18th floor, her irritation spiking the second the elevator doors slid open.

It was deserted.

The halls were eerily empty, the lights dimmed.

She exhaled sharply, running a hand down her face.

Of course.

Of fucking course.

She should’ve known Rio was messing with her.

Yanking out her phone, she fired off a text.

Agatha: I swear to God, Vidal, if this is another one of your games…

Her phone vibrated almost instantly.

Rio: Did you get to the 18th floor?

Agatha gritted her teeth.

Agatha: Yes.

Another buzz.

Rio: Good. Now find the emergency stairs and go up.

Agatha stared at the screen, jaw tightening.

What the fuck was this? Some mystical scavenger hunt?

She inhaled sharply, debating whether to ignore her completely.

But against her better judgment, and because she needed to yell at Rio in person, she set off down the hall, searching for the stairwell.

She found it tucked away in the farthest corner of the floor.

Of course.

Fucking inconvenient, just like everything about Rio Vidal.

Still, she pushed through the door and started climbing.

One flight.

Two flights.

And then—

She hit a locked door.

Agatha stared at it, chest rising and falling with irritation.

You have got to be kidding me.

Her fingers curled into fists as she reached for her phone again.

Agatha: The door is locked.

Nothing.

Silence.

She clenched her jaw. Her patience was all but gone. She had been baited this far, there was no turning back now. If Rio thought she was going to back off, she was about to be very disappointed. She didn’t give a damn about the locked door. She’d find a way in, even if it meant breaking it down herself.

The silence stretched on for what felt like an eternity, and just as Agatha’s fury reached its peak, the lock clicked.

The door swung open.

And there she was.

Rio Vidal.

Her dark hair was down, whipping wildly in the wind.

Agatha's breath caught in her throat, and for a second, she forgot how to be angry. Rio stood before her, framed by the dim light of the rooftop behind her, the wind tugging at her dark hair, making it swirl around her face. She was the picture of casual grace, perfectly poised, as though she hadn’t just sent Agatha on some absurd scavenger hunt across the damn hospital. Her eyes glinted with something unreadable, her lips curled into that infuriating half smirk that made Agatha want to scream.

“Here I am,” Rio said, her voice as calm as ever, as if Agatha hadn’t just climbed three flights of stairs in a fit of rage.

Agatha’s jaw tightened. She stepped forward, pushing the door open wider with a shove, her gaze never leaving Rio.

"What the hell is this, Vidal?" Agatha snapped, her voice sharp enough to cut glass. "A game? A riddle? Because I’m getting sick of your stupid mind games." Her chest heaved with frustration, but she couldn’t quite shake the feeling that this wasn’t just a game. Not anymore. "What the hell do you want from me?"

Rio didn’t answer immediately. She simply stepped back, holding the door open for Agatha to enter.

Rio leaned against the doorframe, one brow quirked. “Are you coming out, or are you just gonna stand there looking pissed?”

Agatha squinted at her, then at the rooftop beyond. “That depends. Are you planning to murder me?”

Rio smirked. “Not tonight.”

“Oh, well, that’s reassuring.”

Rio sighed, stepping back to give her space. “Harkness, if I wanted you dead, I wouldn’t go through the effort of luring you to the roof. I’d just sabotage your caffeine supply and let nature take its course.”

Agatha scowled. “That’s sick.”

“That’s efficient.”

Agatha huffed, still suspicious, but curiosity won out. She stepped forward, crossing the threshold onto the rooftop. The wind hit her immediately, cool and crisp against her skin, whipping at her coat. She pulled it tighter around herself. “So?” she demanded. “What the hell are you doing up here?”

Rio didn’t answer right away. She just turned on her heel, starting across the roof like she expected Agatha to follow.

And the worst part?

She did.

She blamed exhaustion. And also rage. Because she still hadn’t yelled at Rio about the whole food situation, and she wasn’t about to let that slide.

So she stomped after her, boots clicking against the concrete. “Vidal, if this is some elaborate ploy to shove me off the building, I will haunt you.”

Rio just chuckled, leading her to a quiet spot near the edge of the rooftop where a single bench sat. It was a perfect vantage point, overlooking the whole damn city.

And fuck.

Agatha stopped in her tracks.

Because the view was—

Well.

It was breathtaking.

The Mayo Clinic loomed in the foreground, a testament to all the chaos inside. But beyond that? The city of Rochester stretched out beneath them, scattered with streetlights and glowing windows, everything twinkling under the dark Minnesota sky.

It was quiet. Still. Almost peaceful.

And Agatha hated that it stunned her.

That she actually had to take a second to breathe.

Agatha finally turned, squinting at Rio like she was seeing her for the first time.

“What is this?” she asked, voice still edged with suspicion.

Rio leaned against the railing, glancing out at the city. “Second helicopter arrival zone,” she said simply. “But it’s never used.”

Agatha blinked. “What?”

Rio smirked at her confusion. “Found it my first year here,” she continued, gesturing around them. “Technically, it’s a backup landing site, but no one ever comes up here. Too much wind, not enough traffic to justify it. So, it just… sits here.”

Agatha crossed her arms. “And what, you just claimed it?”

Rio shrugged. “I needed somewhere to escape. When things get too stressful, I come up here.”

Agatha eyed her, suddenly seeing her in a different light. This was where she went when things got overwhelming? This was how she handled it?

Her own anger, hot and consuming just minutes ago, fizzled into something more complicated.

She looked away, back at the city, her arms still crossed like a shield.

A beat of silence.

Then—

“The salad,” Agatha said abruptly.

Rio turned her head slightly, waiting.

Agatha inhaled. “Why?”

Rio didn’t pretend not to know what she meant. She just exhaled through her nose, tilting her head back to look at the sky. “You looked stressed,” she said simply. “Figured you needed it.”

Rio just watched her, that unreadable expression still plastered on her face. Her eyes glinted in the moonlight, and Agatha couldn’t tell whether she was amused or waiting for Agatha to have some kind of breakdown. Either way, she felt herself growing more frustrated by the second. She couldn’t even get a solid read on Rio anymore. One moment, she was playing mind games, making Agatha climb three flights of stairs and nearly lose her damn mind, and the next, she was pulling some tender, thoughtful gesture out of nowhere with that damn Greek salad.

That was it?

No teasing, no ulterior motive?

Just… a quiet acknowledgment? A small act of care?

Her stomach twisted uncomfortably.

She didn’t like this.

She didn’t like not knowing how to respond to Rio Vidal.

 

Agatha scoffed, shaking her head. “You figured I needed it?”

Rio blinked at her, clearly not expecting that reaction. “Yeah?”

"I don’t know whether to strangle you or thank you," Agatha muttered, narrowing her eyes.

"You don’t have to thank me," Rio said, her voice softer than usual. It was almost as if Rio was trying to be serious for once, and it unsettled Agatha. "You looked like you were going to snap. Honestly, I was just trying to make sure you didn’t." Rio's words were calm, measured, almost too calm for a conversation that had started with a lot of sarcasm and irritation.

It wasn’t that Agatha didn’t believe her. No, that was the problem, she did. She believed it in a way that made her stomach twist, in a way that made her pulse stutter against her ribs. Because it was so simple. So casual. Like it hadn’t meant anything at all. Like it hadn’t thrown her completely off her axis.

Agatha let out a slow breath, her arms still crossed tightly over her chest, her fingers gripping the sleeves of her coat as if anchoring herself. Her thoughts churned, chaotic and restless. 

She let out a dry, humorless laugh, running a hand through her hair. “Right. Sure. Because you’re so thoughtful.”

Rio frowned. “What is your problem?”

“My problem—” Agatha snapped, turning to face her fully now, hands on her hips, “—is that you don’t get to play this fucking game with me.”

Rio stared at her, visibly confused. “What game?”

Agatha huffed, looking away for a moment like she needed to physically collect herself before she lost her mind. “You,” she said, voice sharp. “You’ve been acting weird ever since last Friday.”

Rio’s brows furrowed. “What the hell are you talking about?”

Agatha let out a bitter laugh. “Oh, don’t play dumb.” She pointed at Rio accusingly. “You barely talked to me all shift, didn’t look at me, nothing. And now, suddenly, you’re nice?” She threw her arms out. “Buying me food? Dragging me up to your secret rooftop getaway?” She scoffed. “What, am I supposed to just pretend that’s normal?”

Rio’s face twisted with genuine confusion. “I am being normal.”

Agatha gaped at her. “No, you’re not!”

“Yes, I am!”

“No, you’re not!”

Rio let out a frustrated breath. “I don’t know what you want from me, Harkness. I’m being polite.”

Agatha shot her a look of utter disbelief. “Polite?” she repeated, voice sharp with incredulity.

“Yes!”

“Oh, fuck off,” Agatha snapped. “You’re never polite. That’s not you.”

Rio raised an eyebrow. “So, let me get this straight. You’re mad at me because I’m being too nice?”

“Yes!”

Rio made a baffled sound. “What the fuck?”

Agatha threw her hands up. “You changed!”

Rio blinked. “What?”

Agatha inhaled sharply through her nose, suddenly feeling too warm, too on edge. “You changed after last Friday.”

Something flickered across Rio’s face, but she schooled it quickly. “What does that mean?”

Agatha clenched her jaw. “You know exactly what it means.”

Rio shook her head. “No, I really don’t.”

Agatha glared at her. “The kiss.”

Rio’s expression didn’t shift. “And?”

“And—” Agatha gestured wildly. “You’ve been acting weird ever since!”

Rio exhaled sharply, rubbing her temple like she was trying to fend off a headache. “I have no idea what you want from me, Agatha. I’m just being normal.”

Agatha scoffed. “This isn’t normal for you.”

Rio crossed her arms, tilting her head. “What exactly is normal for me, then?”

Agatha’s jaw locked. She knew the answer. Knew exactly what she had come to expect from Rio Vidal.

But this?

This wasn’t it.

Rio let out a sharp breath, shaking her head. “This is unbelievable.”

Agatha crossed her arms tightly over her chest. “Oh, I’m unbelievable?”

“Yes!” Rio threw up her hands. “You kissed me, Agatha! You. And then you ran away like your life fucking depended on it. What the hell was I supposed to do?”

Agatha’s stomach twisted, but she scowled. “You could’ve called!”

Rio scoffed. “Oh, sure. That would’ve gone great. ‘Hey, Agatha, just checking in after you sprinted out of the club like you were being chased by the fucking FBI. You good?’”

Agatha clenched her jaw. “Don’t mock me.”

“I’m not,” Rio said, voice firm. “I just— You ran. That wasn’t some accident. That was you deciding you didn’t want to deal with whatever the hell that kiss meant.”

Agatha’s pulse was pounding in her ears. “That’s not—”

“That’s exactly what happened.”

Agatha’s throat felt tight. She turned away, suddenly unable to hold Rio’s gaze.

Because the worst part?

The worst part was that Rio was right.

She had run.

She had kissed Rio, had let herself fall into it, had felt the heat, the pull, the electricity, and then, the second it was over, the weight of it had crashed down on her like a tsunami.

It wasn’t just a kiss. It was a decision. A crack in the wall she had spent her entire life building.

And she panicked.

Because this wasn’t just about Rio. This was about everything. About what it meant. About what it said about her.

She had spent her entire life pushing these thoughts down, burying them, pretending they didn’t exist.

She had tried.

Tried to be normal. Tried to do things the way she was supposed to.

She had married Daniel. Had built a whole life around the idea of what she should want, of who she should be.

And then it had all crumbled.

And now here she was, standing on a rooftop at 3 a.m., fighting with Rio Vidal about a kiss she didn’t even know how to define.

She swallowed hard, forcing herself to look back at Rio. “You should’ve followed me.”

Rio's eyes darkened at Agatha's words, her posture tightening. She took a step forward, the air between them crackling with unspoken tension.

"You think I should've just run after you, Agatha? After you bolted like that?" Rio's voice was low, edged with a mix of frustration and hurt that Agatha hadn't expected. "After you kissed me and disappeared? You think that’s what I should’ve done?  So you could push me away?”

Rio’s eyes flashed. 

Agatha didn’t answer.

Because, deep down, she knew the truth.

That’s exactly what she would have done.

Rio exhaled sharply, shaking her head. “You want to be mad at me? Fine. But don’t act like I’m the one playing games here. I’ve been flirting with you since the day we met, and you know it.”

Agatha’s breath hitched. She did know it. Rio told her that, before Agatha kissed her. 

“You act like I’ve changed,” Rio continued, voice lower now. “Like I’m doing something different. But the only thing that’s different is you.”

Agatha’s stomach churned. “That’s not—”

“Yes, it is.” Rio took a step closer. “So tell me, Agatha. What do you actually want?”

Agatha’s mouth went dry. She couldn’t answer. Couldn’t force the words out.

Because she didn’t know.

Or maybe she did.

Maybe she had always known.

But saying it out loud? That was something else entirely.

Agatha’s hands curled into fists at her sides. “You know what, Vidal? Maybe you’re right. I did run” She let out a humorless laugh. “But that doesn’t mean you had to go and—and—” She gestured wildly at Rio, her words tangling with frustration. “Fucking pretend like nothing happened after you—”

Her voice cut off sharply, her throat tightening.

Rio just stared at her, expression unreadable. “After I what?”

Agatha clenched her jaw so hard it ached. “After you fucking marked me.”

Something flickered across Rio’s face.

Agatha exhaled sharply, her rage barely contained. “You left a hickey on me. And then what? You just—what? Decided it didn’t mean anything? You went completely silent, didn’t text, didn’t say shit—”

Rio’s brows pulled together. “You ran.”

Agatha flinched.

Rio’s voice was calm, but there was something razor-sharp under it. “You kissed me. You bit me.” A humorless smirk tugged at her lips. “And then you bolted like your life depended on it.”

Agatha’s stomach twisted.

Rio shook her head. “So yeah, I didn’t text you. Because I figured that’s what you wanted.”

Agatha let out a scoff, but it was weak. “That’s bullshit.”

Rio took a step closer, her voice steady. “Is it?”

Agatha hated the way she swallowed hard.

Hated the way her pulse jumped in her throat.

Because the truth was, she had run.

And maybe, maybe a part of her had wanted Rio to chase her.

To prove her wrong. To prove that whatever was happening between them wasn’t just something fleeting, something Agatha had imagined.

But Rio hadn’t.

And that meant—

No.

Rio let out a slow breath. “Jesus, Agatha.”

“Don’t Jesus, Agatha me!” Her voice was rising now, the heat of it finally reaching a breaking point. “You want to act like you’ve been all innocent in this? Like you’re some victim of my supposed mixed signals? Bullshit. You’ve been fucking with me since the moment we met.”

Rio’s jaw tightened. “I was flirting with you, yeah. But after last Friday? I figured that was your answer.”

Agatha’s stomach twisted, her anger crashing against something raw and uncomfortable. “What does that mean?”

“It means,” Rio said, voice quieter now, “that I stopped.”

Agatha blinked, her chest tight.

Rio shook her head. “I wasn’t playing some game, Agatha. I wasn’t trying to punish you or make some stupid point.” She exhaled. “I thought you weren’t interested. So I backed off.”

Agatha opened her mouth. Then closed it.

Rio laughed, low, exasperated. “ I gave you space. I backed off. And now you’re mad at me for it?” She shook her head, something bitter in her tone. “I don’t know what you want.”

Agatha’s breath came sharp and uneven.

Because the truth was, she didn’t fucking know either.

Her feelings were a mess, a tangled, chaotic, impossible mess.

Because she had wanted Rio to follow her.

But she had also wanted to run.

She had wanted Rio to tease her.

But she had also wanted to ignore it.

She had wanted—

Fuck.

She didn’t even know what she wanted.

And maybe that was the whole problem.

She swallowed, gripping the edge of her coat. “You didn’t have to—”

Rio laughed, but there was no humor in it. “Didn’t have to what? Respect your very obvious rejection?”

Agatha’s stomach churned. “That’s not—”

“What is it then?” Rio cut in, shaking her head. “Because from where I’m standing, this whole thing only seems to be a problem when I stop pushing.”

Agatha’s chest went tight. But before she could find the words, before she could fix whatever this was. 

Rios phone sounded, notifications coming in. She let out a slow breath, her gaze heavy. “I need to sleep. We have an ambulance arriving in an hour. I suggest you do the same” she paused “goodnight Agatha”

Rio turned.

And left.

Leaving Agatha standing there, alone, with nothing but the wind howling around her.

Agatha stood frozen, her body locked in place as Rio's retreating figure grew smaller and smaller with each step. Her chest felt like it had collapsed in on itself, every breath coming harder than the last. She wanted to shout. Wanted to call after her. But the words wouldn’t come. The weight of them pressed down, crushing her.

Damn it.

Chapter End Notes

At this point, I’m braver than the army. Definitely an interesting addition to my curriculum (and my med school application lmao).
