Chapter 22

Chapter Notes

This is undeniable proof that I have zero self control. I was supposed to save this chapter for next week, but the edits started eating, and my girlfriend said I should do a double drop today, and I am, in fact, very easy to convince. So here we are. Enjoy.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Her hands clenched at her sides, nails digging into her palms as the cold wind bit at her skin. She didn’t know what to do. Didn’t know what to feel. Her anger, her frustration, felt like it was bubbling over, but underneath it, something else stirred. Something deeper. And just as terrifying.

Rio had left.

And now, all that remained was this deafening silence.

She should have said something. Anything. She should have—

Fuck.

She should have known better. Should have kept her distance. Should have never let herself get so tangled up in whatever the hell was happening between them.

But in that moment, when Rio had leaned in, when she kissed her, Agatha had felt it. That desperate, aching need for something real. Something that wasn’t just another part of her carefully constructed façade.

She was so fucking tired of pretending.

The kiss had left her shaken, raw. She didn’t know how to explain it, couldn’t even begin to articulate the mess of emotions swirling inside her. But then she had run. 

She turned and walked to the edge of the rooftop, her boots clattering on the concrete as she gazed out at the city below. The lights from the buildings seemed to blur together, a sea of colors swirling in the darkness. It looked so peaceful from up here. So distant. Almost like it wasn’t even real.

Agatha ran a hand over her face. She needed to think. Needed to get her head on straight.

But the more she thought about it, the more she realized she didn’t have the answers. She didn’t know what she wanted. Didn’t know what she was even supposed to do.

She just knew she couldn’t keep running. Couldn’t keep pushing people away, pretending that she could do everything on her own.

The wind picked up again, the cool air whipping around her, and for a moment, Agatha let herself close her eyes, trying to center herself.

But it didn’t help.

Nothing helped.

Agatha trudged back inside, her mind still racing with the weight of Rio’s words.

"This whole thing only seems to be a problem when I stop pushing."

She exhaled sharply, pushing a hand through her hair. She needed to sleep. Or at least try to.

The on-call room was empty when she slipped inside, the air stale and heavy with exhaustion. She shrugged off her jacket, dropping onto the thin mattress with a groan. The room was quiet, too quiet. Her body ached, her limbs screamed for rest, but her mind? Fucking relentless.

She lay on her back, staring at the ceiling, every word Rio had said replaying in her head like a broken record.

"I thought you weren’t interested. So I backed off."

She clenched her jaw, flipping onto her side. Then her stomach. Then her back again.

Minutes passed. Then an hour.

Sleep didn’t come.

She squeezed her eyes shut, willing herself to just shut the fuck up and rest, but her body refused. Her skin felt too tight, her thoughts too loud. 

By the time her pager went off, she felt like she’d aged ten years. A sharp beep-beep-beep, pulling her back to reality like a slap to the face.

She groaned, rubbing her hands down her face before grabbing the device.

Incoming Trauma. ETA 5 minutes. Multiple victims.

That woke her up real fast.

She was up and moving before she even processed it, shoving her shoes back on and shrugging into her coat as she made her way to the ER.

The ambulance was already pulling in when she arrived.

Chaos. That was the only way to describe it.

The paramedics were rushing to unload the victims, shouting vitals and injuries as the trauma team scrambled to keep up.

“What do we have?” Agatha called out, slipping on a pair of gloves.

“Car accident,” one of the nurses responded. “Two victims, one critical. Drunk driver ran a red light and T-boned them.”

Her stomach twisted.

The first victim was already being wheeled past her, a man in his mid-thirties, bleeding from a deep head wound, his arm bent at an unnatural angle. Bad, but stable.

It was the second victim that set off alarms in her brain.

Young male. Maybe twenty. Barely conscious, his skin too pale, his breathing ragged.

“BP’s dropping fast”

“Shit,” Agatha muttered. “Get him to Trauma 1, now.”

They rushed him inside, and Agatha was right behind them.

The next thirty minutes were a fight.

The kid, Luke, according to his ID, was in bad shape. Internal bleeding. Possible ruptured spleen. Fractured ribs.

And a collapsed lung, because of course.

Agatha worked fast, barking orders as the team scrambled to keep up.

“Romel, get a chest tube in now”

“I’ve got it.”

Rio’s voice cut through the chaos, steady as ever.

She was already moving into position, her gloved hands precise as she worked. The tension in the room was thick, but she was focused, controlled. It was almost annoying how effortless she made it look.

Kate hovered nearby, wide eyed but determined, ready to assist.

“We need to get him up to the OR,” Agatha said, her voice sharp.

“Agreed,” Rio chimed in. “Let’s move.”

They barely had time to breathe before the elevator doors slammed shut behind them.

The OR was already a storm of movement by the time she arrived. Nurses moving in rapid succession, equipment being prepped, the beep-beep-beep of the monitors filling the air.

The surgery was long.

Luke’s spleen was beyond saving. The internal bleeding had been worse than expected, and for a moment, just a moment, Agatha wondered if they were losing him.

But somehow, they pulled him through.

By the time they were done, exhaustion had fully settled into her bones, her brain foggy from too many hours without sleep.

She peeled off her gloves, exhaling.

Rio, standing across from her, did the same. Their eyes met.

Something passed between them.

A moment of shared exhaustion. Of relief.

And then their pagers went off at the same time. 

More bullshit.

Agatha and Rio exchanged a glance before rushing out, still in their surgical gowns. In the waiting area, a fight was breaking out.

The fight in the waiting area was the last fucking straw.

One of Luke’s friends, mid-twenties, built like a linebacker, was trying to corner the guy who had been driving the other car.

The only reason he hadn’t succeeded was Romel physically holding him back.

“What the hell is going on?” Agatha snapped.

Kate, looking absolutely done with the day, crossed her arms. “This idiot found out the other driver was drunk and decided to throw hands.”

Rio sighed. “Jesus Christ.”

The guy wasn’t drunk, not legally, anyway. Just barely over the limit. Enough to be reckless. Not enough for an arrest.

But the damage was already done.

“Alright, enough!” Rio barked, her patience long gone. She stepped between them, glaring. “This is a hospital, not a goddamn boxing ring. If you want to beat the shit out of each other, do it outside.”

“I don’t care what you think,” Rio said, stepping between them. “This is a hospital. You start another fight, I will personally make sure you never see your friend again.”

The guy with bloody knuckles scowled. “I was defending him—”

“Not. My. Problem.” Rio cut him off, voice sharp as a scalpel. “If you start another fight, I will personally throw you out.”

Rio crossed her arms, unimpressed. “And if you so much as look at each other the wrong way, I’ll make sure security gets involved.”

The threat worked.

That shut him up real quick.

Grumbling, he backed off.

Agatha let out a slow breath, pinching the bridge of her nose.

She needed a drink. Or a nap.

Or maybe a lobotomy.

—--------------

By the time their shift ended, it was well past dawn.

Agatha just wanted to go home. She wanted to collapse onto her bed, bury herself under the covers, and forget the hellscape of the last twenty four hours. She wanted silence, sleep, and maybe, if she was feeling indulgent, an entire bottle of wine.

But fate, as always, had other plans.

She spotted Rio in the parking lot first, standing unnaturally still, her hands on her hips as she glared at her car like it had personally insulted her. Even from a distance, Agatha could see the tension in her shoulders, the unmistakable sharpness in her stance. Something was wrong.

Agatha frowned, picking up her pace. “What now?”

Rio didn’t say anything at first. She just gave a pointed nod toward her car.

Agatha’s gaze followed, and her brows shot up.

All four of Rio’s tires? Slashed.

“Shit.”

“Yep.”

Agatha whistled low, stepping closer to inspect the damage. The deep gashes in the rubber were deliberate, angry. Someone had really put in the effort.

She exhaled sharply. “You piss someone off that bad?”

Rio shot her a dry look, and Agatha snorted. Fair.

They stood there in silence for a moment, both of them staring at the destroyed tires like they might magically fix themselves if they waited long enough.

Rio finally pulled out her phone. “I’ll just—”

“You should call the police,” Agatha interrupted.

Rio hesitated, glancing up at her.

Agatha crossed her arms. “It was probably the friends of that guy from the accident. The ones who were causing a scene earlier.”

Rio exhaled through her nose, rubbing the bridge of it like she was warding off a headache. “Yeah. Probably.”

Agatha studied her, waiting. “So? You gonna call?”

Rio scoffed, shaking her head. “And say what? ‘Hi, officer, someone slashed my tires in a hospital parking lot, and I have absolutely no proof of who did it’? You think they’re gonna drop everything to investigate a misdemeanor?”

Agatha considered that. “They might look at the security cameras.”

Rio hummed noncommittally. “Mmh. I’ll talk to security later. Right now, I just want to go home.”

She tapped her phone screen, probably about to call an Uber.

And Agatha, stupidly, opened her mouth.

“I’ll drive you.”

The words left her before she could stop them, before she could think them through. And the second they were out, she regretted them.

Because Rio could just call an Uber. They both knew it. It would be easy, fast, impersonal. Logical.

She should’ve let her.

She should’ve just walked away, gotten into her own car, and driven home like a sane person.

But instead, she’d made the offer.

She’d invited Rio into her space, into her car, into her morning.

Why?

She didn’t know.

She told herself it was just the exhaustion talking, just the lingering guilt from their fight, just the stupid sense of responsibility that had been drilled into her since medical school, take care of your people, don’t leave them stranded.

Except Rio wasn’t her people.

Rio was… Rio.

And Agatha wasn’t responsible for her.

But she’d still offered.

And now Rio was looking at her. Really looking at her. Like she was trying to figure something out.

“You don’t have to,” she said finally.

Agatha huffed, rolling her eyes. “I know I don’t have to. Just get in the damn car.”

For a second, Rio said nothing. Then—

That smirk.

The slow, knowing one. The one that made Agatha’s stomach turn on itself.

“Fair,” Rio murmured.

And just like that, she climbed into Agatha’s passenger seat.

—---------

The drive to Rio’s place was quiet.

Not awkward quiet, just… something quiet.

Agatha kept her focus on the road, hands steady on the wheel, while Rio sat in the passenger seat, head resting against the window. She looked exhausted, like the night had finally caught up to her, but she wasn’t sleeping.

She was just watching.

Not at her, obviously. Just watching the city lights blur past.

It was early on a sunday, the streets half-empty, the neon glow of storefronts flickering against the wet pavement. The rhythmic hum of the engine was the only sound between them, and for once, Agatha didn’t mind the silence. It was a relief after the chaos of their shift. After the fight. After the fucking car accident.

She had spent the entire night trying not to think about Rio. 

But now, in the quiet of the car, with the city stretched out around them, it was harder to ignore.

She could feel Rio’s presence even now, warm in the seat beside her. Could sense the way she exhaled, deep and slow, like she was finally letting the weight of the night settle over her.

Agatha didn’t know why she had offered to drive her. It was stupid. Irrational. 

She just wanted to drop Rio off and go home.

By the time Agatha pulled up to Rio’s building, the other woman straightened, rubbing her eyes before unbuckling her seatbelt.

It was a nice place. Too nice.

Tall glass windows, sleek modern architecture, expensive. Exclusive. The kind of place where the doormen probably recognized every resident by name, where the lobby smelled like citrus and money.

It suited Rio.

Which, for some reason, annoyed the hell out of Agatha.

She had no reason to care. None. But there was something about the effortless way Rio fit here, like she belonged in places most people could only look at from the outside, that set her teeth on edge.

Not your problem, Harkness. Drop her off. Go home.

Rio opened the door, stepping out, the faint creak of leather breaking the silence. A beat passed before she leaned down, one arm resting against the car as she met Agatha’s gaze through the open window.

The streetlights cast a soft glow on her face, turning her eyes darker, sharper.

“Drive safe, doctora.”

Her voice was quieter now, almost lazy, and Agatha hated the way the word settled under her skin, warm and unwanted.

And then, just like that, she was gone.

Agatha didn’t watch her walk inside. She didn’t.

She just exhaled, fingers flexing against the wheel before putting the car in drive.

She needed sleep. Badly.

She drove home on autopilot, her brain fogged with exhaustion, her body heavy from the weight of the shift. Every bone in her body ached, her muscles screaming for rest.

By the time she pulled into her driveway, she barely had the energy to move.

She shut off the engine, grabbed her keys, and pushed open the door, the cold air hitting her like a slap.

Halfway to her front door, she saw it.

Something small, something dark, lying on the floor of the passenger seat.

Rio’s phone.

Agatha stopped short, staring at it.

For a long time.

She should leave it.

She could drop it off tomorrow. Rio probably wouldn’t even notice it was missing until she woke up. It wasn’t her problem.

It wasn’t.

And yet.

Her fingers twitched.

She ran a hand through her hair, exhaling sharply.

Just leave it. Just go inside. Go to sleep. This is not your problem.

But—

Damn it.

Before she could talk herself out of it, she turned right the hell back around.

------------------

By the time she reached Rio’s place again, it was 11.

The lobby was quiet, the kind of quiet that only happened at this hour on a sunday, where even the air felt heavy.. The overhead lighting was dimmed, the usual background hum of city life muffled into something softer, more distant. Even the scent of the place, clean linen, polished floors, money, felt subdued.

Agatha exhaled sharply, running a hand through her hair as she approached the reception desk. Her patience was already paper-thin.

The receptionist, a guy who looked like he was in his late twenties, dark curls slightly disheveled, posture slouched with the kind of exhaustion that came from pulling too many late shifts, barely glanced up from his computer screen.

“Help you?” he mumbled, clearly uninterested.

Agatha tapped her fingers against the counter. “I need to find an apartment.”

That got his attention. He straightened slightly, eyeing her with mild suspicion. “Uh… residents only.”

She forced a tight smile. “Yeah, I figured. I just dropped Rio Vidal off earlier. She left her phone in my car.”

At the mention of Rio’s name, the guy’s entire demeanor shifted. His brows lifted slightly, lips parting as if he wasn’t quite sure how to process that information.

“Rio?”

Agatha narrowed her eyes. “Yes. Rio. Vidal.”

“Are you on the list?”

Agatha exhaled through her nose, already regretting every decision that had led her to this moment.

“No,” she said, voice flat. “But she just got home. I’m not some fucking stranger, and I don’t particularly feel like making a second trip here tomorrow, so—” she placed the phone onto the counter with a click, fingers drumming once against the surface. “Either call her, or tell me where she lives so I can knock on her damn door.”

The guy blinked.

Then, after a moment of consideration, he let out a slow breath and muttered, “Jesus,” under his breath before reaching for the desk phone. “What's your name?”

“Agatha Harkness”

Agatha tapped her foot impatiently as he dialed.

A few seconds passed.

“Morning ms vidal. I've got Agatha harkness here”

“She’s here?”

Rio’s voice, muffled but unmistakable.

Agatha tried not to react to the way something in her chest tightened at the sound of it.

A pause.

“…Send her up.”

The receptionist lowered the phone, still looking vaguely concerned about the whole thing, like he wasn’t entirely sure whether he should be letting her go up or calling security.

“She’s in 14C,” he said eventually.

Agatha didn’t bother responding.

She was already on her way.

 

She wasn’t sure what she expected when the door finally swung open.

Rio half asleep, maybe. Hair messy, wrapped in a hoodie, muttering something half-coherent as she snatched the phone from her hands. That would’ve made sense. That would’ve been easy.

What she got was something else entirely.

Rio stood there, leaning against the doorway, freshly showered.

Dark hair still damp, curling slightly at the ends, droplets of water trailing down the slope of her neck. Her skin was bare, free of any makeup, the soft glow of the hallway lights casting golden shadows across the high angles of her cheekbones, the sharp curve of her jaw.

And—

Oh.

Oh, fuck.

She was wearing a sports bra, a bright pink one. And shorts. Tiny, black, sinful shorts.

Agatha’s brain stuttered.

Because of course Rio had abs. Of course she did.

Defined, lean muscle stretched over golden skin, every sharp angle and smooth curve honed to near perfection. She looked like she was carved from something ancient and dangerous, like she belonged on the cover of a magazine or standing under the glow of a spotlight, not just existing in some dimly lit apartment hallway at three in the morning.

Agatha felt her mouth go dry.

Rio, for her part, just looked at her. Then, very slowly, arched a brow.

“Something wrong?”

Agatha tore her gaze away, clearing her throat. “No.”

Rio didn’t look convinced.

Her lips twitched, just slightly, just enough to hint at the ghost of a smirk, and she crossed her arms over her chest, which did absolutely nothing to help Agatha’s situation.

“Did you drive all the way back here just to stare at me?”

I hate you.

“No,” Agatha said flatly, forcing herself to move, to focus, to not let her gaze drop lower. She held up the phone. “You left this in my car.”

Rio’s gaze flicked to the device in her hand. Then, after a beat, she sighed. “Of course I did.”

She reached out, fingers brushing against Agatha’s as she took the phone.

It was brief. Barely anything.

And yet—

Agatha ignored the way her stomach clenched, the heat that curled low in her spine.

Rio tapped the screen, checking something, before slipping the phone onto a nearby table. Then she looked back at Agatha.

“Thank you. You didn't have to”

A pause.

“You wanna come in?”

Agatha blinked.

She should say no.

She should say no.

She should turn around, walk back to the elevator, and leave.

But she didn’t.

“…Yeah,” she said. “Yeah, okay.”

And just like that, she stepped inside, and the first thing she noticed was that it didn’t smell like she expected.

She wasn’t sure what she had expected, something sharp, maybe, like the expensive perfume Rio always seemed to wear. Or something impersonal, sterile, like those luxury apartments that looked like a furniture catalog and nothing else.

But instead, the air was warm. Lived-in. A mix of fresh coffee, paint, and the faintest trace of something floral, jasmine, maybe?, lingering in a way that felt almost personal.

And the apartment itself…

Agatha hadn’t even realized she’d stopped moving until Rio let out a quiet, amused sound.

“Something wrong?”

Agatha ignored her, taking it all in.

The space was open and spacious but not cold. Unlike what she’d imagined, sleek, empty, detached, Rio’s home felt like a home.

There were bookshelves, actual bookshelves, filled with books that looked worn and well read. Some had spines that were cracked, others had dog eared pages sticking out at odd angles. There were art books stacked haphazardly next to crime novels, medical textbooks wedged between poetry collections.

But what caught Agatha’s attention were the plants.

Everywhere.

By the windows, on shelves, even hanging from the ceiling in delicate macrame holders. Different sizes, different shapes. Some leafy and wild, stretching toward the light, some small and delicate, thriving in ceramic pots.

“Didn’t peg you for a plant person,” Agatha muttered, stepping further inside.

Rio smirked, shutting the door behind them. “They’re hard to kill. Seemed like a safe investment.”

Agatha hummed, but her gaze was already moving, taking in the rest.

A piano stood against the far wall, sleek and black, looking well-loved but not dusty. A guitar rested beside it, propped against a chair. And in the corner, half-hidden by the couch, were painting supplies, canvases, brushes, tubes of acrylics. Some of the canvases were turned away, unfinished. Others had paint smudges on the edges, as if Rio had touched them with bare fingers.

Agatha felt something tight coil in her chest.

This wasn’t the apartment of someone who just existed.

This was the apartment of someone who felt.

She hadn’t expected that.

Rio was watching her again, arms still crossed, but there was something softer in her expression now.

“You look surprised.”

Agatha glanced at her, then back at the piano. “Didn’t think you’d have time for all this.”

Rio shrugged, like it was nothing. “I don’t. Not really. But…” she gestured vaguely to the instruments, the paints. “Some things make time for themselves.”

Agatha didn’t know what to do with that.

So instead, she said nothing.

For a moment, the silence stretched. Not uncomfortable, exactly. Just… full.

Then Rio shifted, stretching her arms over her head, the movement making her abs flex in a way Agatha absolutely did not need to notice.

“I was about to hit the gym,” Rio said, voice casual.

Agatha blinked. “At this hour?”

“I like morning workouts.” Rio smirked. “Keeps me from killing anyone before noon.”

Agatha snorted, but Rio just tilted her head, considering.

“…Or,” she mused, “we could get brunch instead.”

Agatha hesitated.

She should go home. She should shower, sleep, reset.

But…

The apartment was warm. Rio was looking at her like she already knew Agatha was considering it. Wanda was dropping Nicky off at six. She still had some time.

Agatha sighed, scrubbing a hand down her face. “…Fine,” she muttered. “But if you take me somewhere with overpriced avocado toast, I swear to God—”

Rio grinned, already moving toward the kitchen. “Relax, Harkness. I’ll cook.”

Agatha’s brows lifted. “You cook?”

Rio cast a smirk over her shoulder. “What, you think I survive on protein shakes and spite?”

Agatha did think that, actually.

Rio rolled her eyes, grabbing a pan from the rack. “Sit down. You might even enjoy yourself.”

She had no idea why she was still here.

But she wasn’t leaving.

Agatha exhaled, running a hand through her hair before finally dropping onto the couch. 

It was green. A deep, rich shade, the kind that looked soft before you even touched it. And when Agatha did sit, she had to admit, it was soft. The kind of soft that pulled at you, coaxing your body to relax even when your mind refused to.

She sighed, sinking into it, stretching her legs out slightly. She hadn’t realized how tired she was until now, until she let herself stop moving.

From the kitchen, Rio moved with the kind of easy familiarity Agatha could never quite manage in her own home. She reached for things without looking, opening cabinets, pulling out ingredients, setting the pan on the stove with practiced motions. Like she’d done this a thousand times before. Like this wasn’t something she had to think about.

Agatha didn’t cook much. She was never home much. Her house was a place to sleep, to shower, to store her things. A space where she existed, nothing more.

But this, this was something else.

This was a home.

She let her head fall back against the couch, exhaling.

"You want coffee?" Rio called over her shoulder.

Agatha let out a quiet huff. "I always want coffee."

Rio smirked, grabbing another mug.

The silence between them wasn’t uncomfortable. It was… different. Lighter than it had been last night.

Still, Agatha could feel the weight of it.

The unspoken thing.

She exhaled, dragging a hand through her hair before speaking.

"About last night."

Rio glanced at her, one brow raised. "What about it?"

Agatha shifted, tapping her fingers against her knee. "I was an asshole."

Rio let out a low hum. "Well, yeah."

Agatha shot her a look. "I meant—" She sighed, leaning forward, resting her elbows on her knees. "I was stressed. The shift was a fucking disaster, and I took it out on you."

Rio didn’t say anything.

Agatha swallowed. "I shouldn’t have done that."

A pause.

Then, very softly "No," Rio murmured. "You shouldn’t have."

The words weren’t sharp, but they weren’t gentle either. They just were. And that, somehow, was worse.

Agatha exhaled, shifting slightly in her seat. “So. Truce?”

Rio studied her for a long moment, head tilting slightly.

Then, slowly, she smiled.

“Truce.”

Something in Agatha’s chest loosened.

The space between them was too small.

Not enough to be dangerous. Not enough to be obvious.

Just enough to feel.

Agatha could see the way Rio’s skin was still damp from her shower, the way her hair curled slightly at the ends, dripping onto her shoulders. The way she smelled, something clean, sharp, undeniably her.

She swallowed, forcing her gaze upward, locking onto Rio’s eyes instead.

Big mistake.

Because Rio was watching her.

Not teasing. Not smirking.

Just watching.

Like she was waiting for something.

Like she could see straight through Agatha’s skin, straight through the walls she kept so carefully in place.

It made her nervous.

And Agatha Harkness didn’t get nervous.

So she did the only thing she could do. She talked.

“You really stopped.” Her voice came out quieter than she intended, rough at the edges.

Rio didn’t move. “Yeah.”

Agatha wet her lips, her fingers digging into the couch. “Last night. You said you thought I wasn’t interested.”

Rio exhaled through her nose, tilting her head slightly. “Didn’t seem like you were.”

Agatha hesitated, the words tangling in her throat. “I just—”

She clenched her jaw, looking away, staring at the piano in the corner like it could give her the right answer.

“I didn’t mean for it to feel like that,” she muttered finally.

Rio’s voice was even. “What did you mean for it to feel like?”

Agatha exhaled sharply, rubbing a hand over her face. “I don’t know.”

It wasn’t a lie.

She didn’t know.

She didn’t know why she had wanted Rio to push, even as she pulled away. Didn’t know why the distance had felt like relief and disappointment all at once. Didn’t know why, when Rio had finally listened and stopped, it had made something in her chest ache.

Rio watched her, silent for a long moment. Then—

“You really are a pain in the ass.”

Agatha let out a startled laugh.

It wasn’t mocking. It wasn’t cruel.

It was… fond. Too fond.

Agatha shifted, the warmth of it making her restless. “Yeah, well. You’re not exactly a picnic either.”

Rio smirked. “You say that, but here you are. Sitting on my couch. Eating my food.”

“I haven’t eaten anything yet.”

“Yet.”

The weight in the air didn’t ease.

If anything, it pressed closer.
